O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, my very dear sons, I have completed this book which is the last part of the science of medicine together with its fulfillment, and I have made the end through its expositions and by its declarations. 
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is a part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery". 
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is neglected in our region and is foreign throughout, the science is lost and scattered, and nothing remains of its strength except for the small descriptions in the books of the ancients that hands have moved.  
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed off and knowledge is removed. 
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Now it seems to me that I should revive it together with the ordering of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together with the forms of the cautery instruments, and the other instruments of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them, as it is necessary.  
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because there are no good surgeons to be found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected. 
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is fitting for one who undertakes it to delve into the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the arrangement of the limbs, and their shapes, and their connections and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and veins and the number of sinews, and the movements of the veins moving and resting, and the location from which they arise.  
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason Hippocrates says that knowledge without practice is much, and with practice it is little; and the same in surgery. 
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above, beware lest he fall into error and harm men; just as I have seen many times more than those who undertake this science and abandon themselves to it without knowledge and experience. 
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish man who cut the abscess of scrofula from a woman's neck and cut the arteries in her neck; because so much blood came out that the woman fell dead at his hands. 
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another man who treated a stone in a man's bladder, and the stone was large; he took out with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days. 
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and I knew well that if he was cut he would die. 
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another man who took in hand the cure of the duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the break he had a wound; and the ignorant man pulled out the break on top of the wound as if it were by strong force, and did not leave the wound any dressing, and left it like that to the end; and he commanded him not to unwrap it; and he delayed until the leg was all swollen and the foot came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come untie the leg; and when I dislocated it, he was so happy and felt no pain. 
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all the corruption was already confirmed or member, and I could not heal it; and the corruption did not cease to go through the limb until the limb was completely lost. 
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another man who burst the inflamed abscess, and then it inflamed further through the malice of his lord.  
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancre, when it is pure of melancholic humor, it is not fitting that one touch it with iron unless it is in part healed so that one can remove all that is corrupted. 
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, you need to know that manual work is divided into two divisions: namely, work where there is danger in several situations; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger. 
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For which it is necessary that you guard yourself so that the foolish man cannot speak badly of you. 
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in some of his admonishments: “Do not undertake a bad illness unless you are called a fool for doing so. 
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to III chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is of fire cauteries and of medicinal cauteries with hot water, and the chapter is ordered from the head to the feet; and of the shapes of instruments, and of the fastenings of the cautery, and of all that is necessary in the work. 
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is of cutting and piercing, and of cupping glasses and wounds, and of extracting arrows, and similar things; and the chapter is ordered and the shapes of instruments are described.  
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is of restoring dislocations and sprains, and similar things; and it is ordered from the head to the feet, and the shapes of instruments are described. 
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	So as we remember the work, it is fitting that I say the quality of aid and harm of each complexion. 
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and harm are the longest speech and most subtle science and secret answers; and many sages spoke of these, agreeing on them; and I am content with few words, for I fear length. 
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the cautery aids universally to all complexions where there is matter, except for two complexions: that is to know, hot complexion without matter and dry complexion without matter. 
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexions together with matter, some said that the cautery is of great help, while others said the opposite: that the cautery is only good for illness that comes from heat and dryness. 
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot and should not be cured with heat nor dryness. Those who say otherwise argue that the cautery is of great help for hot and dry illnesses that come upon men's bodies. 
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of a man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold. 
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement. 
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it several times through experience. 
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in every way, let no one interfere except those who have experienced it, and who know through long practice the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and their outcomes and the space of time; for other complexions we have no fear, even cold and moist diseases. 
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all those who looked at it agreed with the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cautery combined with fire is one of the secrets of cures, and has a greater benefit than cautery with burning medicines. 
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not come except to the limb that is cooked, and does not harm another limb no matter its name. 
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Burning medicines come from one limb to another by moving away and bring illness to the limb that was healing; and perhaps they kill the patient. Fire because of its height and the goodness of its substance does not do this if there is no excess. 
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found by experience and by the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it is based on the truth of things; and for this reason I excuse the length of my speech, for it does not please me to withhold from you the secret which resides in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives away illnesses from bodies, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; now receive it in your thoughts.  
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on what time the cauteries should be made, and they came out praying. 
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cautery is suitable at all times, because the harms arising are put beneath by the help of the cautery; and especially if the cauteries are for necessary pains, urgent and hasty that cannot wait for a time when greater evil may come to the limb. 
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think like foolish folk, dear son, for the disease that is healed by cautery has no return; and they say so; but it is not as they think, because cauteries are only a medicine which moves the complexion, and dries the humors which are the cause of pain, and is worth more than medicine for its swiftness in its effect, and for the virtue of its work and its mastery. 
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the disease comes sometimes according to the complexion of the patient and the place of the disease and its virtue; and superfluities are gathered in him by the acquisition of foods and similar things, if this is not done, cauteries administered in the place where there is a surplus of superfluity and moisture, such as cauteries for pain because of density, and similar things, and some pain does not return at all; but this happens rarely. 
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the last resort of medicine; but this is true. But they do not believe that cauteries are valuable after medicine, but their intentions are false; and cauteries are the last resort of medicine because when we administer remedies for any disease and they are ineffective, then we administer the cautery, and it is effective. 
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then understand well that cauteries are the last resort of medicine, not according to the intentions of foolish minds. 
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cautery instruments of gold are better than those of iron, and they said this because of the quality of gold and the subtlety of its substance; and they said that the burns from a cautery do not cause putrefaction, but this is not true, for I have tried it and found that it is true in some men; and cauteries of gold are worth more than those of iron, as they said. 
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And however when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it cools quickly; and if you heat it too much, it will melt in the fire; and thus there are enough obstacles. 
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use cauteries of iron which we have found more suitable for our work.  
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I have ordered this chapter from the top to the bottom so that the way may be easier to find. 
dou cautere olivaire	with olive oil cautery 
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and cold on the brain, and there are two reasons why it is done because of a disease called “soda”, and because of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and to the ears, and because of a multitude of dreams and toothache and sore throat, and also all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar illnesses. 
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by a dissolving medicine modifying the head for III nights or IV, according to what the strength and age and custom of the patient can suffer; and then make the back of the patient's head rise. 
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and have him put his hands on your knees; afterward place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and where your two middle fingers come, if it bleeds then heat the cautery which is called "olive," of which this is the form: 
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the spot marked with ink, and descend and tighten your hand bit by bit turning; then lift your hand slowly, and observe the spot to see if you see the bone a little; and if you do not see it, begin the cautery again until you see the bone as I told you; afterward take a bit of silk thread, and put in soft cotton within, and place on the spot and leave it for three days; afterward place moistened cotton in butter; and leave it on until the burn is removed; afterward treat the wound with an ointment called "tetrafarmacon", until it is healed. 
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that when a wound remains open longer, the more it purges; and for this reason it is helped to close. 
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of them said that one must leave the cautery long enough so that part of the bone is burned, and then remove what has been burned from the bone, and it should be healed. 
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And say the others that one must leave the cautery on for a long time, and press so hard that it lowers the bone as wide as a spindle that women put in their spindles so that the humors issue forth moved outwards; and one must leave the wound open for a long time; afterwards one must clean and solder it. 
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of cauteries do not seem to me to be good at all, except in some men where there is a way for fear; and it seems to me that I should leave it; for the head is weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we testify in other members; and even when the head of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of the cautery is safer and gentler for me, and from this one I work in assembly health. 
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain of the head 
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain and long-lasting pain affects the entire head, the patient should use herbs and pills called "cochie", and purging of the head, and oils and plasters; and if you apply the cautery that we have previously mentioned, it will not be effective. 
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the head of the patient is strong and not too cold; then cauterize below the cautery a point as we have said above.  
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After making the cautery on each horn of the head down to the bone, as we have previously said, and make the cautery where it is called "vassels"; and these are the places where one applies cupping glasses; and lighten your hand so that you do not see the bone: the patient feels much more pain with this cautery than with others, and I will speak of this later; and it is necessary for the cauteries on the horns to be subtler than those with which one cauterizes the middle of the head, and this is the form: 
dou cautere dou chief	with cautery of the head 
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain comes to a part of the head, and the illness is extended to the eye, and the head is purged by purifying medicines, and other cures have been done as I said in the division of diseases, and all this does not help: then you make cauteries according to two methods, that is to say of burning medicine and fire. 
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauteries of burning medicine are such that you take a dock of alum, and remove the bark and cut a piece as thick as two fingers, and then place it on the temple where the pain resides in such a way that you can replace the dock of alum under the skin; and when it is replaced, bind it well and leave it like this for twelve hours; and then unbind it and apply crushed garlic over it, and leave the wound like this for two or three days; then put cotton soaked in butter on it as long as it will last. 
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment with ointment until it is healed; and if you see that this can be done by some burning medicines which I have written or else treat with burning medicines. 
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this manner. 
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery which has this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a bell or it has a slight curve, and in the middle there is a small projection; and you put it on the painful spot, and hold your hand steady and twist the iron slightly, until half the thickness of the flesh is burned; and lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is underneath, and flows abundantly with blood. 
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Afterward, put cotton soaked in saltpeter and place it on the spot for three days; then apply cotton moistened with butter, and then treat the spot with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this migraine with the cautery which is called "cultellare," at the very tip, be careful not to sever the artery in this migraine which is not old.  
de emigraine	of migraine 
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraine as we have previously said in the division of diseases and it does not profit, and you see that the cauteries previously mentioned from medicine and iron do not suffice, then it is necessary that you shave the cautery which is called "cultellare" until it is white; and thus draw a line on the painful area half a fingernail long, and remove your hand once, and strain so that you do not cut the artery and do not reach the bone; and beware of the mandible which moves when one chews, and do not care for the nerves except for the movement and that spasm does not come to the patient, and beware of the flowing of blood from the artery when it is cut, because cutting has great fear and also for him who does not know it, and who is not a student and experienced; and leave the work in the middle way; but I will tell you how to restrain blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you at what place it is treated in this book. 
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery is not sufficient for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him on the temple as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you see fit, administer the cautery that we have said in the chapter of the extraction of the artery, with the cautery which has two knives; and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful. 
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	for the pain of the ears due to cold  
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes to the ear from cold, and one has used dissolving medicines and other cures as we have said in the division, and the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery which is called "poin", of which here is the form: 
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After pointing all around the pained ear, or around the two places where the pain is located on both sides, and you remove a piece from its root after you have marked the place for placement; and make 10 points around each ear; afterwards treat the place until it is healed.  
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth 
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture which must be cured by cautery is none other than those that arise from phlegm, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not make a cautery for those that come from dryness and spasm of nerves. 
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this kind of torture which arises from phlegm by means of hydrates and purges of the head and gargles, and this is useless, then it is fitting that you cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and the other a burn near the temple, and the third in the joint of the two lips; and apply the cautery to the part which appears sound, and make a cautery on the head of the ear above a burn below the horn of the head, and another on the temple as long as a thumb; and leave the cautery on so long that half of the core is burned; and this is the form of the cautery: 
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is similar to the knife we have mentioned before, but it is a bit more delicate and the knife should be a bit larger; after cleaning the place as I have said before, until it is healed. 
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and it does not help, and the patient does not have a fever, then you make four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one on the place that is called "vassels" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and they should be treated as we have said before. 
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness it is fitting to give the patient large herbs and purifying pills for the brain; after raise the head of the patient entirely, and put mustard plaster on the back of the head as it is written in the treatise of plasters; and this is the manner of the cautery: if you do as I have said. 
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healed thus, it is good; and if it is not, make three cauteries on the head descending to the neck, with a space of two fingers between each cautery; and treat it as the others, and if you see swelling, and the patient suffers, make one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, two others on the two horns, and treat it until it is healed; and let the cauteries be called "olivary", as I have said before. 
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be cleansed of herbs and of what we have said before; then raise the head of the patient, and make a cautery on the head and on each horn, one behind and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient suffers, and the disease is severe, make four cauteries on the spine of the back; and leave it until the innermost part is burned, and lift your hand; then treat it until it is healed, and let the cauteries be called "olivary" as we have said before. 
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy 
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use cautery except those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary first to modify the brain with herbs and other remedies that we have mentioned in the section when the patient is large and suffering from little medicine. 
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot endure it, make them gargle and chew remedies that modify the brain often with good meats; afterward, shave their head in the middle, and cauterize according to what we have said before, and cauterize on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the patient is strong and suffering, cauterize as I have said to one who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive according to the manner that I have said.  
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is feverish, he shall make a delicate cautery according to this manner: 
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When by the cause of melancholy are the superfluities or corrupted moistures and thick phlegm, then the cautery of several cauteries as we have said to him who has paralysis. 
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if by the cause of melancholy are the superfluities declining to melancholy, and is the body of the patient moist, then let him drink things by which the brain may be purified, according to what is before in the division. 
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After raise the head of the patient; after make a well-made linen tourniquet, as a circle, and put it on the head; and let the patient be crossed, and be well held on all sides; then present the liniment, and melt some old butterbur butter; and heat it over temperate fire, so that the patient can endure the heat; after empty the circle inside onto the head, and let it cool down; and do this to the patient once a week with another good government until he is healed. 
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you see that the cautery burns too much, make many small points with the whole cautery. 
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This manner of cautery removes the brain properly; and then put cotton softened in butter and gelatine fat. 
de l’awe des eulz	from the awes of the eyes 
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When awe first comes to the eyes by the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and give the patient something purifying the head, and protect it from all moisture, and make him sweat or bathe several times on an empty stomach. 
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After you command him to bend his head back, and make a cautery around his head, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the descent of the awe is in both eyes together, or one if the descent is in one; and apply the whole cautery to all the veins and arteries that are below the heart, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; and beware of the flow of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, staunch it as best as you can. 
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in incision the caution how you shall stretch it; and never make a cautery or burn below the two bones behind. 
dou cors des larmes	Where the body sheds tears 
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins or near the arteries that are in appearance on the head outside; and one sees that they are superfluities, cold and phlegmatic, then make the cautery that I said at the beginning of this work descending towards the eyes: I cauterize above the head, and II cauteries on the II temples, and II cauteries or burns below the II bones; and if there is need for more, then cauterize abundantly above the eyebrow with all small cauteries. 
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Where the body sheds tears within the eyes 
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat it according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit, then give the patient III nights of henbane broth; afterwards burn the head with a cautery or half a cautery of olive oil; and make II cauteries of the cautery called “clavilis” on the II shoulders, one point below the ears; and beware of the artery so that you do not cut it. 
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery which is called “clavilis”: 
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the skin of the oil is softened by illness and moisture, then use this cautery which is called “olive”. 
de coi ci est li forme:	Of which this is the shape:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see fit to make II cauteries on the II shoulders as long as the eyebrows are; and do not remove your hand until one-third of the skin is burned, according to the way that I have said. 
dou poil qui point l’oil	where a hair pricks the eye 
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyes are converted to parchment, and prick the eye, and one does cauteries according to two manners: that is to say, of fire, or of burning medicine. 
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow. 
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and are even, then put the patient in your hand; afterwards draw on a piece of paper a shape that is like the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs; then put cotton moistened with egg white and persillone juice on the eye, then heat the cautery which has this form:  
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the face, point by point many times, so that the flesh is burned at each spot; and the signs of the health of the work are that you see the paper withdraw, and the hairs rise at the point of a needle; then lift your hand and leave it for three days. Then put cotton softened in butter until the burn is removed; afterwards cure with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the hairs come back and the paper is softened, then begin the cautery on that same place as you did first; and if the hairs are gone, cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural position, and is even, and does not prick the hairs at the eye. 
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cautery of medicinal burning is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make from parchment the shape of a myrtle leaf; then take French soap and quicklime, of each a dram, and grind together well; and make it haste so that it does not cool down, then spread it quickly on the form that you have made like a myrtle leaf, and place on the paper the eyes; and if the illness holds in one eye only, one should work on one, and if on both, also; and put under the eye cotton softened in egg white; and the head of the patient should be in your hand and put your finger showing on the medicine, and press one spot and then another every time the patient feels a bite from the medicine, for he will feel a bite as from fire.  
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your hand. 
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the bite has passed, lift the place of awe, and see if you see the paper raised as it was raised by constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is so, it is well. 
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, apply more medicine to the place where the medicine has not worked, until your works are equal, and your eyes are set; then put soft cotton soaked in butter on it until the burning is gone, afterwards treat the place of the ointment which is called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed. 
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to be careful with your work so that the medicine does not fall into your eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hair pricks in the eye, start the medicine again on that place which is softened by the paper properly, just as you did before; afterwards treat it until it is healed; and this is the form of the myrtle leaf: 
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this be your constraints; and let not the right way be responded to him whose study is this art. 
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the cure of fistula by cautery 
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your cures do not profit at all, then it is necessary that you make a cautery for it according to this manner. 
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Command the patient to place his head in your lap; and let his attendants hold his head between your hands in such a way that it does not move nor shake its head; afterwards, put moistened cotton in egg white or parsley juice on the eye; afterwards, heat the cautery which is shaped: and is fitted to the head as the shape of a sparrow's feather, together with the cautery; if you see, it is pointed from one side to the other, and if you see, it is also like a tent; but nevertheless, that which is fitted is better for your work. 
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula if it is open, and treat the rot, and dry it; and if it is closed, do the work, and treat through the bowel; afterwards put a hot cautery on it, and hold your hand at the cautery on the part where there is no flesh above the eye, so that your hands do not make a fool of themselves; and put the cautery in the fat of the oil, and corrupt it. 
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, it would be good. 
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, start the cautery again once more, and another if you need it, and leave it for three days; afterwards put softened cotton in butter on it, and cure it with a desiccant ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass and it is not healed, put corrosive medicine on it until the bone is uncovered; and the king according to what he would come in his chapter. 
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cautery for fistula that none of the ancients said. 
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand a fistula and make the place; afterwards put in the fissure a subtle cautery of which this is the form: 
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and make it the size of one-third of an inch; and hold your hand or the cautery firmly, and do not let the patient move at all so that the melted lead does not run to his eye; and it is necessary that you put on the patient's eye moistened cotton soaked in wine or in water: the lead will burn the place of the fistula, and heal wonderfully.  
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, it is good. 
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, it is necessary to administer a purge at the nape of the neck, and return the fistula to the body from the nape according to what is proper in its own place.  
des crevaices en levres	of fissures in lips 
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times fissures occur in the lips which are called "hairs," and similarly in the lips of children. 
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these fissures as we have said in sections, and the treatment does not work, then heat a small surgical cautery knife according to this form:  
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And quickly place it in those fissures until it reaches a boil; afterward treat the area with wax until it is healed. 
de l’aposteme de la goule	of an abscess of the throat  
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the uvula, or palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it has become rotten and swollen and aged and becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in sections, and it does not profit: then it is necessary that you have a cautery according to the quantity of the fistula; afterward burn or pierce the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron becomes red hot and reaches the bottom, and wherever the last place is; and do this once or twice, after the treatment as we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, it is good; and if not, it is necessary to uncover the area and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.  
dou movement des dens	of teeth movement 
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines and that is not worth it, then put the head of the patient in your lap; afterwards heat the cautery so that its form will come here later in part so that you put a cane on the tooth; and put the hot cautery inside quickly, and hold as long as your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; afterwards lift your hand and start the cautery again according to your will; afterwards fill the patient's mouth with salt water, and keep it for an hour and then wash it out. 
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the moving tooth is fixed, and the softened gum is restrained, and the corrupt moisture is dried up. 
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of teeth 
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from cold, where there is coldness or wind, and remedies of medicine are ineffective, then it is necessary to use a cautery according to two methods: butter cautery and fire cautery. 
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Butter cautery is such that you take butter from a cow and put the end in a spoon of iron or silver; then take cotton and wrap it around the point of a tent peg, and moisten it in boiled butter, and place it on the aching tooth quickly and hold it until it cools down; and thus do often so that its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see that moistened wool and cotton in cold butter is placed on the aching tooth, and hot iron is put on top so that the fire comes to the chewing surface of the tooth. 
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Fire cautery is such that you take a piece of iron or silver, and it should be thick so the fire does not come to the patient's mouth; then heat the cautery, so its shape will come later, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down. Do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next. 
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is fitting that the patient fill his mouth with good butter in the haste of this cautery, and then make it cool; and this is the form of the cautery: 
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery of whatever metal you wish, and according to what you have power; and this is the form of the cauterizing iron: 
des scrophules	of scrofula 
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofula are of phlegm and cold humors, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery as follows, and it has two openings for the smoke to escape from the other side of the cautery; and put the hot cautery on the abscess once, or twice if necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, put the cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it like that for three days; and put softened cotton with butter on it until the burn is gone; then treat the area with washes and dressings until it is healed. 
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cane: 
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture overcomes the channels of the body, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be purged first with dissolving medicines; afterwards, apply a cautery to the root of the throat, and be careful not to come near the throat itself, and not burn the heart, but only make a small mark. 
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterward, apply another cautery at the joint of the neck to the head of the spine, and let the cauteries be called "clavile," as we have shown the form before; and treat the place as we have previously said until it is healed. 
de la toust	of the cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and illnesses of the body are from cold moisture, and the patient has neither fever nor dryness, and the illness is old, then make two cauteries on the shoulder blades in their hollows; and another cautery between the breasts under the two nipples; let the cauteries be called "clavile" according to the form that is previously mentioned.  
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see it, make a cautery by pricking with the whole cautery which is called "points", whose form is as described before in the illness of the ears; and let the points be up to XXX, or as many around. 
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After cauterizing the place according to what is said before, let the cauteries be at III inches according to this form: 
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because the cauteries are lighter, for that reason you make III in a row.  
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder 
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first loosen the dislocation. 
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, place the patient on his back and on his side; afterwards, lift the heart which is inside the armpit with two fingers of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inward, heat the cautery which has II points, which form is this:  
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the heart as long as it pierces to the ribs, and the figure of the cautery together with four cauteries; and for this reason, a cautery is made with the cautery which has three nerves, so that the figure of the cauterization is six cauteries; and are the nerves according to the subtlety of a tent and this is the form of the cautery which has three nerves: 
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never is added on this one nerve so that there are eight cauteries. 
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After put on the cautery a poultice crushed with thread; after let the patient rest, and do not move the limbs for a long time until it is well comforted. 
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated from above, which thing happens rarely, then make a cautery on the thickness of the cautery clavicle, or many cauteries by pricking.  
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed. 
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When cold and much moisture come to the stomach until they draw it from its complexion, and phlegm is multiplied in him, and customary treatments do not help him, then the patient must be turned on his back, and extend his legs and hands.  
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Then make three cauteries below the spoon of his foot the size of a shilling, applying each cautery with a point. Make two more cauteries on either side of the ribs so that the shape of the cauteries is triangular, and have an equal space between them so they are not joined together when they rot; let the cauteries be so deep that they stain both parts of the heart, and let the shape of the cauteries be like this with no adjustments: 
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form; and he who will have fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and marking on the stomach in one point according to the quantity that you see of inch; then cauterize with the whole cautery which is called "points". 
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the cure that we have had before, as long as it is healed. 
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver comes pain from cold and moisture and great windiness, as long as it is out of its natural complexion because of superfluities; and the patient is treated with what we have said in divisions, and it does not profit him, then it is necessary that the patient be cauterized on his upper part; and make three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, below the hypochondria, where the ribs of the stomach come; and have space between each cautery the thickness of a finger; and let the cauteries be as long as the body, and do not press your hand too hard on the whole cautery; and let it burn only half of the heart, and let the patient be straight on his feet; and if he cannot, let him lie down, and extend his legs, and lift his arms; and this is the form: 
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if your intention is to cauterize these wounds with a knife, be skillful and wise in the art and beware that you do not burn all of the heart, for you would dry up all of the body; and that it does not reach the eye, for the heart is very delicate in that place, and you will know by sight. 
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh or the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain but not too strong; and if it is in the membrane, he feels very severe pain. 
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then when this cure requires the mires, it is fitting that the patient be laid on his back; and then mark the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a ray, of which here is the form: 
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize I cauterize until the flesh is burned, and comes to a boil, until the pustule is all dry; after the cure according to the cure of wounds until it is healed; and it does not befit that any use this cautery except those who have long studied in the art of medicine, by whose hands these diseases have run no times.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can boldly work, and nevertheless it seems to me that it is better to leave it. 
dou cautere de pleuresin	For a cautery of pleurisy 
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one must make for pleurisy cauteries of aristolochia roots, and in this manner: take an aristolochia root long, the largest that you can find, and let it be dry, and also as thick and as long as your thumb; and moisten it in oil, and put it to the fire, and cauterize I cauterize between the shoulder blade and the neck, and two small cauteries one below in descending in the part that is below the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining behind one below; and one cauterize on the breast, and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two as the two ribs of the breast behind the cautery that is between the two shoulders; and do not press your hand, but rather make it open as if smelling.  
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And some ancients say that a man should use a fire cautery resembling a razor, heat it and place it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess; and the pain will flee, as we have said about the abscess of the liver. 
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed. 
de la mice	of the mice
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the disease of the mice as we have said in the divisions of cures and it does not profit, then apply three methods of cautery all of which are good.
