Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which the first way is that you make three or four cauteries, aligned according to the length of the mice, according to the shape of the liver cautery that we have said before; and do not press your hand on the whole cautery, and let the patient often turn onto his back; and another way of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has two points, as we have shown it in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the heart which is located at the mice, or where the ribs of the patient come towards the left side, and let the elevations which you lift the heart according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and the cauteries be according to the width of the body.  
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After he puts the two inflamed nerves in so that the heart is pierced on the other side, and then draws the cautery out, and thus he will have four. 
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has festered for a long time, this is worth more than the other cures mentioned before. 
de ydropisie	Of dropsy. 
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not worth anything for a person with dropsy except in the manner which is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the manners that we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not profit at all, then it is fitting that you make four cauteries around the belly, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the thigh, and two behind the back on the spine, and one place on the breast; and let the cauteries be very close to the space of the heart.  
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterward leave the cautery uncovered to engender putrefaction for a long time, and do not leave the patient's care after the cautery; and healing will hasten, and both intentions will be fulfilled with the help of God. 
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly should be the key that we have shown before; and that for the back should be oval-shaped, according to what has been said before. 
de l’enfleure des piez	Of the swelling of the feet 
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in those who are dropsical, and are full of yellow water, it is fitting that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning. 
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not go in too deeply, so that the yellow water is strongly driven out, and let the cautery be according to this form: 
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	Afterward make on both legs two cauteries in each leg at the point of the knife; and let the cauteries be long, one below the knee in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries exposed for a long time without cleaning so that the water issues forth; afterward cure with the other cures that we have said. 
de la menoison	of the menstruation 
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When a solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, as long as the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by ways of cures; and you see the patient suffering greatly and green of complexion, then make a large cautery on the stomach according to what has been spoken of it before, or the stomach cautery, the circular cautery; and four cauteries around the navel subtle at all the subtle staple cautery, and two cauteries on the thighs. 
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moisture abundant and the patient suffering, then make a cautery on the wrist, and one cautery on each thigh, and two small cauteries on the stomach below the large one, for the cure is profitable when there is good help. 
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemorrhoids 
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or several, and they are old and are large humors cold and moist corrupted, and they are cured as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit, then make cauteries: three on the spine of the back, that which is furthest below the almecdate point by point in a triangle, and one cautery below the elbow two doses; and if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the meat does not cook, and you see the face swell, then make one large cautery on the stomach as it has been previously said, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with all the cauteries clavile; and leave the cautery open for a long time. 
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After healing the place as much as it is healed. 
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "thelul" 
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the "thelul", heat the cautery which resembles a razor, and then put it all ablaze upon the said "thelul" cut; and leave it so long as your hand and the cautery reach the birth of the vein, from which the blood flows; do this one or two times, and if there is much "thelul", cauterize each one as we have said; afterwards apply healing ointments that are beneficial as long as they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery upon the flesh, it will be of greater help. 
de plaie mal curee	of a poorly treated wound 
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or an opening, which we will recount in its place, then comes a certain illness that cannot be healed except by cautery. 
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When any fistula comes, and is old and has foul rot and corrupted moisture, if you wish to prove it with a subtle probe, and be sure that you know at all times the depth of the probe. 
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After you heat the cautery which resembles a razor, and insert it into the fistula according to the quantity that the probe has entered, and restart the cautery until those rotten and corrupted tissues are burned once, or twice, or three times, according to the quantity needed; and beware of burning the nerves that are nearby, and large veins. 
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestine, beware of these places, and do not make these fires except in a fleshy place, and think that it is not dangerous; after you treat the place until it is healed, and if the place is salty, and the materials are removed for a long time, then know that the place is completely healed; and if the materials are not removed, know that the place is narrow, and corrupted bone at the bottom; and thus as one of these that we will say in its place. 
de la maladie des reins	Of the disease of the kidneys 
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and from great windiness, and takes no pleasure from a woman, then you must make a cautery on the kidneys on one side and the other with the clavile cautery as we have said before; and if we cauterize it in the middle, it will have three cauteries in a line, and they will do more good. 
de la vessie	Of the bladder 
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the outer part above the bladder, where the hairs begin to grow, on the right and left side, and let each cautery be as long as the length of a thumb; and make one cautery above the back or two if needed; and let the cauteries be clavile according to the form previously mentioned. 
de la marris	from the marsh 
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marsh is cold and moist, and does not allow for conception at all, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are slow; and when they come, there is great pain; then it is necessary to make III cauteries around the womb, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and II cauteries behind the back; and let the cauteries be sharp, as we have said. 
de la hainche	of the hip  
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous humors descend to the hip socket, and for this reason it moves out of place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the two legs are found to be uneven in their division, then you must cauterize the patient on the hip socket with one cautery resembling a circle, and mark in front of the place around the socket as it turns, so that the socket is within the circle; and let the cautery be like those with which we have cauterized the stomach.  
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not available to you, make three large olive wood cauteries, and let the cauteries be as perfect as all hearts; and burn it until it is healed. 
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip 
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the hip joint and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured by what we have said in the division and the cure is not worth it, and the disease is old: then you must purge the patient of the thick humors with foul-smelling pills or other good-looking pills. 
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After you make the cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two ways: that is to say together burning medicines, and fire cautery. 
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is according to many ways, of which one is this: that you cauterize on the hip joint three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make them deep and large, and put between each cautery space the thickness of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive wood; sometimes one makes a cautery in the middle above the head of the hip, so that there are four according to this form:  
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, if the cautery with the fire circle that we have previously said in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circle contains all of the hip, and all the types of flesh be burned. 
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way it is done in sciatica, when the pain holds in the hip, and does not reach to the thigh nor to the leg. 
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes to the thigh and the leg, make II cauteries where the patient says the pain holds him, and I cautery above the ankle IV must, on the left side a point; and let the cauteries be lancet-shaped, and burn the thickness of the flesh; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the toes or near them, then cauterize him where he feels the pain III points or IV with the cautery which is called "points". 
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, do more; and if it seems that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, apply a cautery with a knife or circular cautery, and be very careful in all your cauteries so that you do not leave the cautery so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and so that you do not cause the patient more pain and contraction. 
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who applied a cautery on the ankle of the foot and left it so long that the leg was all swollen and the foot also, and it became pierced and corrupted all the foot. 
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After which death ensued.  
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, apply a cautery to one and the other, according to this manner.  
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the sages said about the cautery of the hip, which is the manner: make a tool like this and let the head be as thick as a doctor's nail, or a little less, and let there be spaces between the points and from one space to the other the distance of a fingernail; and let the spaces be opposite in two parts and be like knots, and let it have a handle well-made of iron; and this is its form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is all red and feels hot, and then put it on the box of the sick hip, and turn it on the healthy side; and the cauterizer once I cauterize it and leave it for III days; and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the cure of anointing until it is healed. 
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use this cautery little because of fear of its appearance, and we see few who use it; and nevertheless it is a good cautery, which can endure it, and where it applies itself. 
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The burning medicine cauteries are such that you make an instrument at intervals in which the margin of the door descends, and it is made of brass or iron with a long handle, and in its height it has two knots, and between each one the quantity of the thickness of a finger; and they are open outside and above, and they join together according to this form: 
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After place the box on the hip of the patient lying on his sound side; then press your hand firmly on the box on the hip; afterwards put between the two circles of a hot awl that has been heated in the fire for one hour, and let the patient suffer the heat and burning. 
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it finds a bite as well as of fire; and when the bites have passed, lift your hand with the instrument and raise the hip with warm water, and leave it so for three days, and put butter on it until that which is black from the scald is removed; and leave it for three days until the rot is drawn out; and this would be the last help after the cure of ointments until it is healed. 
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or to the leg, make an instrument that has a hot awl according to what you have done on the hip equally; and this is the manner of the hot awl, and I have written it in my treatise of medicine. 
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and hot coals, as much of one as the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot. 
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	Where it has a small hole so that the point of a razor can enter; and put on top of that pot another well-sealed pot, and put alkali and hot coals and sweet butter on top, as much as there are two above the powders until you have well heated it in your hand; and leave it like that until there descends watery vapor and cheese into the sealed pot, then take all that water, and pour it on the hot coals and alkali as before. 
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very watery and is administered in a variety of medical works and for cauterizing other limbs; for it does the same work as fire, and to other medicines with which one cauterizes well the hip thus mixed together: terebinth and honey, anacardium and hot coals with soap. 
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a remedy by which a man was cured of the pain of the hip and sciatic vein, and praised it greatly, saying that no other remedy was done, and that he was healed at once when this remedy was done, and he bathed himself as he teaches here afterwards. 
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in part that you take two drams of green vitriol fresh and dry, and grind it very much with a bit of fat, and put it on the hip and thigh and leg where the pain is, and bind it; and leave it for III hours and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the burning. 
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then have him enter a bath until his body is a bit warmed up, and have him enter into bed, and the pain will go away entirely and he will be healed. 
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use a cautery of such medicines unless it is after the evacuation of the body. 
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat hairs, it helps a lot; and the cautery should be done in this way. 
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take wool and soak it in old oil, and put it on the hollow between the thumb and the other finger which is called the fossa. 
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Then take dry goat hairs and ignite them until they are charcoal, and place them on the wool, leaving them there until they are extinguished. And repeat this process again and again, not ceasing to do so until you think through feeling that it has reached the hip and the pain has ceased; and this manner of cautery is called "goat hair cautery".  
de la dolor dou dos	of back pain 
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from falling or percussion or from excessive evacuation, or from similar cold, spreading matter, none of these resemblances are worth cautery, except for that which comes from an infusion of cold matter.  
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this that the patient be purged of foul pills or other similar things, and then three lines marked with notches be made on his back where the pain is, and in each line V cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can bear; and let the cauteries be made according to the cautery which is called “points”; and if you see fit, make III cauteries or IIII with the medium-sized pointed cautery according to this form:  
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a tight throat when they rise, and fear; and you find in the last spine of the back and on us the appearance which comes up on the other spines. 
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you want to cure it, cauterize it with the cautery of a circle according to this form. 
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery evenly burns each part of the spine. 
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see that you cauterize around the spine with a pointed cautery making two or three lines, and the points are close to one another. 
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	Afterward, treat the area until it is healed according to what we have said, and be careful not to administer the cautery in gibbosity which is in spasm of nerve. 
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints 
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pains of the joints are from moistures that are spread to each member of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which the wise call "podagra" properly, and when it is from a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to this form: 
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need for you to grasp the face of the foot, then burn it all with fire which we call "point." 
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, which often happens, then burn each knee with three or four cauteries on each side, with all olive oil cautery; and if you need more, do more, but do not hold your hand stronger than until the thickness of the heart is burned.  
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, give them the cautery as we have said in this chapter. 
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the wrist two lines long; and if there remains any pain in the arms, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good governance to the patient and have him take medicine. 
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give it good management and purge phlegm, it will be healed with God's help. 
de la routure dou syfac	of the fracture of the bone
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a fracture comes in anguish, and the bowels descend as though they were new, it is fitting that when you see it cleaned, it should not be disturbed that day; and let him use things that loosen the belly so that his humors descend from his belly; afterward, make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath while the bowels are repaired, and set them straight at your will, and press down below the fracture upon the bone of the wrist, and make a sign like half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery in the shape: 
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and gives off sparks. 
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bowels to their place; and let the assistants keep their hand on them so they do not move back; and work well the thighs of the patient, and put under him a cushion and a sergeant on the thighs, and another on his foot to hold his hands; then put the cautery on the sign with all your hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again another time until you come up to the bone; and be careful subtly that the eye does not protrude when you are doing the cautery; so as not to burn it; and so that by this the patient does not die, or have other ills. 
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. 
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is fitting that the cauteries of children be subtle according to the measure of their limbs, and those of large people also be as large according to their measure; after three days, treat the place of the cautery with butter until the burn is removed; then treat it with other ointments until it is healed, and have the patient lie on his back for forty days so that the wound is well closed; and it is fitting that his bandages be loosened lengthily, so that the eye does not protrude when he prepares to go into chambers. 
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wants to rise, give him a well-made bandage and let him wear it for forty other days; and let him have good rest, do little work, and beware of too much drinking and eating, and of raising his voice too high; and when he follows this instruction, he will be completely healed. 
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say here after the treatment of the thigh in its chapter. 
de la routure dou ventre	Of a rupture of the belly 
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, make a cautery on the belly according to its size, and burn one-third of the core; then treat it as we have said; and none of the ancients have said that one should cauterize it with a three-angled cautery according to this form: 
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	But first mark the site of the incision and make a line across its width above the break, and another behind it, and keep your hand steady on all sides with the heated cautery iron. 
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and milder. 
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any limb 
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, whether from a fall or a wound, and that pain lasts a long time, and medicine does not help it, then it is fitting that it be cauterized with the cautery called "points," and the cautery should be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and its virtue and its location of twists and its pain. 
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it is healed by the first cautery, that is good; if not, begin another cautery upon the first, for such a custom is that it should change to the limb that is closest, so it is fitting that you make the cauteries until the patient is healed.  
de meselerie	From medicine 
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The cautery is aided sometimes by great help, and the same disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. 
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	If you see that it can be cauterized, take care if the disease is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not spread or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the patient, then make five cauteries on the head: one towards the nape of the neck, and another towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and two on the two horns [temples], and one behind on the haunches; and leave your hand there until the cauteries reach the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors from the thick humors can escape; and cauterize the thigh according to what it is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the malady is scattered throughout; and it clearly departs, then you must cauterize it with those cauteries that we have said or chief, and one cautery on the nape of the neck, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the buttocks and another nearby, and two on the two shoulders; and two on the elbows, and two on the tendons of the foot, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are on the last bone of the leg, so that you do not burn them; and never make a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and one other on the bone of the stomach, and one other on the liver. 
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that when you make more cauteries, you do more good and it increases the benefit; and know that the sick do not feel any pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because their body is already completely corrupted. 
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauteries be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in a variety of irons. 
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After healing, dust the place with flour of spelt mixed with honey and other remedies until it is healed. 
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes in any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and poultices, but it is not healed, then make cauteries on the limb according to the size of the limb; let the cautery be a small puncture going into the thickness of the flesh; then treat it with ointments until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes cautery is done on the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; however, let no one interfere unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the nerves that move the body. 
de albaras	Of aloes 
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the illness which is called "albaras" has aged, and the medicines do not work, then cauterize with a cautery a spot perfect, according to the quantity of the species of heart so that the whiteness be removed and its color changed; then cure it with flour of vetches and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and colonic blood and almond blood, of each one part; mix everything together and bind with a cloth and air it in place until it is healed.  
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of chancre by cautery 
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre first appears and you see it stop, cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, entirely surrounding the chancre. 
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And although some say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the chancre; nevertheless, this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen several times; and a better thing is that it be cauterized around, with a cautery that is called "circular", as we have said in the discussion of cauteries. 
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot move 
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has an illness that is called "adubelati," and it is slow to heal either because of the excess it produces or because of the weakness of the patient when he is decrepit (that is, too old) and he has little blood, or because of time; and you wish to hasten its healing: then the cauterizer applies many small cauteries by pricking; after which he leaves it like that.  
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to heal. 
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you wish to pierce it with the whole cautery, heat the cautery in such a way as this is its form: 
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of that illness that is called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the core, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it burn in a twofold manner so that the course of the corruption is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the healing as long as it is perfectly healed. 
li cure dou feu par fer	The treatment by fire with iron 
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of disease there is which is called "corroding," and it is nothing else but a devouring of limbs for it eats the limbs as fire devours dry wood. 
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place which can suffer cautery with fire, then heat the cauteries both small and large according to what suits the place where the disease is; after cauterizing all around so that you eradicate all the corruption and none remains of it so that everything which is corrupted be removed. 
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for 3 days and put on the burned places softened bread with oil so that the burns from the fire are removed and all the corruption. 
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After treatment of ointments engendering flesh.  
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, it is good; and if not, begin the cautery again on that which remains from the corrupted ones. 
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this ailment has sometimes been cured with a caustic medicine instead of fire cautery; but nevertheless, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already mentioned the cure with caustic medicine in the division: take it when you need it. 
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of onions that come to the feet 
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often it happens that at the feet by defects a disease arises which is called "close" according to our understanding, and it is a large, foul thing that bleeds the foot. 
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries for this disease are according to two manners. 
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery and hot caustic cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is when you heat the iron cautery as hot as a sparrow's feather and make it from good iron to the size that it can encompass all sides of the nail and so that it has delicate edges; then you put it hot on the nail and turn your hand around the nail until it comes to the bottom of the nail; and you leave it like this for three days until it begins to rot; then you make a plaster of wild mallows crushed with salt and leave the plaster on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots. 
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the place of the cautery by anointing it with oil until it is healed. 
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by fire the body, and it often happens in hands and feet, it is necessary that you administer a hot cautery; and it is done in this way: take a cane of elder or iron, or a sparrow's feather, and put it on the nail and the surrounding skin, that is to say, warts; and put the cane on so that it encompasses all around, then he puts a piece of burning coal on and holds his hand well, and presses his hand while turning so that the edge of the cane reaches the root of the nail, and can find the hot coal deep down to the root; and let the patient endure the bite of the hot coal for an hour; then leave it like this, and it will come out by the roots. 
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Then do one after another, until you have pulled out all those that are on the body, then treat the inflammations which breed flesh. 
li cure dou trembler	The treatment of trembling 
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from coldness of nerves, or from quartan fever or other, it is fitting that you make him four cauteries or IV on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine; and one cautery at the foot, and one on the stomach with an olive cautery; this will leave the trembling, and will hasten the health from the cold illness. 
des pustules puans	Of stinking pustules 
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes appear by force on the body baths, or stinking pustules, which come from large corrupted matters.  
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	It is fitting at first when they appear that one make a cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of myrtle wood, in which the point is taken up by fire, or of long birthwort root, or a lentil cautery. 
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow further forward, but the superfluity from which they come is broken up, and they are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood. 
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut 
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are great outpourings of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes by accident, or in the incision of an abscess, or at the cautery of a limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to staunch. 
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nevertheless when this happens to anyone, if you hurry to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press it very hard so that the blood is quieted under your finger, and no drop issues forth; then heat several small and large olive-wood cauteries until they are all red; then take one, either large or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is cut, and put the cautery on the vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cautery on it as long as the blood is restrained.  
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your hand from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, quickly take another cautery that is in the fire. 
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do one after the other until the blood is stopped; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes upon the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be well stopped by itself when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by a strong ligature of thread, or by medicines put on which have the power to stop blood; and let it be bound and tightened. 
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	He who will administer a stopping of bleeding by tightly binding bandages or by putting hot things on, or other similar things, it will not profit and it will do harm. 
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and they have neither mirror nor medicine present, they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press well until it is numb above the wound and above the vein; and do not move the finger, but moisten it with cold water often, so that it be very cold, until the blood is frozen and thickened and numbed; and make inquiries beforehand about those who need cautery and medicine. 
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of treatments of wounds 
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all the diseases in which it is fitting to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and the applications, the causes, the instruments, and the forms of the cauteries; and I have placed this chapter from its head to its feet, and I will go in this chapter by the same way so that those who want them can find them more easily. 
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so as I begin this one, it is fitting, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and because of this it is necessary for greater caution. 
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter there often occurs evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die. 
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly. 
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for treatment. 
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	Some come who are so frightened by their illness that they die easily because of the fear they find from their illness and the severity of its harm; and one must be afraid of these. 
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And some of these give you their meaning and say: “wait, I am healed”; and the illness is pitiful. 
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put greater caution in your honor than in your greed, and do not work rashly but wisely with those of whom you are certain, and whose illness you can take and treat; and use prognosis and indication in the cures of your patients so that health is restored; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, glory, and long remembrance.  
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lord gives you good understanding and uprightness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, amen. 
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have ordered this chapter by dividing it into chapters, according to what is before it, the chapter on cauteries, which I have divided from beginning to end so that you can more easily find what you need. 
dou chief plein d’aigue	Full of sharp pain 
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this ailment often comes to children at birth, and when the midwife pulls the child's head too hard; and sometimes it comes from a cause unknown. 
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never saw this ailment except in children, and all those I have seen hastened death; and therefore it seems to me that I would rather leave the work in such cures. 
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose shoulder was full of sharp pain, and the head grew larger each day until it could no longer support it; and the moisture grew so much that it died, and this moisture gathered under the bone above the spine, between the heart and the bone; and the work is such if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, that you make a wide slit in the head; and it should be as long as two of us, so that the moisture can run out; and see the shape of the speculum:  
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is thicker and the abscess larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form: 
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is below the bone and the signs you see are that the corners of the head are open on each side, and a sharp pain goes through when you press it with your hand inside, and this is not answered by the patient: then you must cut three incisions into the middle according to this manner: 
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture. 
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After extracting the moisture, cover the incisions with linen and powders, apply wine and oil, and leave it like that for five days; then untie it and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, allowing the head to be straightened evenly, and let the patient eat dry meat free of moisture as long as the limb is strengthened and healed. 
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look where the size of the abscess appears, and its gathering of pus; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left. 
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore cut where the abscess appears, and the gathering of pus, and make the incision according to your ability; and beware that you do not sever an artery; and let flow a little blood so that the patient does not die from the depletion of blood and evacuation of moisture. 
de reume	of rheumatism
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When a disease called "catarrh" occurs in the eyes or breasts, and the illness is old, and medicine does not help, then the final remedy is cautery with which one severs the two arteries. 
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you have severed them, it is necessary that the patient lays his head back; then rub the area with a coarse cloth until the arteries appear, then pull the patient's neck taut with the cloth; then look where the vein beats, and the two sides are after the ears, and they are filled up; then mark the sides with chalk, then sever both with a sharp knife in two parts, so that blood flows to the bone, and this is done across the breadth of the head. 
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see it, put the spatula underneath the artery and the cup above, cutting as much as needed through. 
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood flows continuously upward.  
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open with feeling, it is necessary that you measure the quantity of space of three fingers, then cut from there to the bone; and what blood should flow out is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less according to what the patient can suffer and the repletion of the artery. Then look at the wound: if there remains above the bone a point that does not weep pus, then it is necessary that you cut the abscesses so they do not come back, then strain the wound and bind it, and treat it with ointment until it heals. 
de emigrainne	of migraine  
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine comes, and acute catarrh, due to moisture from tears and the heat in the temples and a supposed ancient indisposition and similar things, and it is treated by methods of medicine and all that does not profit it at all, then we extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them as we have told. 
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the way of extracting them is this: the patient shaves the hair from his temples and feels for the artery that appears in the temple, for it appears well by its beating and is less full than in some men who are too cold; and if it is full, then the patient constricts its neck with some cloths, and then rubs the area with a rough cloth and applies hot water to the area until the artery appears clearly; then take the scalpel which has this shape:  
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then lightly scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then hold it up with forceps and remove all the cobwebs that are beneath it from each side; and if the artery is delicate, turn it at the point of the hook, then cut that part according to the quantity of the two heads. 
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, it will not jump out completely at all. 
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And let the blood flow for six to three hours; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread so that rot does not come before the suture of the wound, and blood flows; then cut off the excess between the two ties at that very hour; and then, if you see fit, cauterize the wound with a sharp cautery down to the bone until the heads are cut off; this is a small operation if the patient does not have a fever and is of hot complexion.  
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cautery is aid to finish the humors; therefore it is of greater aid against humors. 
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, it is fitting that one fill the place with old cotton and put well-made tents on top; and when they are untied, let it be treated with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and with tents, until it is healed; and if there is a lack of the artery as much as you work, hurry to cut it with cautery, or apply vitriol to the place and hold it in your hand so that the blood is stanched; and if you do not have this present, put your finger on the place until the blood is frozen, and apply cold water to the place so long as the blood stops, and extract it as it should be; and what is easier and lighter for the extraction of an artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cutting cautery in two parts, but let the cuttings be well spaced to keep their heat longer.  
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds less heat. 
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have between the two blades a space of one finger's width, and then when you have marked to cut the two sides, and you place the hot iron upon it until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two; and they are spaced between the two sides because it is not soldered altogether; and this is the form of the cautery. 
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are descending from the veins that are on the top of the head of a person, and no medicine cure that one does, and you see the face of the patient reddening, and feels his forehead throbbing like shivering; and his oils are thin and moist so that the hair on the papers is fallen out, and the papers are heated and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this cure is needed.
