Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it the ancients “cure contuse”, and you make at the back of the patient who has this ailment the hairs that he has on his forehead, then you make III cuts on his forehead equally according to the length of his forehead; and let one of the cuts be as long as II fingers altogether going down along the forehead until the nose, and the other II as II ribs are above the paper, and guard yourself from cutting into the arteries that are at II sides above the papers; and remove your hand from the continuation of the II jaws, and let each wound be the quantity of III fingers across joined together; and have ready a piece of sponge and much linen to wipe up the blood, then put in the spatula sharpened on II sides which is this shape: 
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is down from the temple to the second incision; and scrape away all the flesh that is between the II cuts as far as the membrane which is on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second one, and then pull out this spatula. 
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you put in the first fissure the instrument which is called "cultellaire", and it is very sharp on one side, and blunt on the other side, that is its form: 
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the sharp side towards the flesh that is to be cut, and the blunt side towards the bone, and put it in until it reaches the middle fissure. 
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the flesh so that the incision is continuous until it reaches what appears at the heart, and then make another incision in the middle fissure until the other side; and then draw out the blood equally, and press on the place for the blood to be drawn out; then put in each fissure a tent of old cotton, and put on cloths softened in wine and oil and anise, and guard that no abscesses form there; and on the third day untie the bandage, and apply a large poultice of hot water, then cure with ointment basilicon mixed with rose oil, and other cures as one cures wounds, until it is healed. 
dou reume des eulz	about rheum of the eyes 
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When some catarrh comes acutely accustomed and you see the eyes red and small and weakens the sight and the papers burned; and the hair falls out and where it falls there is acute pain and the patient sneezes; then know by these accidents that those humors and this catarrh come not only from many veins, but the cure which it has if it is this. 
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to raise his forehead, then make a large incision above the forehead, and another one as wide down to the cheekbone. 
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the incision of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples which move the jaw; and when the bone is uncovered, if you wipe all the blood with a sponge, then insert between the two lips of the incision and put old cotton, and linen bandages; then tie over soft cloths moistened in wine and oil, and beware of a hot abscess; when it is removed, it is fitting that you rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then cure it with drying things which cause the growth of flesh. 
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of colophony and make a plaster; and administer it in these wounds to draw flesh everywhere. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	For the deafness of ears  
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that is lodged in the ears is one of four things: either grains or beasts, or stones from mines or similar things such as iron; or seed, such as peas, beans, lentils; or flowing things such as water and pus and similar things. 
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When there is a stone or another kind of thing lodged in the ear that does not adhere to the ear nor grow in the ear, set the ear in the sun.  
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, instill a few drops of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and make him sneeze with caution, and plug his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and stretch the ear upward.  
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times it comes loose through this treatment; and if it does not come loose, you should administer extraction with delicate forceps, the form of which is this: 
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes loose with the forceps, that is good; if not, you should administer extraction with a delicate awl of small size; and if it does not come loose by this, make a cane of elder and insert the head of the cane or hole of the ear strongly, and stuff what is around the cane with soft wax so that the veins cannot enter with the cane; then draw it out forcibly, for many times it comes loose as we have said; and if it does not come loose in any of these ways, take glue of which you catch birds, and put some on any instrument suitable for this, and put a bit of cotton around; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and draw it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not jump further from all these things that we have said, then hasten to split the ear as an abscess that has boiled and a spasm; and the manner of the incision is that you first bleed the patient from the cephalic vein, and draw out blood according to the measure of his strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn his ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear in the fat or place depending; and let the incision be as round as the moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your power, and suck it quickly into your mouth; and heal it until it is healthy. 
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grain that is within and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer a thin, subtle spatula according to this form: 
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	And make an incision near that grain. 
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grain is moist because of ear moisture, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with delicate pincers and a sucker, as we have said, so that the extraction is smooth. 
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In sharp pain, then when a shoulder joint is in the ear it is necessary for the patient to use sneezing initially, and stuff the ear with old cotton. 
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on that same ear where the pain is. 
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps strongly because of this, it is good. 
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take many stones according to the length of your thumb, light and smooth, and heat them a little in the fire; and put one or two of them in the patient's ear, and press on it with your feet on the other side, and strike one stone upon the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease doing this from stone to stone until all the pain has ceased, so that it jumps away completely; and if you see that, take a wire, and put one end in the ear, and grasp the other end with fire until the thinnest wire is burned; then repeat with other wires until all the pain is gone, as we have said with the stone.  
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of a beast, if it is of small size, such as a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size so that one can feel it, then use extraction with tweezers; and this is the lightest thing to remove which is in the ear. 
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the removal of worms embedded in the ears, when you cure it as we have said in the division and when treating distillations, and the cure does not profit, then you must look at the ear in the sunlight: if there appears any worms, then remove them with fine tweezers; and if they do not appear, take a cane of which this is the form: 
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above. 
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the most subtle tip into the ear according to the amount of the patient's suffering, then draw it out slowly with all the cane; do this often until all the worms come out. 
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to come out, stuff cotton around the cane as I have said in the stone; and if they do not come out forcefully as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven for the removal of worms, and you will find them or treat the distillations; and if you distil your oils and medicines in the ear with all these instruments, from which this is the form as you see: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	Whether it is of silver or iron, make three holes below the small openings, and above cover for distilling; and to press the distillation inside the instrument of iron well made for this, and if you see take the razor and wrap cotton around the point evenly; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you see of your medicines into the cane, and let the cane be in the ear; then put the razor into all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or finished from the ear; and the patient feels it inside, and let the distillation be slightly heated by fire thus so that it is distilled in the ear; and beware that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as good.  
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping up of ears 
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have some opening in their ears; and the same thing happens to men by stoppage of a wound, or by something getting stuck inside the ear, and this stoppage sometimes comes entirely in the ear, so that one cannot see it; and sometimes there appears a small hole in the opening, and one can see well. 
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, that which comes entirely in, if one cannot see it, is of a troublesome nature in several ways, and in this case where you see it, you must put the patient's ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see apparent swelling, the work has already begun its course, because this is its form. 
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be sharp and pointed both in front and behind, so that it does not hurt the ear; if the swelling is from something stuck or a piece of skin on the ear, then hold it with fine tweezers, and remove it gently, until all those things are removed.  
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the operation is performed perfectly in the ear, then take a subtle, light razor and heat it a little over the fire, then apply it to the flesh of the ear. 
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the operation causes the patient pain in the ear, pierce it lightly and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear; then place a tent in the ear according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment. 
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for no day until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it with rose water and powder on ground vitriol; and if you see the ear swell, then it is fitting that you draw out the tent and put in another tent moistened with cerate which is made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then cure it until it is healed.  
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, dip a sponge and cloths in cold water, and place them on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the bleeding, which are used to treat distillations. 
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of paper  
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This ailment which comes in papers from the eyes when they are moist and dry, it is fitting that you extend them with pincers and tweezers, and cut off the tip of a spatula from its roots; then put vitriol powder on the spot.  
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they do not come out, cauterize them with a lentiform cautery, and cauterize again after the incision heals; and many times they repair, when nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, their roots are destroyed and they do not return.  
de la gresle	of gravel 
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come upon the eyes things that seem rough in their form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "grandine," and it is a gathering of thick moisture in the eye above and below; the operation is such: take care if the grandine moves from one side to the other, and this is an easy thing to know; then make two large incisions, then lightly scrape each part, then take it with forceps and cut it out. 
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it out, then pierce the eye a little, and it will not grieve the patient; and if the fissure is large, and the gathering has a seam, cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not force it, for ointments restore it quickly and bring flesh. 
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grandine descends into the inside of the ear towards the upper part, then invert the eyelid, and take the grandine with forceps, and cut it out and press from one side and the other; and if the eyelid is removed by incision, it does not grieve anything; and when the grandine is cut out, wash the eye with salt water, and heal the place that brings flesh until the patient is healed. 
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes 
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is spread on cloths of paper upon it, and this happens more to children than to adults, and it grieves much their eyes, and there comes to them catarrh in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears hasten to their eyes; and for this reason they lie down upon their faces often, and sleep upon them, and have their papers under their eyebrows moist that the swelling and appearance have covered with exinach which appears in the eye. 
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place at your two fingers and feel the exinach between them.  
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is such that the patient puts his head in your lap; and then take a cloth of linen, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity which contains exinach from each part, then put it upon it; and press with your two fingers on one side and the other, so that the exinach is gathered within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture at the spatula cutting a slit about as wide, and not be any larger than the wound that one makes to open a vein; and make the skin perfect until you come to the exinach; and in several positions comes exinach out of the slit, according to the form of a piece of white fat.  
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take then a whole piece of charpit cloth between your hands near the fire and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread; and be careful not to put anything in the fissure so that you do not reach all the spatulum up to the eye, lest you blind it. 
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the splinter does not appear at the beginning of the fissure, slightly enlarge the fissure until it appears; then extract it as we have said, and moisten cloths with vinegar and water and apply them to the place and bind with bandages. 
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind salt and put it on to corrupt the remaining moisture.  
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed. 
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess comes to the place, treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed. 
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of paper 
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper hairs are added other than those of nature and they are old, they harm them and cause various diseases such as accustomed tears and softening of the papers and albugine, as long as it is a cause of their destruction; and the cure is according to four methods: either by cautery with fire, or by a sharp medicine according to that which is before in this chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and suture or by canes, according to what I will say. 
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the head of the patient in your lap, then turn the paper from the eye to your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, if you put a needle through all the threads on top of it; and let this be near the edge of the paper or where the hairs grow near these hairs, and pull the thread on top of all the paper, and turn it to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the added hairs, at all the spanile cutting, from the large tear to the small; then remove the thread, and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and linen, then draw on the paper a figure of an anchor, like the leaf of myrtle, and it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see raise the paper which is divided into all. 
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is someone who needs a large quantity of paper according to how soft the paper is; then make a mark on all the spatulate lines that you have signed, and begin from the largest tear to the smallest; and let one of the tears be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the needle into one of the two angles of the heart, then flay it all; then bring together the two lips with a stitch using a needle and a thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and air out the superfluity of the threads on the two eyebrows for any gluing things, if you see fit to do this; and if not, don't worry about it, then leave the stitch and the threads until three days or four; then treat the wound without stitches with drying and constricting things, because the paper will adhere at the healing of the wound and its assembly, but the stitch is useless (as the ancients said), and this work is done without fear; and if there is another way: and it is that you mark the paper with a figure that is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have recounted, at three needles according to the shape which is here: 
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then take that which surpasses small strengths equally according to the shape which is here. 
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with thread, and put it into the shape; and put one thread beyond the large tear, and the second thread beyond the small one, and assemble between your two hands the threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin on which you have marked, as we have told, then assemble the two edges of the wound by suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; and it sometimes happens that the hair of the paper is converted: then it is necessary that you use what we have said about the incision; but the suture in one and the other is more artificial. 
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the canes is done in this way: and it is that you convert the paper and put the end inside according to what I have said, and then make two canes by art, and two fine ligatures as long as the paper and the width of a span; and cut as two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on what protrudes from the paper at the eye, and strain the two canes from the two parts form; and leave it like that for several days, and the leather which will grow strained will die and harden and carry, as long as it seeks by itself.  
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes too long, cut with one force, then cure until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, and if the paper is removed, and they will no longer pull the hair; and this is the shape of the two canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width: 
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a very fine needle and thread a very fine silk thread through it; then bring the edges together and tie them both delicately, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then arrange another fine silk thread on the top quickly and tie the two ends of the thread together; then have the patient put his head in your lap; and be near the sun so that the work is illuminated, for it is a delicate and small piece of work; then put the needle all the way through the root of the hair next to it, and make it pierce the paper quickly while you are drawing it over the natural hair; then pull the hair up to the top of the paper, and thread the hair into the top; if there is one or two or three or more hairs; then withdraw your hand so that the hairs come out at the top of the paper with the natural hair. 
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the boil is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, you will treat the boil below along the thread that you have ordered, until the boil comes out through the hole above it and you see it with the vision of your eye; then you will treat the boil and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh grows over it; and if the hairs are small, you will accompany them with one long horsehair, which will be raised along with the one that you leave, until it is lengthened and then you will remove it. 
de la porriture de l’oil	from the corruption of the eye 
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacratio" or corruption comes to the eye, there are two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural. 
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs by means of a wound, or a cut, or a cautery, and by similar things. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of the work on it is that you cleave that suture, and separate the lips of it, and put linen tents inside, and bind it until it is healed; and it does not behoove that you use in its cure things that dry and constrict. 
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the sickness returns worse than the first; but work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and rose water or elderflower water and flaxseed cooked, and unguents of diamas dissolved in any of the oils, and envelop a tent, and cure it with this. 
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not heal according to the shape it had before; and this work which we have said is nothing other than directions for this ailment, so that it does not return according to the shape it had before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye 
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness which is below, which is truly called "axacrati," and it is natural and accidental. 
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental cause comes from a wound and a fissure and a cautery and similar things; and the way of working in this is that you take a needle, in which it has a double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear duct as far as the right, so that the threads come out on both sides of the flesh; then lift the flesh above the entire needle, and cut at a span wide. 
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what is necessary, it is good; if not, take a razor and put it in the fissure, and turn the paper, and make two fissures on either side within the paper; and let the sides of the two fissures be at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and make one angle so that when they are joined together, the shape is like the shape of a Greek letter "I"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its sides are below, from that which follows the paper, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of wool; then care for it as we have said with softening medicines and bandages, until it is healed. 
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the ailment comes from a cut or suture or cautery, it is necessary that you make a full cut below the hairs of the skin, and according to what has been said before; then detach between the two edges of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the ailment, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare instruments of all sorts so that they can bring the figure back to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what he needs of work and instruments, has several positions. 
dou soudement de la papiere	For the stitching of the skin 
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this stitching occurs in a way that the skin above is sewn with the white of an egg, and it cannot move nor do its natural actions, then it is necessary that you put the point of a razor under the skin and lift it up; and hold it with pincers, as long as you cut what is attached to the subtle spatula, which is not too sharp nor too cutting, so that the patient does not suffer that the spatula is too sharp or that the oil is irritated; and let your incision, from which you detach the joined parts, be light, so that the skin returns according to its natural form; and it heals all the joined parts, and sometimes in the stinging salted water, and lift with lukewarm water, and with colander; then put between the skin and the oil a linen tent, and put on the oil moistened wool abundantly soaked with egg yolk; and after the third day use lukewarm colander and things that are softened as long as it is healed. 
de l’ungle de l’oil	From the corner of the eye 
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is according to two manners: one is nervous and appears like hard flesh, and another which is not nervous, but appears like white frozen moisture, which when touched by iron and one thinks it will bite as pincers, yet one cannot; and both these appearances begin near the large tear duct and grow little by little until they cover all the sight and all the light and movement of the eye. 
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is such that the patient puts his head in a healthy position, then opens his eyes; and lifts the paper with your hand, then coils the nail like pincers of small double-twist, and extends it upward; then takes a needle, and puts horsehair, or cowhair, or oxhair, and strong thread; and doubles the point of the needle a little and inserts it into the nail, and pierces it through with the whole needle, and ties the nail with thread and extends it upward, and scrapes all the hair along the side of the nail which covers the wrinkle and the silk to the hair up to the head, then cuts off the remainder at the root by the tear duct with a very thin spatula and with small forces, and leaves the flesh natural or tear duct so that by the incision no body fluid accustomedly comes; and sometimes extend the nail only to the eyelid with thread as we have said; then scrape it on the whole side of which is its form:  
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the speculum does not touch the fleshy web and tear it, and that the pupil is not pierced; and after the incision place in the eye a piece of silk thread, and with a collar made of silver, and leave it until the next day; then treat it as needed until it is healed. 
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot insert the needle, and the forceps cannot enter, many times this appearance of a nail is cured by medicines; and it grows as I have said in the division, and if you see it covered, work on the eye of the patient, and take the speculum, a small sharp piece according to this form: 
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail subtly, and if you see that it diminishes a little and the rasping presses it, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collar made of silver and with a red collar and silk thread, and close the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same work, until it is all removed. 
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you in the eye, such as an abscess, then milk it and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed. 
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh around the tear duct obstructs in the eye by great harm, then suspend it to an awl and cut off a part and not all at once so that no bodily fluid comes forth; then distill into the eye red collyrium which is made from litharge. 
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the iris 
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In the eye of some men flesh sometimes grows red and covers the iris and extends onto the eyelids, and it resembles a rosehip; and the work is such that the patient places their head in a healthy position, then they work on the flesh, and cut all the flesh with suitable awls for this purpose, and hold it firmly; then they cut the first flesh, and continue cutting with a razor until the end, and be careful not to damage the eye during the work; and let the incision be made in the spatula as we have said in the incision of the nail and with small forces with which one removes the pus, as the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, apply oil of almonds well crushed or distill red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines into it, and put over the eye a hot compress with a mixture of egg white so that it is well secured from a hot abscess; and if there remains anything, and the pus still troubles you and you doubt a hot abscess, then leave the eye and treat the abscess with soothing things for a hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and do this as many times as flesh grows in the eye by this manner.  
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless it is necessary that you lighten the treatment of each weak vein of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works as long as you see that this member suffers from this work. 
des voines des eulz	of veins of the eyes 
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	These are red veins that are covered on the eye, and they tolerate at sight their work and weaken the eye every day. 
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary therefore that the first thing you look at is whether the eye is red, strong, and there is no other disease except for the redness; then treat it in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head in your lap, then suspend those veins at every angle according to his skill, and let the angles be subtle double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be two ounces by degrees in the body according to this form: 
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then you will cut these veins subtly, and wipe the blood hour after hour until you see those veins move away from the eye; and be careful not to prick the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you only cut the veins; and when you have done this, pour green and red collyrium into the eye to corrupt what remains inside. 
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot remove it all in that hour, make a plaster on the eye with soothing things for its pain, and leave it for several days until the pain is relieved and it is assured of a hot abscess, then start again according to the manner described above until it is healed; and this is the form of the forces: 
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye 
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	They are called "arissati" fistulas; when you treat it with cautery and burning medicine as I have previously said, and it is not healed, then cut into the abscess where it should drain, and extract all the moisture that is there until the bone is exposed. 
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, then shape all the instruments as follows; it is called "sharp head" and is made of very hard iron in the shape shown, and pointed like a file as shown in its present form. 
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	Place it on the spot of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two fingers and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is removed, and do this several times, then restore the place with drying medicines. 
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is soldered and flesh grows, and the body of the bowel is soldered and remains thus for forty days, and it does not reopen and is not abscesses, and no evil accidents befall it, know that it is healed; if this is not so, and there is nothing else to do but to bring the fistula back to the perforation of the nose according to this manner: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron and with sharp medicines; and when it is uncovered take a drill in this manner, and let the head of the iron be at three angles and let the bit be thinned down to the point as you see here. 
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the tear duct and move your hand away from the eye a bit, then turn the drill until it pierces the bone, and let the patient feel it by placing their hand on their nose; then restore the place with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and the wound hardens, guide the matter to the nose; this is a lighter thing for the patient.  
de l’issue de l’oil	From the removal of the eye 
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye has opened completely and there is no sign of clouding or diminishing, it is necessary to bind the patient; then bandage, then apply cupping glasses or a hot iron to suck, then put on the eye a plaster made of acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocolle, and then strain the eye, and apply a plaster over bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is such that you take cloths soft enough, and double each one into four, and then place one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye needs; then bind it with a hard bandage above, and resume cupping glasses to suck without hurting; then remove the cupping glasses and leave the strained eye day and night, and if the bandages loosen, it is necessary to tighten them very much; then remove the bandage after day and night, and if you see the eye recover, that is good; if not, resume the plaster and cloths and the bandage and the cupping glasses until it is healed. 
dou derrompement de toile uvee	For a tear of linen cloth 
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a rupture comes in the linen cloth, and it opens up, and there are strong papers like resin grains, and it is noticeable to see; then if you want to sew it together, the work is such that you stick a needle into the root of the part below up to that above, then you stick another needle where it has double thread from the tear part; and make it pierce through, and leave the first needle according to its position; then sew the place of the double thread and tie one part of the linen around, and pull it tight, then remove the needle and put a wool cloth soaked in abundance of egg white on top; and let it be there as long as the threads heal with the linen, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and never restrict the wound by the linen on any side with a circle of cloth, as long as it is healing. 
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye shows a great appearance, pierce it with a fine spatula that comes perfectly in line with the eye, and drain the white moisture and draw out the eye, and insert it again quickly; then extract it when it is healed. 
de la bowe de l’oil	from the bowel of the eye 
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This illness which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but the bowel that is gathered in the eye, appearing like descending acute [pain], and it is not acute; and the manner of its appearance for the operation is such that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands in two parts, and move it so that you see the bowel come up over your eyes; then be careful it does not descend and be obscured from the light, and have the patient look at things as they usually do; and if it does not descend below, know that it is acute, and if the descending of the bowel is not equal as we have said. 
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take a subtle spatula and cut on the cornea with it, point by point, along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea, until the bowel is lifted; and when it is raised, you should distill in sharp hot oil mixed with honey, or sharp fenugreek boiled with honey, then let it be cured with another remedy until it is healed. 
des aigues de l’oil	Of the sharp oil 
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen similarities of sharpness in division, and what it is necessary to pierce; so work according to health. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands crossed, far from the light of the sun, and bind the healthy eye tightly; then put the paper of the oil in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called “almagda”, or in your left hand if the eye is right; then put the point of the instrument near the cornea by the thickness of a ray in the white of the eye at the side of the smaller tear duct, then push the instrument which is called “almagda” virtuously, and turn your hand so that it pierces into the white of the eye, and feel that the almagda arrives at the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the almagda path be perfect in the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the blackness; and this is the cornea of the eye; if you see the bone in the paper because of the clarity of the cornea, then put the instrument up to where the sharpness is, then press it down one path after another.  
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the point is aimed now, let the patient see it in front of them and the instrument in their eye. 
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After a little rest, and if the point goes back up the second way, put force with the instrument, and when it is stuck in and it does not rise, extract the almond slightly by turning your hand bit by bit; and then put the point back in a bit of silk thread, and lift the eye from within. 
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply the eye with compresses of wool or linen soaked in rose oil and egg white, and tie it with the healthy eye. 
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, we and those of our time, put common broth on it with egg white. 
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almond cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have eyes too hard, then you must take the instrument which is called "alberet," which has this form: 
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle opening; then insert the almond, as we have said; and for the completion of the work, prepare the patient with an approaching doctor, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and let him be devoid of all movements, and take light meats, and not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and let him be bound according to his disposition until the third day; then untie him in that same darkened house, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then re-tie him until the seventh day; and it is not fitting that you do this during the hour of treatment or after the incision now, but it is fitting that you delay this, because the sharpness rises quickly. 
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When abscesses come, untie the eye before the seventh day and refer it to one who soothes abscesses; and when it is appeased, untie the vision and place an oriliet on his face to cover it for a few days, and let him remain in that darkened house. 
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then he should leave the house little by little, and return to his usual activities; and know that no disciples should interfere in this case. 
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the land of Yrach, who told us that in his country people made a drink called almagda, with which one succeeded in obtaining the aguish, but for all that I never saw any in our land, nor did I ever read of it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing. 
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagda, so that those who do not know them may recognize them: and they are properly made of iron: 
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And the heads of these are also of this same subtlety, and the rear ends in three sharp angles.  
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh to the bone 
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes there are born or grow fleshy growths of various kinds, some of which appear like scorpions with many feet; and if there are such that have flesh tinged with a fox's color, and if there is flesh of bone color.  
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In those cases of these carts which are soft and not hardened, it is fitting that you make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open their nostrils and pour the ointment on those carts and draw them out; then cut what you can hold with a subtle sharp spatula on one side, as much as you know that this cart is entirely removed. 
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be cut, work on it with all the subtle instruments lightly so that nothing remains; and if without pain there is a boil or abscess, treat it as needed; and if these are malignant boils hasten and cauterize until the blood is dried up and all the carts are removed, then pour or smear easily with sharp or wine vinegar. 
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the vinegar works and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healed; and if the moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is a cart lodged in the bone above which the instruments cannot reach to cut: then it is fitting that you put a flax thread one hand thick and knotted by hand, and have between each knot a space of an inch or less; and place the patient's cheek on the thread in their nose at their highest power, and draw while smelling until it comes through the nostril into the mouth; and many times they do this to children in schools, and it is a light thing for one who wants to do it; then hold the head that comes through the nostril with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and pull them one after the other as we are who are on the thread. 
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do as much as you know that the new flesh has corrupted the wound, then draw the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and put it back in place at the beginning as before; do this for III days or more, until the ointments corrode everything that remains of the flesh; and then put a reed cane in the wound for several days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, through which one distills oils and medicines into the wound. 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	It should be made of silver or iron, resembling an open lamp, like a cane, and lead it the same way; and if you see that you need to, make a closed cane, and let the instrument be full for purging the head; and it has a handle on the head for holding it while heating the oil or any liquid. 
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh out of the nose 
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.
