Many times is born at the head out of the nose a disease which is called “telul”, and it grows and becomes large until it is a thing to behold; and for this reason it behoves you to cut it off at the beginning, and remove all the bone, then put upon its place a cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays cutting it until it is large, be careful if it is hard, of dark color, of poor sense: do not touch it with iron for it is an ulcerous abscess, for when one cuts it, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of dark color, and you see that one may cut all of it, then empty the patient and cut without fear, and heal the place with drying and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn 
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes in one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men. 
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary when this happens to anyone, if you see that the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two edges together in one suture, then care for it until it is healed; and if the edges are already separated on both sides, then you must scrape all the parts of their core so that they bleed, then bring the two edges together in a suture, and extract it, and sprinkle powder upon powder of dragon's blood, and ground incense; and put upon the powders a piece of plaster of Paris or other soldering plaster, and leave it until it drains by itself, then care for it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of suturing is such that you bring together the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or by thread, as I have shown you. 
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips  
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Sometimes there occurs within the lips an abscess hard, appearing like grains of lentils, both smaller and larger; then it is fitting that you turn back the lips, and split upon each node, and take them with pincers and cut in each part; then apply white lead after the incision with powdered vitriol, as long as the blood is stopped; and then a dressing of linen, and treat the area with dry things until it is healed.  
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums 
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times arises upon the gums flesh added, which the ancients called "albulus"; it is fitting that you hold it with forceps, and cut it at its root, and let run the pus or blood; then apply upon the area powdered vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders; and if that flesh returns after the incision, and this often happens, cut it a second time, and cauterize: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting. 
des sordens	of the deaf 
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow-green, as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth are foul-smelling; it is fitting that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his jaws be in your lap, and raise the teeth or the scabs that appear, as much as there remains nothing; and thus do from the blackness and the greenness, and from the jaundice and the other stains, as much as they are cleansed; and if one removes that which is at the first reason, it is good; if not, one begins again on the second day and the third, as long as you have all raised; and know that teeth need various forms of instruments to raise, according to what the work shows, for the razor with which one raises the front teeth has other forms than those with which one raises between the teeth; and these forms and others be prepared with you. 
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat a tooth for its pain that you delay the pulling as much as you can, for this one must not do; because it is a very high substance until one has no excuse for pulling. 
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to pull, it is necessary that you are certain of the aching tooth. 
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and he thinks that it is in a sound tooth, and pulls out the good tooth; and nevertheless the pain does not depart because of this, as long as the bad one remains, for we have often wanted to do this to these gentlemen; and when you are well certain of the aching tooth, it is necessary that you scratch around the tooth at all its gum with a very sharp instrument to protect the gum from all sides; then move it to your two hands or to subtle pincers at the first stroke and stroke until it is well loosened, then firmly grasp the pincers; and have the head of the patient in your lap between your knees, and hold him well so that he does not move. 
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and insert its point into each side lightly, and move it as you did at first. 
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and gnawed, it is necessary that you fill it with rags where the holes are; and if you extract it subtly with forceps, so that it does not break when extracted; and it is very wise to work around the gum to loosen the tooth. 
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be very careful not to break it, and a part remains, and returns to the patient through the wickedness of the root greater pains than the first. 
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not do as ignorant barbers do, who through their haste and boldness sometimes break the jawbone and do not apply what we have said; but they bring about a great illness many times because of the roots that remain, or for the jawbone that they break, as we often see; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply powdered vitriol; and if this does not work, cauterize it. 
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments with which one pulls the teeth first should have long points and large handles so they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms: 
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have large members so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be of good well-made iron, and they should have teeth to hold the molars. 
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth 
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after pulling, it is fitting that you put on the spot cotton moistened with butter for one or two days, 
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	so that the gums are softened, then you put in the forceps which are called "algefri", of which the head resembles a bird's beak; and they are made inside like a file and this is the form: 
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these forceps, it is fitting that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and put in the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say, a chisel, of which this is the form: 
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps because of this, it is good; if not, help yourself with all the instruments, from which the forms come hereafter: 
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument which has two handles, of which here is the form:  
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other ironworks which are in front according to the reason of teeth, and of this instrument which seems like large tongs, of which here is the form: 
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be strong so that it cannot break, and know that many instruments with teeth exist; and also other instruments which are not counted; and wise master craftsmen invent by themselves their own instrument according to what their works and the illness show them, for there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach any instrument because of the diversity of others, so that it does not break the chariot or other bones, or it rots, if he seeks the instruments which suit it, as I have told you, and help yourself with gestures, of which here is the form: 
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be thick and strong to hold the bone so that it does not escape, but can hold it and remove it; and then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, if you have all these instruments. 
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural course of the body, and the shape is ugly, even in young women, it is necessary that you know if the density is born after the tooth, and is not in its proper place, and it cannot be treated or filed: then the rasp; and if it is loose with the tooth, take this instrument which has this shape, and is similar to a small beak, and is made of sharp iron at the end. 
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the rasp cuts little by little in your hands for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be filed, take a file of this type which has this shape:  
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and file the tooth little by little in the hand lightly so that it does not move until it falls out; then smooth it at the end with no razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and it cuts the tongue, then you must file the sharpness until it is even so that it does not cut the tongue nor corrupt speech. 
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth falls out 
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth falls out, either by percussion or by falling out, and the patient cannot press on what he eats without it hurting, and you have treated him with astringent medicines, and that is no good; then you must restrict it with a thread of gold, because a thread of silver turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see that you need to straighten the teeth, take the thread and wrap it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the loose teeth between the good teeth, if there is one or several, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin the wrapping again to the part where you started, and pull your hand subtly and carefully so that it does not move; and let your ligation be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.  
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the head of the bone with forceps and bring them together and place it between the healthy teeth so that it does not bite the tongue. 
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is knocked out, if you put it back in its place again and again, as we have said; and no one interferes who is not wise and experienced, and sometimes one makes the shape of a cow's bone tooth, and puts it in the place where the lack is, and removes it as we have said, and it stays and serves for a long time. 
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut the ligament of the tongue 
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this ligament that comes from under the tongue by nature, which one is born with; or by accident of a sewn wound; and the work is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your lap, and lift his tongue; then cut the nervous ligament broadly, so that the tongue is freed from its attachment, and if there is hardness or knot, and it is from sewing of a wound, then put in the hook and cut the broad ligament; and be careful that the incision is not too deep, because of the artery that is under; and when you have done, apply a dressing of rose water and vinegar, or cold water, and then place a linen tent under the tongue; and bind it each night, so that the wound cannot close.  
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if there is a flow of blood, apply powdered vitriol to the place; and if it does not stop, cauterize it with a lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed. 
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is of a dark color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is inclined to whiteness, and there is moisture, then cut the skin with a fine scalpel, and deliver it from one side and the other; and if the bleeding does not stop in your work, apply powdered vitriol until it is extinguished, then return to your work until you draw out everything; then lift the place from its ailment and treat it with other remedies until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat 
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there come within the throat boils which are called “godath”, and they are properly called the two almonds, and when you treat them as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is a hard abscess of small size and dusky color, do not touch it with iron at all. 
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron at all, also for the discharge of blood; but leave it until it is ripe, and then you will cut it, or it will burst on its own; and if it is whitish in color and the root is slender, prepare the instrument to cut, but first look to see if the abscess has cooled down and is quieted. 
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit facing the sun, and his hands should be in your hands, and open the mouth and take the forceps between his hands and press the tongue down below the instrument, so that it takes this shape; and it should be of silver or of fine steel just like a knife: 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Press your tongue against all these instruments, and you will see the abscess. If you take the lancet and put it in the almond, hold it tight above as much as you can; and do not take anything from the cloths with it, then put the tool back on, so that this is its shape, which seems like a force. Nevertheless, the tips are curved, one towards the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of hard iron or steel: 
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, take the forceps, which has this shape: 
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And it should be sharp on one side and blunt on the other. When you have grasped one of the almonds, grasp the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot water that is both hot and easy to swallow, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with hot water in which the cores of pomegranates have been cooked or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood has stopped; then treat it until it heals; and if at any time other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two almonds, cut them just as you cut the two almonds. 
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was born inside her throat, to be known as an abscess of small sense; and she had nearly closed the whole throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passage which was stopped up, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained thus for one or two days. 
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had forced put two reins through the two holes where it was born.  
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then and put in one oncine, then I drew it out forcefully, and drew out a large portion of pus; then I redid the other hole where it was born, and opened the mouth and pressed the tongue; afterward, I put the oncine into this abscess, and emptied part of it, and only a little blood came out; and thus the passage of the woman's throat was unstopped, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and I did not cease to cut away at this abscess for a long time; and the abscess would grow again, and fill the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I lanced it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it remained without growing; and I departed from these parts, and only God knows what happened to her afterward. 
de l’uve	of the eye 
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the rheum descends to the eye and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below, large, and round, it is called "eye". 
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the boil has softened and it is subtle, then it is fitting that you cut it; and the one that is round, gathered together, and not long; and it is blood-colored or yellowish or black, then it is fitting that you make an incision into it. 
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient. 
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is fitting therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue against the instrument which we have previously mentioned; then insert the lancet into the eye, draw it beneath, and cut with one or two of the instruments that I have mentioned for the incision of the two almonds. 
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut away more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut away more, it grieves the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and heal it until it is healed. 
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears being cut, it is necessary that you use something to cauterize their sense of fear. 
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp and acute.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts their head in your lap, and then presses their tongue to the instrument that we have described in the chapter on cautery, and closes with sharp hot coals, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in applying the point of this instrument, which has this shape: 
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place on the head a hair where one puts the medicine, such as the hairs of a spoon, and put the instrument on all the medicine onto the eye; and let the patient lie on his side so that the saliva and mucus runs from his mouth into the medicine, so that it does not go down the throat, and the bleating; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it on the eye, for the quantity of half an hour, until you see it shrink and the bites of the medicine are appeased; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument on all the cotton into the cane above it, until the cotton is heated on the eye; and do this often, until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and cut afterwards in four days or five. And if you need to restart the cautery from the medicine, if you restart it, and after the cautery wipe it around the eye with cotton soaked in butter, and cleanse what is around it from the medicine; and let it be washed with cold water, and treated with gargles until it is healed. 
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calament and wormwood and oregano and rue and chamomile and lavender and similar herbs, and assemble them all or some of them in a pot, and put it on the fire and boil it; and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and stick the instrument in the pot according to this manner: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or iron, and stick one of the ends into the mouth of the sick person as long as the vapor rises to the eye through the tube, until the eye is mortified; then start again often, until the eye dries up, and make sure you do not do this at the beginning of the arrival of the hot abscess, for many things happen; and do not do this except at the decline of the hot abscess. 
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put inside the head a crust of egg, so that the mouth of the patient does not become too hot; for the crust of egg does not make the vapor weigh down the mouth, and it is a good cure together with salvation. 
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or fishbone, or any thing, gets stuck in the throat. So it is necessary that you draw out what you can see and press the tongue against the sun with the whole instrument so that you see the thing move; and what you cannot see, and which is lodged in the throat, then you must make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the thing will be drawn out by vomiting. Or if the patient has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a piece of stale bread, and tie a thread to the sponge and then swallow it. And when it comes to the place, it will come loose, and then draw it out forcefully. And if it does not come out because of what we have said, then take an instrument for plumbing according to this form: 
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head lifted up high; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all the air go out, or push any bone inside; and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument in, because he knows where the thing is airy; if it goes down, or he pulls it back forcefully with the whole instrument equally, until it is firm. 
de la sansue de la gorge	from the bottom of the throat 
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes medicine is sufficient for the bottom, as I have said in the division, by the treatment of medicines; and when that does not profit, then look into the patient's throat toward the sun, while you press his tongue with the instrument which I have described to you. 
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the bottom, draw it out with all a small hook, or with fine forceps which are suitable for that. 
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that doesn't work, take a hollow cane and insert it into the patient's throat, then insert the hot end of an iron into the cane and do this often. 
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And keep the patient thirsty all day. 
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth and pour it in, making him swallow and move his hand often; and as soon as he feels the water, he will disgorge. 
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if he doesn't disgorge as we have said, fumigate the patient with asafetida, using the instrument I have described for the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, because it will come loose without delay. 
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	The method of fumigation is as follows: you take a pot with live coals and cover it with a cloth pierced in the middle, inserting the head of the instrument into this hole. Then pour in your fumigation, and have the patient put the end of the cane in his mouth, closing his mouth so that no smoke escapes, but reaches his throat; his throat will now loosen, and if he doesn't disgorge, repeat the fumigation many times. Allow the patient to be thirsty, and give him salty and other things to eat, and do not let him drink any water; then it will be necessary for it to come loose through this method.  
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the sinus, it is, when one can see it, like tongs curved for entry into the throat; and it has the resemblance of a bird's beak, and it has the roughness of a file, so that what it takes hold of, it cannot let go; and see here its form: 
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses 
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what memory brings here one after another in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and size; and it is in two ways, one of which is in its own appearance, and from what moisture it holds. 
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is by the places where they are on the body.  
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses on the head are different from those on the buttocks, and abscesses in fleshy areas are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.  
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if to abscesses one must not pierce, as long as the belly is dead according to its fulfillment; and if there are such that it befits to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their fulfillment, such as abscesses which are near joints. 
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves it as long as it is ripe inside, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which is a cause of contraction in that limb. 
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is near the principal limb, and if you delay perforation until it is dead, it will harm the principal limb; or if it is near the fundament, pierce it even when it is dead; and it does not behoove you to pierce an unripe abscess without complete digestion, except that which is near the fundament, so that it may rot perfectly and be elongated within, and a fistula may form; and it cannot heal in a long time. 
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the perforation of the abscess which is death according to accomplishment, and it is when the pain is eased, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and from the softening and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation at a higher location than the abscess, and where it appears to move; and let the perforation be the length of the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all their equals where there is no weeping. 
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that weep, according to the member.  
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in fleshy location, it is worth moving that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. 
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before this, the venom of it will spread throughout the body and be full of much filth; and by chance the lips and its depths harden. 
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there are any abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what its members need. 
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you administer small abscesses, small openings; and in large abscesses, large openings, and many incisions according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cover the heart, and to sew it up; when it has become as soft as a cloth, and is dead, then it is necessary to do as one does with buboes: and if there are such that are split into three angles, and if there are such that are sewn up like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of the angers; and if there are such where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar sutures. 
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, such as a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it thoroughly; and it is necessary when the abscess is large and has collected a great deal of pus, and you pierce it, if you do not draw out all the pus at that time, but draw out some part; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out anything remaining; do this many times, gradually, until all the pus comes out; likewise if the patient is weak, or a woman carrying, or small children, or old men decrepit. 
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirits jump sometimes with the release of pus, and by chance the patient dies, and you do not blame yourself. 
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, if wipe the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a full incision, put on bandages of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, it is necessary that you put in each one a bandage so that they come against each other; and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and have sewn around it, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or tow of linen without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then unbind it, and cure it with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, apply cold, fresh water and moisten the cloth, and place it on the bleeding area many times. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, apply a dressing and treatment, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is cold weather and the wound or abscess is very sensitive, then you should put on bandages and cloths moistened in warm wine and oil; and if it is summer and the wound is fleshy, then you should put on cloths moistened in water and oil, or wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then untie the abscess and wipe it and treat it as necessary, until it is healed. 
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be universally known in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and see here the chapter.  
des soros	of  sores 
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the heat of the head comes small abscesses, and are manners of us that are in webs, as the joiner of a spindle, and many there are of likenesses. 
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some of fat and such where there is moisture as well as pus; and if there are such that are hard and piercing at the waist, and there is no doubt whether the artery does contrary. 
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of the loin are such that you prove with all the instrument which is called "introducer," from which the form comes here after, what it contains.  
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, so let it pass through by a long way. 
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, so scrape without leaving any skin that contains the moisture, for it returns immediately when you leave anything; then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in vinegar and salt, and apply the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those which remain from the night. 
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not stay at night; then heal the wound with ointment as is suitable, until it is healed. 
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds onto thick pus, so do the cautery according to this form for a long time; and put your ointments, and flay it from all sides, and put all your treatment of drawing out the pus where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, do what I have told you afterward. 
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do this for an abscess if it is hard, and in the thigh and in the belly as I have told you. 
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on a hard abscess and moisture is lighter, because they are less prone to bleeding.  
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses have no moisture, and of those it was I who cut the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not break it; and if anyone had done anything to it, they would have made as much of a wound as with a stone. 
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	For other abscesses coming on the head, like those that come on children's heads and at the roots of ears, the opening should always be in the lowest place so that the pus can come out; and treat them as necessary.  
des scrophules	of scrofula 
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come elsewhere in the body, and are very painful, and are joined together. 
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its rib, just as the knot and the abscess on the head, as we have said; and there are many resemblances of these scrofula. 
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are some that are so malignant they do not want to obey health. 
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Therefore, in the one that you see with a good disposition to touch, and it resembles the color of the body, and moves from every part and is not inflamed at the nerves of the neck nor the artery nor the conduit, and it is not deep; then it befits that you cut it above, and scarify it from every side, and extend the two lips of the core to the incisions, if you need them, as we have said in the abscesses of the head; and treat it little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and let the scalpel be neither sharp nor trenchant, so that the hands do not slip, and do not go too far ahead, lest you cut what you should not. 
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put vitriol powder in the wound, or some powders that staunch blood, and extract the wound; and leave it until the abscess is appeased, and the wound softens, and begins to rot. 
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stanched, return to your work, until you complete it; then with your index finger see if there remain any small scrofulas, and cut them out and clean them. 
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrophula, it is not fitting that you cut that scrophula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall off by itself, without harm; then apply the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and then dress it. 
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you have removed all the scrofula, it is fitting that you bring together the two edges of the wound, and sew them now, since there remains no excess due to the size of the scrofula. 
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	It is fitting that you know how to cut out the root of it, and draw pus, and sew it as we have said. 
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofula that have excess, pierce them where it appears dead; and pierce it as the one previously mentioned, in a dependent manner, then apply tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, apply a healing ointment that promotes flesh, until it is healed. 
de squinance	of squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their words. 
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have squinting, it is necessary that the fissure of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be drawn back; and one should not help with this, because all the veins and the lung of the patient are for those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in the two almonds. 
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the lung, it is necessary to raise the epiglottis to avoid the destruction which comes from strangulation. 
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below three circles or four a small cut across, between the two circles or by the quantity of the cut of the pharynx, not in the cartilage; and those are convenient for the section of the epiglottis that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from being near. 
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it is fitting that he extends the skin of the throat to the entire width, then splits the chest until it reaches the trachea; and avoid blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the syfac, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the trachea which escapes through the place that is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a time. 
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which we doubt strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the chest, and sew it all alone without touching the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote the growth of flesh, until it is healed. 
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is entirely torn open, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the lack of breath indicates it. 
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cover the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and they breathe through the wound, and thus are saved from death; and for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. Then they commanded to sew up the wound and cleanse it, as long as it was cleansed; and I will tell you what I saw. 
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a young woman take a knife and stick it in her throat, cutting part of the channels of the windpipe; and I was called to cleanse it, and I found her as if dead. 
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found the blood that had issued from it, and although she had not covered her throat or any conduit but the throat, and the veins were severed by the wound. 
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound and treated it until it was healed; and nothing further happened to the young woman except that her voice became hoarse, and she returned afterward to her normal state; therefore I say that you should have no fear in cutting the epiglottis. 
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat 
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat" and is a large abscess of a yellowish color, and it is very common in women; and there are two kinds according to nature and accident, or natural which has no cause. 
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental kind is according to two manners, of which one resembles fatty tissue, and the other manner resembles an abscess that comes from us of the artery; and there is danger, and it does not behoove to work with fire except in the one that is small, and you should try and search at all the openings: if you find it as soft as new fat and it cannot be moved at any vein, then cut it, as one cuts nodes, and treat it throughout its whole course; if there are any remaining parts, enclose them well and soon, and treat it as is fitting until it is perfectly healed. 
des nous	of us 
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways there are to us, of which I will say all the resemblances; and now it behoves me to say all the difference which is between us and issue. 
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is heat and fever lasting until the boiling over has passed, and putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat subside. 
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With a boil there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins as a pea, and becomes large; and they are according to two resemblances, either fatty or moist, and much in color are as I have said in the division. 
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It behoves, when you come to the treatment of a boil, that you probe and inquire first with all the instrument which is called “introducer,” according to what its shape will be or chapter which comes after. 
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way of inquiring into abscesses of us is that you take or the moister place that you find in the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess; then withdraw the instrument, and take care in this lest it jump out. 
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moist humor runs out, whatever color it has, do as I have said for the other abscesses; and if after the instrument no moisture comes out, know that it is fatty, then make an incision in a cross shape and grasp it with pincers, and lightly scrape it on each side and guard the area where it lies so that you draw it clean with a new cloth; and if you cannot draw it clean, draw it off piece by piece so that nothing remains. 
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it remains there for nothing, the nose returns many times; and if it remains one spot, and it does not grieve you, apply the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, and remove the wound, and put soothing things on a hot abscess, and cure it with other cures until it is healed; and if the nose is large, cut the two lips of the wound, and treat it with those who bring flesh. 
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beats against you or another hastens you, apply the place of crushed vitriol, and leave it there for two or three days, until the wound dries up and stops the boiling of blood; then return to cover what remained in the wound. 
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of inserting instruments, and they are of three manners: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret," and one which is called "breb," and there are three manners: large, medium, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistulas; and they are also like needles with which one sews charms, and are made of citrine iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are worth more, and are better tested for black lead to encircle the curves of fistulas; and they are of three manners: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the holes.  
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of forceps are of many resemblances, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are forceps that have two curvatures in three ways also; and there are forceps that have three curvatures, and are also of three ways; and there are forceps that have two curvatures, and forceps of a single curvature only, and are of three ways; and all this is necessary in their place. 
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The chief of these with which one works are cutting, and of these there are some that do not cut more than from one side, with which one scrapes the skin, so that one does not cut the vein nor the nerve; and of these introducers are the alemeles fitted in handles, so that the patient does not perceive them at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one does not use them more than in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument resembling a fistulous scraper, according to this form, with which one cauterizes blood. 
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and place it at some time where there are veins and arteries, and never return according to this great form: 
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so much so that they resemble women's breasts; and they remain unsightly and swollen, and those who wish to cure them should follow this form from line .b. to .g.: 
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medicine containing charcoal, then bring together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed; and if the breast hangs down and is softened by its size as it happens in women, then make two cuts on it above, with two similar incisions; so that one holds onto the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.; then scrape the skin that is between the two edges, remove the fat, and administer what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made because the patient does not want to rest, or because of the discharge of blood, it is necessary that you fill the wound with moistened cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it shrinks back the remnant and the fat, then treat it until it is healed.  
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits 
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come below the armpits are types of hard scrofula where there are ribs, and some of them contain moisture. 
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore those which contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line .b. up to the line .g.: 
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.
