And when all the pus which is in the abscess is emptied, apply the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and treat it with ointment suitable for this until it is healed. 
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of a similar nature to scrofula, then cut it as we have said in cutting scrofula, and if the wound fills with pus, then apply a cautery as we have said before. 
de la routure de l’artere	of the breaking of the artery 
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is broken and the skin above is sewn together, many times abscesses form, and the same thing happens with a swollen vein and an abscess; and if the one who knows recognizes it as for the artery, the abscess is long and thin; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel a pull; and when it is for the vein, it is round and appears further out; and it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is below the armpits and at the angles or neck and in many other places, and it is very large.  
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary to remove the iron cure and whoever is in charge must also remove it, and in the one who has swelling of the artery going through the skin for a long distance; then operate with the incisions as needed, and beautifully separate the artery from the tissues, until it is uncovered; then put an awl underneath it and make it pierce through to the other side, and extract the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in extracting the two arteries that are in the temples; then point the place between the two ties with a speculum so that the pus that is there comes out, and the abscess is delivered; then apply a cure that draws pus, until the ties break; then cure it with an ointment suitable for this, until it is healed; and if the abscess is due to the size of the vein, it is necessary that you hold in your hand what you can grasp from the abscess all the way to the skin, then put the awl underneath the place that you are holding in your hand and make it pierce through and have a double thread so that you draw it from the other side; then tie the abscess as I told you, or tie one of the two ends with two threads; and if you doubt that the threads will come out, put another awl all the way around the threads under the entire abscess at the incision of the first awl and extract the threads in four places; then cut the abscess so that the excess comes out, then cut the excess from the heart and leave what is tied; then put a softened cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then apply cures of bandages and ointments until it is healed.   
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of nerves 
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses come to the nerves when they are injured, or by too much work, and similar things. 
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	This happens most often in the shoulders and arms and in all their joints, and it is a painful abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in several positions without pain; and when it is removed, it causes the patient pain, and it is not completely in the body, but below the heart; and it moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor down nor up, and that which is in the joints should not be cauterized with iron: for fear it would cause contraction; and that which is on the head or forehead, cut the skin with a scalpel. 
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, take it with forceps and cauterize it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it from a bandage, and flay it, then the bone surgeon sews up the wound and dresses it until it is healed. 
des grosses boces pendans	large boils hanging 
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the belly and nowhere else a swelling, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and the root is subtle, and the head large; and there are some small and some very large ones; and I saw a man who had two in his belly which were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a small root, and were easily cut open, and there constantly ran moisture. 
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them open and found that one weighed eighteen ounces, and the other six ounces and a third, and the work in the incision is such that if you see the patient is moist, and the color of the joint is white and wet and has a subtle root; then cut it at the spatula wide, and have the fire cautery present. 
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the waist there often come excessive blood flows, and if it does not stop by itself, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision with iron, then take a thread of flax well made, and tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then release it, and do not cease to tighten the flax thread until it catches the artery, and flows through it without effort; and if the roots are large, fear to catch itself because of the belly, but you can well catch half, then cauterize so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and be careful not to catch the tendon which is of a dark color and poor sense and milky appearance. 
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an ulcerated abscess, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers afterwards. 
quant li boude ist fuer	When the bone is strong 
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the bone comes from cautery of wound or cleavage of sinew, and is on the belly and in one of the bowels, as it happens in other fractures, or from blood that cuts from veins or arteries according to what is in front, or from windiness; and if it is from the fracture of the sinew and by the issue of the bowel, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and appears with diverse issue. 
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it at its sides, it rebounds and then returns, and by chance if it is squeezed, it swells greatly at the entrance of the bath and due to hard work. 
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is from moisture, it is a light thing, and appears well when you press it with your hand, and it does not constrain at all; and if it is from blood, then it appears by these signs the abscesses are large and hard, and are fixed according to a quantity; and if it is from windiness, then it is soft to the touch, and the operations are such that you look to see if the appearance is from the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.  
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is fitting that you leave the treatment. 
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For he has doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein. 
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the bowel, it is fitting that you instruct the patient to hold his bowels, and be stretched out straight, then sign around all the belly with your finger; then command him to grasp often between your hands, then go around the place that you have signed at all the span of a thumb, then stretch the half of the abscess above at all the great hook; then tie it around with strong thread, or a cord of strong silk firmly, and let the knot be double tied; then work the half of the abscess stretched out upon the tie, and put your index finger, and seek the intestine; if you find it caught by the tie, untie it, and push the intestine out from the belly's depth; and if you find the bowel, take it at the hook, and cut off the superfluity; and if the artery works against you, or the vein, go slowly around, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads in them, and put the two needles around what you have made in a cross shape that you make pierce; then strain the abscess in four places upon the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place so that it may rot, and fall off the dead flesh by itself; or you cut it off when it is thin and rotten, then cure the place as it is fitting, and finish the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place as it is fitting, and sew up the place.  
dou chancre	where a sore 
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the resemblances of a sore, and how one should work by medicines, and how one should avoid the cure of iron; and we say that a sore spreads in the flesh, and great caution is needed in its treatment, and they said the ancients that when a sore is in a place where it can be shaved like a sore which is on the breasts, and on the thigh, and in similar places, and one should remove it all when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, it does not suit you to approach it, for I have never been able to heal any, nor has anyone ever healed one before me. 
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed as we have said, is that you purge the patient several times with black bile; then make him fast if he has manifest repletion, then put the patient in a good place to do the work; then shave your ointments or sore, and the hair from all sides, and remove the bone from all sides without leaving anything; and let the blood run freely, and squeeze the area well with your hand or something else; if the flow of blood hinders you from the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the blood is stopped; then treat it with another treatment until it is healed. 
de ydropisie	Of dropsy 
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already said in the division the resemblances of dropsy, and in what manner the gathering of water is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the cure which is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: if it is split only; and one should not touch iron in these two resemblances: that is to say, tympanites and hypoarche, for it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicate this resemblance of dropsy which is called “split” with medicines, and the cure does not profit, see if the sick person is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as cough and loosening of the belly and similar things; if not, do not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the sick person is of strong constitution, and he has no other illness besides dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must proceed thus: lay the sick person straight on your hands, and have the assistants press the belly at the end by pushing the water to the lowest part below the breast, then take the thorny spatulate according to this form: 
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be sharp on two sides. 
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let it be pointed and in no way so inserted that it can reach the intestines when put in, and cannot pierce; then see if the dropsy is directed towards the intestines: if so, you must cleave within from the belly three finger-widths below on the left side; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, let your incision be on the left of the belly three finger-widths; and if it is for the spleen, let it be on the right, and it is not necessary that the patient lie upon the incision so that superfluities do not run into that weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument and push it in, and lift your hand to all the spatula between the skin and the facia as much as when scraping a nail thickness; then pierce the facia until the spatula comes to the eighth place, which is the place of the sharp part, then draw back, and push this instrument from which it has this form: 
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a delicate silver cane, and is made of iron or light artichoke, and has a small hole at the bottom; and on one side are three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the head is cut like a pen, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes use to cut a pen.  
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the alemele, so that when the instrument comes to the point, it now descends onto the instrument; empty therefore half or a third part, for if you empty more than is necessary at that time, the patient may die by chance due to the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he may become paralyzed, or he may approach death; but in emptying according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's virtue signify, and his pulse; then treat the instrument and hold the point, and it is now held for the heart which pierces the hole that is on the syfac, of which I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner; then restart the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering, and treat the point with a small quantity; do this every day, and be careful not to follow as long as there is more than a drop of blood. 
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the patient, and leave a lot of moisture in them, then the cure is burial or hot sand, and much sweating or bathing in the sun, and they should drink; and the cure with drying medicines until they are healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the moisture as I have said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	of the cutting of the penis 
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who do not have an opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place. 
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary soon, he should pierce all of the penis with a very thin instrument according to this form: 
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put a small plug of lead on the penis, and tie it and leave it there for III days or IIII; and when he wants to urinate, remove the plug and let him urinate, and then put it back; and perhaps it is not necessary, because the urine that comes will not allow it to be closed. 
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He of whom the hole is small, if it is treated with a clove of garlic, as we have said, it will enlarge. 
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the hole in its place are wretched, for none are born who have the hole at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate before they lift their penis upward; and they cannot impregnate because the matter cannot come up to the urethra, and it is a bad disease. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is such that the patient lies often on his back, then extend the head of the penis and cut it as the size of a feather, so that the hole falls in the middle, as it should be; and beware of bleeding which comes many times, and if it happens, let the one who stops blood stop it, and treat the wound until it is healed.  
des pustules de la verge	of the pimples of the penis 
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these boils come to the penis, and they are an ugly appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and benign ones; so it is fitting that you take them with a subtle lancet, and cut and clean them all, then put moistened cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment on them; then treat them with diafinicon ointment until they are healed. 
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the boil is malignant, of a foul color and discharging, it is fitting that you administer cautery to it. 
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it, and if the boil is at the top of the penis, and has part inside the skin and part outside, it is fitting that you remove the boil which is inside first; and when it is sewn up, then treat it outside. 
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, unless the penis is very securely held so that it is not pierced, blackness and corruption come to its penis and its glans; so it is fitting to remove all that is black and corrupt, then bind an ointment plaster of honey and flour made from pomegranate rind and vinegar on top, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, apply the lunar cautery in this form: 
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauteries help in two ways together: that is to say, in the bleeding, and in the corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you draw or conduct from the penis a cane of plumb, and make the patient urinate among it; and when the hairs are burned at the head of the penis which occurs in those who have not been circumcised, or there is a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you cauterize it with a sharp instrument, so that the ligatures are untied, and the head of the penis is delivered from all sides; and if this is a difficult thing to do, it is necessary that you cauterize it with a scalpel in several places at the head of the penis and on the skin; then gently separate them between them, and put a fine linen cloth softened in cold water, so that it does not burn immediately. 
de la circoncision	Of circumcision 
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a continuous operation like other wounds; nevertheless, when we undertake this work of our own volition, and especially on children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the lightest for safety. 
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience. 
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I want the greater part of masters and saints who performed circumcisions around the eighth day, and with force, and with a single lancet; for it would cut the heart because there are two layers, and by chance if one cuts on top and leaves the bottom one. 
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Therefore it is necessary to cut again, and the pain is doubled, and with healing which is on the eighth day the tip of the member is not guaranteed; and with healing of the foreskin, the iron may escape by chance, and ruin the work, and many times are born so that they do not need healing and I want it. 
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the modification which is made to all the length of thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut exactly as well above as below. 
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, it cuts equally in I all the while you hold it; but let the thread be well twisted around the leather; and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only making him tie the thread around the penis just so, and then let him rejoice in all the ways he can; then let him hold it between his hands straight up, and put the forces between your hands or below your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the penis and blow on it, and draw it upward until the head of the penis is in; then clean it well of the filth that has gathered there, then tie the marked place with a double thread, then tie it below I the other tie; and hold it with II fingers at the pouch and index finger, and cut between the II ties, then quickly lift the heart above and draw the head of the penis; then let the blood run drop by drop, for this is the best thing to do; and put powder on top, and on top of the powder a cloth glued with half an egg yolk cooked and tempered with rose water, mixed with good fresh oil of roses, and leave it on until the next day, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.  
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces for purification is this: the two edges must be held and sharp, and the edges must also be as large as the handle equally. 
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of purification is when the core escapes inside at the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your fingernail, so that the pus forms an abscess; and the cup equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then hold it with forceps, and then cut. 
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pass three days, and that which is below the rod is swollen, then leave it until the abscess under the foreskin is appeased, and lightly scrape it; if you can cut, then do so, and beware of the part of the rod, for it will not harm anything. 
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore treat the place of things within the wound with powder, as we have said in our treatise on powders, and if you cut out the core excessively, and it goes above, it will not harm; therefore treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.  
dou retenement de l’urine	For retention of urine 
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is from obstruction of stone, or congealed blood, or bowel, or fat, or similar things that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see the retention is due to a stone which is at the neck of the bladder, it is fitting that the patient be bent on his knees; and his feet be put on his back, and extend his belly on the part above the back, and restrain the patient from moving as much as he can; and then the neck of the bladder is constrained to the expression of the stone above, so the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, it is fitting that you administer extraction with an instrument called a "syringe", of which this is the form: and it shall be made of fine silver light and curved, like the feather of a bird; and the tube shall be one and a half palms long, and fine at the head. 
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of removing urine is that you take a double thread and tie to its end a bit of wool or cotton, and insert the end of the thread into the syringe; and cut off the excess of the wool and insert it up to the end of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and yolk of egg, and make the patient sit on a seat, and anoint his bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water; then gently put the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis over toward the buttock; then insert the syringe forward up to the bladder, and let the patient feel it go up to the empty space, and this is not done according to this order unless he who guides it where it goes is crooked; then pull the thread at all ends bit by bit, and the urine follows the wool, then remove it, and make the urine flow; and repeat the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved. 
des maladies de la vessie	of the illnesses of the bladder 
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scaldings or blood come into the bladder, or putrefaction is gathered there, and you see sharp waters and medicines distilling, then make with all the instrument which is called a "clepsedre," and it is of this form:  
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed and has three holes: two on one side and one on the other, as you see; and the leather sheath through which the medicine flows so that it stops up the penis well without addition, so that one can draw out the moisture and push in when necessary; and when you see your medicines flowing into the bladder, put the head of the catheter into the moisture, and draw with the string that is inside; if you draw the moisture into the catheter, then push the string firmly back in; then the moisture will enter inside and come to the bladder right away so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of a subtle clyster with which one clysters the bladder: this is it. 
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	It is of silver or of artichoke and the head is higher; and below at the breast where the linen sheet; then take a sheep's bladder and put in it the moisture which you see to make the bladder swell, then tie it between the two breasts with a good strong thread, and heat that moisture over the fire; then insert the head of the enema into the penis, and hold your hand on the bladder so all the moisture arrives, until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle out of it, and pierce it roundly around; then insert a strong thread through these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a dish, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it into the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, to press with your hand so that the moisture comes. 
de la piere	of the stone 
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the manners of stone and its extraction with medicines; and we have said the difference between a stone lodged in the reins and all the signs, and in what kind of stone one must work by incision; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly. 
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone lodged in the bladder happens more often to children, and its sign is that sharp urine comes from the bladder seeming like sharp water in its subtlety; and it appears bloody, and makes the patient's penis sore, and he can urinate many times, and then becomes stiff; and many of these urinations are cloudy; and the healing is lighter for children until they are four years old, and it is a great grief for older people, and it is moderate for those who are between youth and old age; and it is easier to cure those who have large stones than those who have small ones.  
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient by enema, to draw out all the phlegm which is in the intestines. 
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders the seeking of the stone. 
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and pull and move them downwards so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes comes out from there; then make him sit between your hands evenly, with his hands below his thighs so that the bladder is entirely sloping downwards; then search for and touch it within. If you feel the stone in the space, hurry now to cut upon the stone. 
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if you do not feel it at all upon touching, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is feverish, or your middle finger, if the patient is young and healthy; and insert it into their foundation, and search for the stone, and when you sense it with your finger, grasp it at the neck of the bladder; then press upon your finger, and guide it out to where you see that you can cut. 
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend the testicles upward with his right hand, and with his left hand remove the skin that is under the testicles in the part where the incision is made; then he inserts the speculum cutting, of which this is the form: 
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And enter between what is between the testicles and the fundament, not in the middle but on the side of the left buttock; and let it be straight upon the stone, and your two hands should be right there or at the fundament, and let the incision be made so that it is wide outside, and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; by chance press with the hand that is at the fundament, so that it jumps out without effort; and know that there are some stones which have angles, and edges: if it is grated it is easy to remove; and if there is a part underneath, resembling a gland, and round, from which the passage is easy. 
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	Where there are angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, you must pull it out with tongs which are like a file at the head, to draw out the stone so that it does not escape; or you put under it a subtle instrument curved at the head; and if you cannot insert it this way, enlarge the hole of the opening, and if the sinews cut, extract them with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, put the largest first at the neck of the bladder, then draw up, then pull hard, and the small ones afterwards if there are several. 
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it must be sewn, and a larger wound made. 
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes out immediately because the veins cannot be sutured; but nevertheless you must try to draw it out, or to break it up with tongs, as much as you can draw it out in pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloes and dragon's blood, and extract it, and put a cloth softened in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water on top, to soothe the hot abscess; then put the patient back on his bed, and do not untie the bandage until the third day. 
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you unbind it, if it rises very well in the place of oil and water, then cure it with ointment diaphyticon and ointment basilicon, until it is healed. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses come to the wound and corrosions, and congealments of blood in the bladder, and it is retained by this urine, which is known in part manner without jumping with the urine: put then your fist into the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and rot it; then lift the wound with water and oil and salt, and help it in all the ways that you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that every hour that you cure it, that you tie his two thighs together, and assemble the medicines on the place. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is where the conduit of the penis leads, and stuck in, and the urine cannot come out; if you cure it as I have said before, that you cut it many times, there is an excuse for the cutting by this cure. 
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already seen this happen like this. 
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take a piece of iron according to this shape and fix it at three angles in a fire: 
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then insert the drill into the shaft gently, until it reaches the stone; and turn the drill in your hand on the stone bit by bit, until you can pierce the stone through to the other side; urine will come out soon, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the shaft. 
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it breaks soon and comes out with the urine, the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this for anything that prevents it, tie one thread below the stone and the other above, then make a cut on the shaft near the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women 
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that stone is lodged in women, and if it ever happens, so is the cure grievous, and it is forbidden for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows well how to expose herself to the mirror, even when she is chaste. 
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a woman who knows well this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is deeper embedded than the stone of a man, for which it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear. And if these necessities arise, it is fitting that you take a midwife who knows well, and at pains one finds her, and if you do not find her, no less let a chaste mirror subtly; and present her with a good wise woman experienced in the life of women, or a woman who knows some part of the art, and command her to do what you command her from the inquiry of the stone; and look very well whether the woman is a virgin: then it behoves you to push your finger or thumb and seek the stone; and if she finds it, constrain it under her finger, and recommend that she put her finger or hand on the ill woman, and wants and presses her left hand on the bladder below.  
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it is necessary that she moves it little by little from the entrance of the bladder down below, as far as it comes to the root of the thigh; then grasp onto the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the hipbone, where it is most easily moved, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her finger above the stone or below, and let the incision be made at first small; then put the knife into the incision, if you feel the stone press hard on the wound so that the stone can come out as forcefully as possible, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those that have horns. 
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the resemblances to know the outcome. 
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood comes, put powdered vitriol on it and hold it for an hour until the blood is stopped; then return to your work, as long as the stone is out, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of a stone from men to help you in your work; and if the blood comes, and it is from an artery that has been cut, put powder on the spot and bind it with tents and bandages, and do not start again, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, lest the patient should die by chance; then treat the wound. 
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the pain subsides, you may return to your work, as long as the stone is strong. 
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia 
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	A watery hernia is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white yolk, which is below the heart of the testicles, that contains the egg; and it is called "yolk," and it is sometimes properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is another egg; and it is the skin of the testicle between the white yolk that we have said; and this does not have a pocket. 
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia is from weakness that comes to the testicles, and it is spread matter. 
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: either it is a declining color to jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more; and these are the signs to know this assembly, for if it is white yolk as we have said, it is a reabsorbed abscess, the pocket is long as the shape of an egg, and does not open the testicles, because it has moisture all around.  
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in the very fabric, then the abscess returns with a portion of the egg, and for this reason one thinks that it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white membrane, then he feels it well; therefore when you see to know the color of the moisture, test all the inserter, the form of which is mentioned before. 
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this then which comes after the inserter, judge what is inside. 
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we heal it with iron, it is fitting that the patient be cleansed according to our power and the repletion of his body; then place him on his back, on a thing a foot high, and put many cloths under him; then sit on his left, and command the assistant to sit on his right, and extend the instrument to one of the two ribs near the heart of the testicles; then take the scalpel, sharp and clean, and cut the skin of the testicles along its length down to the penis, and let your incision be straight by dividing the skin of the testicles up to the white membrane, and delicately scrape it according to your power; then pierce the membrane full of liquid with a large opening, extract all the liquid, and then apply your ointments, and stretch the membrane upwards; and do not touch the heart of the testicles, but only the membrane; cut all or in pieces immediately its side subtly, so that if you do not cut it wisely, the liquid will return; and if the egg jumps out during your work, put it back in its place when you have completed the work on the membrane; then join the two edges of the heart of the testicles with a suture, then heal it as other wounds, until it is healed. 
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspensory, doubting the flow of blood; then cut the cord at all the suspensory parts, and extract the egg, and cure it as we have said. 
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the sharp point is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; then cut the other part as you have done the first equally, then wipe away the blood, and put into the wound linen moistened in oil of roses; and put another linen moistened in wine and oil on top of the two cords, and put double cloths over them, and bind it all together according to this form: 
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths and fill them with shredded linen according to this appearance and let them be joined by stitching at the throat of the breeches, and let one of the straps take hold on the base up to the back, and the other at the handle side; and the other two chiefs on the two angles, and let all the restraint be assembled in the buckle of the breeches; and it is never treated with this branch of cautery instead of an iron knife, and it is that you take a subtle culinary cautery, and cut the skin of the cords, and it is heated as we have said, so that the white syfac which contains the point is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that syfac at the oncines, and scald it with this subtle hot cautery:  
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cup in all the ways that you can, as long as you scratch everything; and guard that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is safer; and be careful of bleeding, and gentler than the works of cutting; and if anything opposes you, or an abscess bursts or there is bleeding or anything else, then treat what opposes you according to what has been said before. 
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to wait for this work because of its horror, then make a perforation as I tell you, and it is that when you are well certain by the signs that we have said that clear water is there, then make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess below at the entire width of the spatula, and make the perforation as long as the body; and let the hole be wide so that all the pus runs out; then put cotton on the place and bind it, and leave it to drain the remaining pus, then treat it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not let the pus issue into the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a feather or the instrument with which one treats the pus of hydrops, of which the shape is described before, and enlarge the hole of the wound, and know that the pus returns and gathers after six months or thereabouts; and when it is gathered as before, then the patient will pass his days. 
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the thighs 
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the cutting of this branch there are many dangers because of which it seems to me better to leave it; and I will tell you the work and the appearances of the abscess. 
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come on the body, and especially on the thighs; and this is in many cases. 
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to know by superfluous sour and sharp humor which is spread on the thighs, or by percussion; and the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and there is no pain found, and it is a troublesome abscess; and by chance some abscesses are painful and hard, and of a dark red color, and sometimes it comes from a new artery, or swelling of a vein. 
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from a new artery, it is known by the disposition of the hot abscess, when you press it with your fingers; and it is not good that you touch it. 
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of swelling of the vein is known by his disposition to the touch of the two fingers, and one can well make the incision on this resemblance, and on the other carts; and it is that you cut the heart of the onions, then lift the egg up high, and draw a line through the white, and deliver the suspensory from all sides of the egg. 
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already boiled with these carts new, then it is fitting that you draw the egg and cut; and if it is air at the white, or in that which is inside the vessels, then it is fitting that you deliver all of that string, and cut roundly.  
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the cart is or place behind, then it is fitting that you cut all of it, and extract the egg, as we have said. 
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is done, dress the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed. 
de l’aposteme des coions	of abscesses of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a covering resembling a boil, with the softening of the testicles, and the patient groans as he walks; and the treatment of this disease is just as dangerous as the one before it, nevertheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a raised seat, then pull down the scrotum of the testicles below your knees, exposing all the vessels that are near the penis, and hold them with your masters and extend them; then cut with a sharp scalpel in a crosswise direction between the vessels until they are exposed, and then flay from each side as we have said in the extraction of arteries in the temples; then insert a needle threaded with double thread and tie it at the first place where the pus came out, and tie it directly to the other end; then cut it in the middle straight according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupt humors; then treat the wound as others where there is inflammation, so that no vessel bursts that nourishes one of the testicles; for by this there will be no harm, and if all the vessels appear, it is necessary to milk the testicles at all the vessels; so that the testis does not lose its nourishment because of the incision of the vessels, and they dry up and can no longer be helped. 
de la routure dou syfac	of the fracture of the bone 
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The events of this branch occur by the section that comes or goes to the bone, or the extension upon the belly in the part of the angers, for which the intestines descend from that fracture to one of the colons; and this fracture is either of the bone, or of the extension of it, and these two manners come from many causes: either from percussion, or from a leap, or from a blow, or from lifting a heavy thing, and by similar things; and the signs when it is from the extension of the bone, are that it happens little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are equal as far as towards the bottom, for which the bone presses the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the section of the bone, that it brings at the beginning sudden pain, and the abscesses diverse appearing, under the skin nearby, and this is for the exit of the intestines and the body at the outside of the bone. 
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never separate the intestines with the entrails, and it is held there, and makes the patient suffer great pain, even when pressed.
