Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments out of fear, because he should avoid them.  
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the work is such that you command the patient to knead the intestine with his hand inside the wound if he can re-enter; then be careful on his neck between your hands and lift up the thighs; then extend the heart above, and cut all the skin of the testicles from length; then insert the levers of the waist into the incisions according to what you need to open the wound, and let them be such that the bones can come out; then flay the fascia which is under the skin of the testicles until the white fascia hard is uncovered on all sides; then put your index finger in that which follows the testicle, in that which is between the white fascia which is under the skin of the egg and the second fascia, and detach what is behind the egg and between the second fascia; and then move with your right hand inside the heart of the testicles and extend the white fascia upwards towards your left hand and lift the egg toward all the fascia towards the waist; and command the minister to extend the egg upwards and loosen what is after the ligation; and with your fingers, see if there are any intestines entangled or white hard fascia, and if you find anything like that, put it in the belly below; then take a needle where it has I thick thread made of X threads, and insert it into the back part of the fascia which is after the skin of the testicles; then cut the ends which appear from the threads as long as there are IIII threads; then gather them one on top of the other in a cross shape, and tie the fascia, of which we have said that it is under the skin of the testicles with a strong tie of II parts; then wrap the ends of the threads and tie them forming II parts so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter inside, so that no abscess will come in; and put the ligature according to the first ligature long II fingers from it, and after these II ligatures leave the fascia which is under the heart of the testicles the size of a finger; and then all the other according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cut in the part which is under the skin of the testicles as long as the sinew and the bowel, as we have said before; then apply wool soaked in oil and put it on the wounds, and administer the ligature as we have said.  
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the white flesh as we have said, after the incision, for fear of stopping the flow of blood. 
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and leave the ligature until it bleeds by itself; and if it delays in bleeding, apply a compress of hot water, and place on what we have said, until it bleeds; then treat the wound with another remedy, until it is perfectly healed.  
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia 
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I have never seen anyone who dared to make the cure with iron. 
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done as the branch which is together with the vein, in part manner that you tie the vessels, after the incision under lightly below; then cut in half, and treat the abscess from what works, until the vessels bleed; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the joints as we have said and opens the flesh; and no intestine is drawn out from the joint, if any are drawn out it is only a little and it heals every hour. And however if it remains too long in this state, the wound or fistula grows until the intestines are drawn out; and this happens because of the extension of the fistula which is in the joint as we have said, for it is extended then it softens and swells the flesh and opens. And the cure is by cautery as we have previously said; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner: and that is the patient lies often on his back between your hands, then you cut the place of the rupture swollen with a width according to the quantity of three fingers; then you draw out the fistula which is under the skin where the flesh has grown together; then take a hot iron and place it on the visible place of the fistula. And press down hard on the belly, then cauterize the two visible places of the fistula on the head of the iron and cauterize one and the other. Then remove the head of the iron and do not cut the fistula nor stretch any thing else as I have made known to you in the cure for a rupture of the intestines; then cure it by the cure of wounds.  
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, let the patient cleanse and care for the wound until it is healed. 
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The face is constricted, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is weaker in this place, and closer to safety. 
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles 
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin of the testicles is softened in some men, because the cords that are inside are softened, and it is made to be seen; and it is necessary, when one wants to treat it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and cuts the softened skin above the natural skin; then he brings together the two lips at one stitch, and if you see, first sew the superfluity of the softened skin with three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches, and cure as the other wounds, until it is healed, and pull out the thread. 
dou chastrement	Where cautery 
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that cautery is forbidden in our law, and therefore it would please me not to speak of it in this book; but it is necessary for two reasons: one is that the sick person can answer when asked about their cure; and the other is because we often need to cauterize some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and dogs and other beasts. 
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that cautery is done in two ways: either by attraction or by incision. 
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by attraction, we make the beast sit in hot water until its bowels are softened and drooping; then take them in your hand, until they are relaxed and you no longer feel them.  
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the cautery of testicles: It is necessary that you hold the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and cut on each testicle one time, when you have well skinned them; and leave no mark or slight mark which is upon the vessels; and this manner of cautery is better than that which is done by attraction, because in attraction some parts of the testicles may remain, by which the beast desires lust; then treat the wound until it is healed. 
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites 
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodism is according to two manners like men: one if it appears between the two testicles as the form of nature of a woman, or it has hair, and sometimes urinates therein.  
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and they have upon the hip as a penis and two testicles. 
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the cure of the man and the woman is that you cut off the added parts altogether, and cure them like other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine passes through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.  
de la tentigene	Of the tentigene 
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	The tentigene is an added part upon the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have them as large as a hand, and this is the cure. 
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is fitting that you hold the superfluity of the tentorium in your hand or at your fingertips and press lightly; and do not press too hard so that blood does not flow out. Then cure it with another treatment until it is healed. As for another sore that arises at the mouth of the wound, apply it and if it jumps off it is according to the appearance of a cow's udder and because of this, the ancients called it "cow-udder disease". 
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is fitting that you press it, as we have said with the tentorium, and treat it until it is healed. 
de erratique	of wandering  
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic it is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or when the orifice is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental by illness that has come; or by a sore added, or through a subtle or thick vein, and is made hard in the womb, or on the side, or below, or wherever it may be; and it prevents conception, and childbirth, and perhaps having flowers; and the knowledge of this is by looking at the belly. 
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the splinters are close together, whether at your wrists or on the right. 
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a very fine splinter and close to the two lips, hurry and do this: put your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then extend the two lips as far as possible until the fine splinter is removed, and all the splinters are out; then take wool and soak it in oil and place it on the spot. Let the woman remain at home each day so that she cannot sew. 
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the splinter is hard and thick, it is necessary that you cut it with a scalpel resembling a myrtle leaf. 
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the splinter is of oak wood, suspend it to a pincers and cut it off; and have medicines that staunch blood ready, such as alum, dragon's blood, frankincense mixed together with egg white; then apply a wide bandage of linen so that the wound cannot close; and let it remain like this for a long time, applying a tent of dry linen. Then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a carbuncle comes in the flesh, if it is necessary to cover it according to this manner, unless it is an ulcerated abscess. 
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an ulcerated abscess which is in the flesh, one should not touch it with fire. 
des emorroides	Hemorrhoids 
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which without a court usually accustom themselves, and when the hemorrhoids are old they become hard; and as we have said in the division the resemblances to other things and signs, I will say here those which receive cure. 
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and hardness, when they are embedded in the flesh and do not appear to the touch unless cured by iron. 
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those which are at the mouth of the flesh, one can feel, are those which one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then take the uterus with tongs, and grasp it at its roots, then sprinkle powder of medicines that restrain blood, such as alum and dragon's blood and frankincense, and similar things; then place her feet against the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, have her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and gallnuts and similar things, and then take barley flour and mix it with honey and oil, and make an emplaster on her back. 
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops, that is good. 
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, have her cupped on the back and breasts without piercing; then take wool and wet it in plantain juice or hawthorn juice with old wine and apply it to the area. 
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess subsides, treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles rough salt, so you must cover it as I have said for the thelul; then treat it until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the jaw
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come in the jaw, such as chancre and putrid abscess and herpes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other illnesses that I have mentioned in the division. 
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, it is fitting that I speak in this treatise of the hot abscess that comes in the jaw, which is not among those that cause a swelling; and if you wish to know the work of iron, see if this abscess is sharp at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red so that you can see it. 
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hurry to pierce, but let it rest until the pain is eased; and then make the patient sit on a seat, and have two small seats where he can lean, and support himself on his back and bring his feet together behind the leg; and let his thighs be spread, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then turn him towards the right side, and apply the instrument used to open the mouth of the wound, for which the form will follow afterwards; and it is necessary that when you see this instrument applied, you insert the point first in order to know the depth of the wound, so that what enters with the instrument does not go further than it should, and so that it does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the wound with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt him; and it is necessary that he puts the funnel of the instrument on top, and holds the instrument. 
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is opened and it is pressed gently by hand, if it is necessary to cover the head, do so with lint moistened with rose oil or green oil; and place the tent firmly from the edge of the wound to the margin of the swelling, and put over the swelling and on the wrist clean linen moistened in water, whether aquas are cooked.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is healed in the marrow, it is fitting that you beware of cauterizing with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division. 
de l’enfantement	of childbirth 
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is first necessary for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth and its signs: when you see the woman hasten downward, and desire to smell the air, then the child hastens to come forth; then you know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and the issue is below her head, and the afterbirth with it; and when you see these signs, it is fitting to press lightly on her belly so that the child comes forth quickly; for when it descends head first, the afterbirth comes with it, and the marrow is cleansed of its superfluities by good cleansing; and that which comes otherwise does not come naturally. 
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it sometimes comes up on its feet, and the body or the head comes loose, and the hands, or it comes up on its belly, or often, and is converted by chance off its neck, and by other bad figures; so it is necessary for the midwife that she be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures how one must help her. 
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the infant comes up on its head by natural passage, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, then make her sit on a saddle, where women hold her; and prepare oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then put the midwife between her thighs the small spatula of which this is the form: 
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the secondine, and press at her fingernail until the moisture that is within comes out; and hold the woman's belly until the infant descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to cleanse the woman with a mixture of fenugreek and sesame oil; then make her take and sneeze from mustard, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: then extract the infant now.  
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out strong, it is necessary that you reset them lightly little by little; and if they cannot enter, put the woman on a stool, and lift her feet up high; then overturn the stool to the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall during the overturning; and if the hands still cannot enter, and the child is dead, cut the hands with the knife which has been placed there before, and extract the child, and reset it equally. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the delivery of the child on its feet 
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes on its feet, it is necessary to push it up; and then turn it little by little until it is equal; then take it by the feet and extend it little by little. 
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps as far as the thighs, then command her to take it and make her sneeze with restraint; if it jumps strong, God willing. 
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not strong as we have said, turn it little by little until it is according to the natural form. 
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is lighter. 
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come strong as we have said, take musk, oil of cedar, and melted gum, grind all in a mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and apply this ointment, then let her sit in hot water up to below the ribs; and when she is softened below, give her a collar of myrrh and put it underneath, and leave it for an hour; then let her sit on a seat, then make her sneeze and pull out her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, for the infant will now jump. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the delivery of the child onto her knees  
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if it puts its hands on its chest little by little; then be swaddled on its neck, and let its feet hang down, and let it lie down off the bed; and fold its hands little by little, and then take its hands on the belly, and remove the cushions from under it, so that it is exposed downwards; and if the child does not jump, take its feet and move them upwards, then move the belly upwards, then push its hands; and lift the child little by little; and command the woman to hold it as long as the child rises. 
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the delivery of a child who comes forth with one hand hanging out 
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to try to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, make her lie down on the bed, and unbend her legs upwards; then administer the muscilage that I have mentioned; and if she does not deliver, make her sit on a chair, and then try to bring back the hand; and lift the child according to its natural form, and make her sneeze, and command her to hold it as long as the child rises up.  
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the delivery of the child upon its neck, and has spread its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother 
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is fitting that the midwife holds her hand, then turns it little by little, and lifts it lightly; and when it is equalized, she puts on the natural muscle-softening ointment of honey and oil, as we have said, then commands her to move it little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on a seat, and command her to grasp; and make her sneeze. 
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner for all of the afterbirth 
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes forcefully in this manner for all of the afterbirth, grasp the afterbirth at your fingernail, as long as the moisture is drained; and if the infant leans upon its face and upon its neck, grasp it from the shoulder, so that it is not retained, and the infant dies; then push the infant inside, as long as you have put it as it should be, and command the woman to grasp herself several times: then pull gently. 
de l’issue des gemelz	From the issue of twins 
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and never three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, and it often happens. 
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things and do not live if it happens. I know that they should be multiplied, and are delivered by the umbilical cord which divides them, which is tied to the belly; and sometimes they also issue naturally as one under another, as we have said. 
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue badly, then the cure is as we have said, and let the midwife be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what she does; and do so as it is worth moving towards salvation. 
de plusors enfans	of several children 
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or several up to fifteen, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measure of the glorious Sage, and it is fitting that the midwife knows all this, for by chance similar things happen; so do according to what is fitting. 
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child 
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman of a dead child in the womb, as I have said in the division, and no waters come forth, and you are compelled to work with your hands; it is fitting that you know if the woman is of sound constitution, and has no accident or fear of death; it is fitting that the woman be laid on her back, and her thighs inclined downwards, and her legs raised; and the attendant should hold the woman's hand in two parts, or tie her to the bed so that she is not treated for the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils with a mixture of althea and fenugreek and flaxseed; then anoint the midwife's hands with these oils and mixtures; then insert them gently into the womb, then choose the place where she inserts the ointments to be suitable for this, and take care that if the child is delivered, it descends on its head; then insert the ointments into her eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the chin or in the armpit or near the ribs, and if the delivery is on foot, put them at the hip and lower ribs; and it is fitting that she hold the ointment in her right hand, and place the curvature between the two fingers of her left hand, and insert it with all her hand gently, and insert the ointment into any of these places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the ointment: 
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then place it against the other forceps, or a third if you need them, so that the extraction is even; and then stretch them evenly by moving from one side to the other, in order to make it come out, and let the forceps have teeth in order to hold it, as shown here: 
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, anoint the wound with some of its oil, and put it in that part, and pull out the other part; and if none remains, put these forceps higher up and do this until all comes out. 
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes forward in front of the other, and it cannot be brought back due to tightness, it is necessary that you wrap it up in a cloth, until it all comes out; then bind it at the joint of the foot or with a knife, and thus do as for the other hand, and the two feet. 
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of a child is large and it is stuck in the birth canal, or it has a sharp point assembled, then you must put the thorny spatula between your fingers and cut the head and extract the point; or you can grind it with an instrument which is called "almidach", from which the form comes with the instruments or chapters which are after this one; and thus the same if the child has a large natural head; and then draw the bones with tongs, and if the head jumps out and it is extracted by force, it should be split, as long as the moisture that is in the worst part exits; and if it cannot exit, cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, then you must pierce it so that the moisture runs. 
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, the attraction is light, and the straightening at the mouth of the womb is light. 
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is embedded in the belly or breast, it is necessary that you extract it with a cloth wrapped around the hand; and press the belly or breast, until the moisture that is there runs; and if the other members are removed, and the head remains, then put the arm in with the hand covered with marjoram, and draw it to the mouth of the wound; then he puts one or two fingers in and draws further; and if the mouth of the wound is constricted by a hot abscess that has come, then it is not necessary to work at it, but rather administer moist and greasy things; and administer plasters, and ointments that are soft and moistening. 
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the arrow is on its side, and you can put it even, then administer what we have said in the live child; and if one cannot, then draw it out in pieces, and leave nothing of the shaft. 
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if he administers what we have said to abscesses that come in the marsh; and if bleeding occurs, it should be put in sharp restraint, and administer other remedies. 
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb one child had been dead, then conceived another upon that one, and the other was born dead. 
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time an abscess came to her in the buttock, and it swelled so much that it opened, and began with great discharge. 
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to cure it, and I thought long, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and there came out a bone, and after some days another. 
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I wondered greatly, for it is not usual for the belly to have bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought these were bones of a dead child. 
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I probed the wound and found bones there, as long as the woman was in a better state; and I left the woman for a long time like that, and it became a little bit swollen in that place; and I do not remember this chapter except because when masters find something strange they should know how to provide help. 
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the marrow to its place 
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here follows the shape of the press, with which we bind books; and at two turns are the two heads of the two lines. 
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle than the restrictor and should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the wood should be two fingers wide, and the edge of the tree one finger, and a half palm long; and between the two lines are two adjustments of this same wood, which are fixed on one side and the other, half a palm long or a little more; and these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the marrow to open when one turns the two horns.  
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of tongs; and have two jaws with two adjustments, as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; and when you see the vulva open for the whole instrument, make the woman sit on her bed with her feet dangling and her legs open, then insert the two adjustments together into the vulva, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs; then work your hand along the whole instrument as you did with the tongs equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the vulva, until the woman does what she wants. 
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all assembled and are multiplied in their likeness; and when the women have them arranged, the work is so much faster, and higher for men according to their quantity. 
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despair of the instrument until you have prepared it, for its necessity is inexcusable. 
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the placenta is retained at childbirth, you should instruct the woman to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze by force, and remove your hands from her mouth and nose; and if she jumps because of this, it is good. 
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If this does not work, take a pot and make a hole or lid in it, and put herbs in it that can open the mouth of the womb, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia lignea, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked in a pot with water over the fire; then put one end of a reed or tube into the pot and the other end into the mouth of the womb, and hold it there until the vapors enter the womb; then make her sneeze, as we have said. 
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second sinew jumps quickly. 
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and is not strong, command the healer to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or mallow mucilage, and then insert it into the wound and seek the sinew; and when she has found it, grasp it and extend it little by little straight so that the flesh does not tear at the extraction; but gently move it to the right and left, and then pull; it will come and loosen. 
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the flesh is tight and constricted, we have said the cure of sneezing, and fumigation of herbs; and if it is not from all that we have said, be careful that you do not pull in the opposite direction; but it is fitting that he who is at the mouth of the flesh, you bind him to the thigh of the woman, then give an enema of tetrapharmacon ointment; if it will hold and return, and come strong; but nevertheless, when it returns there comes a bad odor to the stomach and head, and hurts the patient.  
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is necessary then suitable fumigations for this: none of the ancients have tried fumigation of cress and dried figs. 
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman to retain flowers and the afterbirth is this: 
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is like in appearance to a cane, and one puts the tip subtle in the nature, and the legs wide on the fire; and let the fumigations be on the coals, and the smoke as long as it is wasted, and begin another. 
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the foundation 
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but rather have a subtle syfac stopped up: so it is necessary then for the midwife to pierce that syfac with her needle, and not pierce it with a sharp spatula, and keep the ligature so that she does not touch it; then put on linen moistened in wine and oil, then cure it with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will stay in place, put or pierce a cane of plumb, and leave it for forty days, and let it be removed when the child wants to go into the room. 
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this dislocation comes from the closing of a wound or an abscess; then it is necessary to treat that closing.  If it is healed, do as we have said about the cane of plumb. 
de la fistule dou fondement	of a fistula in the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come below the fundament are swellings and thickenings that come from beneath the fundament behind, or in the space between the two buttocks, whether there is one fistula or several; and when this swelling is old, it works, and still produces moisture which brings forth white or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are known by those who have them, whether through defecation or flatulence when the patient has a bowel movement, and perhaps by squirting one or more times.  
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that extend to the bladder and to half of the penis; and reach as far as the junction of the thigh and as far as the knee. 
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one recognizes the fistula penetrating at the base and not penetrating; and it is that you place your second finger or thumb at the base and insert a fine needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting. 
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is twisting, then insert a thread of silk or a horsehair until you feel the thread or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and nothing comes out through the hole - neither discharge nor flatulence nor worm as we have said - know that it does not penetrate; if you hesitate to cleanse it. 
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula penetrates as far as the bladder or as far as the urethra, if it spurts urine and cannot be healed by medicine. 
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced as far as the joint of the thigh, then the tendon coming to the place; if there is no tortuosity and the invention of the pain goes around, then it will immediately become better, and medicine or dressing by ointment are of no use; and in these fistulas that persist there is no cure except labor, and vanity of foolish remedies that interfere. 
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not persistent and is not old, there is hope for healing with iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and lifts the legs up to his thighs, and has his thighs inclined towards his belly; then insert a tendon of hemp, or of lead if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tendon comes. 
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the base, it is necessary that you put your two index fingers, if then you feel that the tendon has pierced it; and be uncovered where you feel between your finger the sinew or the flesh, then know that it is persistent; if it does not work at all, it cannot be healed. 
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	We say that one can heal some well, but it happens rarely; and the help that we do is to heat a subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula as it has been said before, and put the whole thing hot in the fistula until it reaches the bottom; and do this two or three times, as long as you know that these bad hairs are burned, which are like a bird’s feather; then cure with softened tents in butter, as long as those hairs are strong, then cure with ointment binding hair and welding. 
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is healed thus, it is well. 
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it cannot be healed otherwise; and if the tent is inside and does not pierce through to the bottom which is at its foundation and there is between your finger and the tent a thick covering of hair or pus, and you see the fistula beyond that which covers the heart; if you cut off from the beginning of the fistula and put it in front of the tent, and then apply the cautery afterwards until it reaches the head of the tent; and the tent will be released and fall away; then burn those bad hairs that look like a bird's feather and do not leave any.  
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if your blood goes away, and it is short between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicine. 
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cauteries assemble two good things: that is to say, the burning of these charred objects, and the stopping of blood and drying of moisture; then the healing of softened tissues smeared with butter or chopped herbs, as long as the wounds begin to boil, and if the wound is burned in the boil; then heal the wound with ointments made of hard-burnt charcoal, and they are dry medicines. 
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes right up to the base of the foundation, and is far from the body, then you should insert your finger or instrument into it and inquire there. 
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tissue, and between them is the cloth or sinew or char, or if it is about to pierce, then there is no other way but a path of faith and hope, through the administration of one of three ways: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it down to the base, or if you can put in tissue and heal it as first; and do not go too far towards the base, lest you cut the ligament that holds the foundation, and the evacuations come forth against your will; then heal it as we have said; by chance it may be healed, or you remove that covering and cleanse it after it has been cut away from the foundation, either by tissue or by another pointed instrument; then cleanse that faulty char which is in the wound as much as you can; then try to restore the wound, and keep the fistula in the part furthest from the foundation: this will be a lighter thing for the patient. 
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And never are fistulas made according to this manner: and it is when you place the tent in the fistula, and it is near or touches the foundation beneath the skin above, then take a tent pierced at its head according to this form: 
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I place the twisted thread in II, and I place the tent on all of the thread in the fistula as far as its head. 
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin of the foundation inside, then extract the thread from that hole, so that you place your finger or foundation; and hold the head of the thread, and join the two ends together, and pull one from the other, and leave it for one or two days; and restrain it no more, as long as the threads catch those strands which are between them and click; then heal the wound until it is closed and clean. 
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, do it in all the ways that you can, if it is not too constricted.  
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not fitting to treat for a placement by itself so perfectly and then cure it as we have said until it is healed. 
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spatulia with spines from which we make a fistula is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other; for this reason we do not cut as we ought not to cut, as you see here. 
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are according to two manners: either they are inside the fundament, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they often bleed, and there is one or several, and they protrude outside the fundament and at the head of the fundament; but those that are outside have little moisture, and still bleed a little or a drop of yellowish liquid or a drop of blood, and have the color of flesh; and the cure for those who have them inside the fundament is to order the patient to strain himself to go to the toilet, as long as the fundament allows him to release, and the threads appear; if you hurry, and it can be grasped with tweezers, or held at your fingernail, then cut it at its roots; and if the lancet cannot hold them because of their moisture, grasp them with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamois leather; and pull them out with your hands, then cut them, and sprinkle some hot powders on them which are in place of cautery; or cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then cure them with other cures until they are healed; and if the fundament cannot be released, give the patient an astringent and harsh enema to wash what is in the fundament so that it can come out freely; when the patient is relieved, and the threads are removed from the fundament, the cure is easy; and it is to grasp them with your fingernail or tweezers, and cut them, then cure them as we have said, until they are healed, and he fears the incision by iron. 
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you administer the suture in this manner: take a twisted thread, and put it into a needle, then draw the thread upwards and make the needle pierce through to the other side, and turn both ends of the thread under the needle, and let it be double; remove the formed thread, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do this for all the others, and leave one to correct the superfluity of blood; then put on the foundation a softened cloth in rose oil or cerate, and place it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave him until they fall off, and when they have fallen, treat them with ointment and other cures, until he is healed. 
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	on the drying of the wound or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is drying of the bowels due to constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is of no use. 
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you scrape the top of it with the point of a scalpel or your fingernail, so as not to let it get moist; then treat it until it is healed as it should be; and if it cannot heal, start the scraping again more strongly than before, until it heals well and is scraped; then treat it until it is healed. 
dou fremit	Where there is trembling.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formication is a small, false appearance against the body, and it goes very much by preference; and one sometimes finds cold, and feels it as if dead from trembling, and it comes throughout the whole body, especially in the hands more than anywhere else. 
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is such that you take a cane from a goose feather or a strong vulture feather and place this cane on top of the trembling, until the circles completely encircle the trembling; then turn your hand around the entire cane until you grasp everything around the trembling, and insert it straight down, and pluck the trembling from its roots. 
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make one of a cane of iron or steel according to this form, and let it be subtle underneath and sharp above. 
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce, but hold it to the pain and press. And if you see, cauterize the flesh, as it is before or in the chapter of cautery. 
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a clyster  
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes a clyster of silver or artichoke, or iron melted or hammered; and sometimes one makes these instruments small and large, according to those to whom they are administered. 
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those then that are administered in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small.  
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of a small and large clyster is wide above, where the belly is tied according to this manner: 
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is a separation where the belly is tied, as you see, and the flesh is pierced within; and it has on one side II holes, and on the other I; and let the belly be where we put medicines from a bladder of a beast or parchment, and be pierced all around with small holes, and have between each hole I space apart, then put into these holes I strong thread of raw silk twisted in X or in a circle, and assemble the belly as it is a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front of a strong thread, then clysterize; and this is the form of a circle: 
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or yolk of egg, or a similar thing, then put it in gently; then the attendant grasps his two hands together, as long as it is all gone, then removes the clyster, and lifts the patient's legs to the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it flow as much as it can; and if he sleeps a whole night, it is of greater help. 
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cauterize it with illness of flux of the belly, and the medicine hastens to go in, then start again until it is healed. 
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the fundament, or abscess, then let the enema be as subtle as for an infant; and this is the form of a subtle enema on which the skin is extracted: 
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments by hand and medicine according to accomplishment. 
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the places or wounds where they are made, and of what they are made. 
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the striking of a stone, and cutting of a sword and knife, or a lance or a gun or an arrow, or similar things; or that they are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the foot, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and begin with the wounds of the head simple, for the remembrance will come in its chapter.
