Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, if you are careful it is from the blow of a stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you slightly doubt a hot abscess: if it heals quickly from the cephalic vein itself if little blood comes from the wound, and let it heal on the contrary side of the injured part; and avoid giving the patient repletion of wine and heavy meats. 
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not want to heal, reduce his food, and let him not drink wine, nor eat meat; and put on the wound, if a hot abscess should come, cotton softened in rose oil alone, or in astringent wine; and if there is no hot abscess, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder, which I will say a little later; and if he has already moved it, put on some ointments until it is healed. 
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like from a sword cut or similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by tents, then sew them together, as I will say about wounds of the belly, from stitching. 
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone and can be indented and does not hold but by a point, then cauterize it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as heads and cooked wheat, as well as poultry, and similar things. 
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rotten skin and it does not reach the bone, then cauterize all the rot thoroughly, and cut away the dead tissue, then treat it; and if it has an artery or vein in the wound, which bleeds without stopping and cannot be staunched by medicine, then tie off the artery; and if you find it dislodged, tie it with thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it. 
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light: and it is that you put this powder which heals as soon as the fire has moved it. 
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is as follows: take frankincense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and powder them subtly, and apply it to the wound, and hold it firmly, until it burns well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it well, and leave it without loosening, unless it swells; for you do not remove the medicine until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one makes this with quicklime alone, when one does not have frankincense or dragon's blood, but let the fire have moved the wound. 
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has moved the wound, immediately in this, one does not put this powder; but put some digested ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it runs well; then the cure of other cures until it is healed.  
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you later about fractures of the skull. 
de la plaie dou col	Of a wound to the neck 
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, it has no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.  
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, there is no other remedy than to leave the wound alone and not apply anything constricting, for it injures the nerves and causes them to withdraw; and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be underneath, such as hot water washed in clear sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and chamomile washed likewise in clear sweet water, and other mine stones according to this manner, and moist ointments. 
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed. 
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and raised and full of pus, pierce it lower; and if the artery is cut, and blood flows, bind it, tie it off, and cauterize it is necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the heart, and the conduit is kept, through which the flesh goes, sew the heart onto the bone of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural shape; then extract it gently, and leave it for a few days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, scrape it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove them all if you can, and those that you cannot get, leave them until the wound rots, and is freed and aligned; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle powder on the powder that I have said. 
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter. 
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Of a wound from a spear or knife  
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a blow from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, see if the wound lets out wind when the patient breathes: then know that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it for the blood which will not stop flowing abundantly, and return to the heart, and kill the patient; but apply an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days or four, or more; if there are no spasms, tremors, heartache, or strange movements of the limbs; and when you see good signs, know that the wound is saved.  
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure it then with tents and other remedies, as long as it heals; and if it cannot heal, and the work is done, then know that there is a fistula; if the cure is as it should be. 
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, whether on the front or back, the cure of what is in front should be done; if it is large, with stitches; and if it is small, with powder; and if it penetrates into the bone, and has splintered pieces, then wash the wound and treat the broken bones if they are loose; and if they are not loose, leave the wound to fester, so that extraction is easier; and for other wounds on other limbs, judgment should be made as we have said. 
dou derrompement dou ventre	of rupture of the belly 
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Ruptures of the belly are large, medium, and small; from a large rupture sometimes the intestines or nerves of the intestines protrude, allowing entry for others; and stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a small rupture is worse than a large one because the intestines can be replaced more easily, if they are not put back one by one; because the intestine swells as soon as it feels cold, and does not go back in easily. Therefore, a medium rupture is better because the intestines can be more easily returned to their place than with others. And know that a rupture of the belly occurs in four ways: the two common stitches occur in the stitching of the belly; and the stitch for other wounds of the body and the two other proper stitches are common to other wounds; and all the same they are more appropriate with the stitch of the belly, and I will say one and declare it. 
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestines is protruding, and greasy things are put back in place, it can be done in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen from the cold. 
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in two ways: soak a sponge or a soft cloth in lukewarm water only, or you cook in water with vinegar and cypress and spikenard, and lift the intestine until the swelling is gone; and never do this by restraint, it must be done gently so as not to swell.  
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling subside, moisten the intestine with water or broth if they are cooked, for this will make it easier to insert things; and if it cannot enter, make a cut in the wound with an instrument used to remove hemorrhoids; and the first cure is gentler than its size, that we should not cut except in great necessity; and here are the instruments for splitting: it cuts inside the curve and goes out, and look at this shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine jumps out, if you put it back together according to its natural form in its proper place, if you have power, because this is worth a lot. 
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the part below the belly, it is fitting that you make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part below the belly, then put the head and chest higher than the parts below, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, then put your mind to this so that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus it is fitting to administer what I say in large and small wounds. 
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, put what appears to you, then have in your hands a compassionate minister who holds the entire rupture in his hand, and assembles the lips; and this is the common manner of stitching, and it is that you take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave from the head of the wound two spaces, and put a needle where it has strong thread; and pierce the two edges of the skin with the two edges of the fascia, which is under the skin inside, as long as you make it pierce from that part, and assemble the two edges of the fascia together four times; then strain it with double thread around the needle twice, then assemble the two edges of the wound evenly, and then leave a space, and put in another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not cease to do this according to what you need needles, as long as the entire wound is restrained; and let the needles be medium-sized, between subtle and large, because subtle needles cut through all the flesh, and those too large cannot enter well: therefore it is fitting that they are medium-sized; and do not put the needles too far from the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before suturing; and then cut the ends of the needles so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and put bandages or cloths at the ends of the needles for them to hold, and leave them as long as the wound is healed; and this manner of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it suffices with one needle or two. The second stitch is common, and it is that you assemble the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the fascia together at a needle where it has strong medium thread; and when you have pierced these edges all four together, then remove the needle from the part where you began, in the manner one sews clothes; and leave a space between each stitch the thickness of a small finger; this stitching heals the man, and I sewed a wound on a man's breast or belly, which was wounded by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and it protruded two palms wide from the intestines, and the wound was in the middle of the belly. 
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I put the intestines back in after they had been out for 24 hours, and the wound healed up to 15 days, and I treated it, and it was cured. 
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they who saw him thought he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with any ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I put nothing more on the wound than old cotton twice a day, and washed it with water and honey until it was healed. 
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing: take the needle and put it through the outer part to the inner part; when it has pierced straight through the center, hold the head of the thread or twine or where you have put the needle in, and make it pierce through from the other side from the inner part to the outer part; and the understanding of this suture is that you sew as furriers do furs, and that you leave the thread once on one side, and pick it up again on the other, until the entire suture is complete. 
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second way of stitching, which Galen properly calls, is as follows: some assemble the two parties together naturally, and apply one end of the sinew to the other end in this manner: insert a needle or the end of a thread nearby, and pierce only that place, leaving the two ends of the sinew; then turn the needle, and pierce it from the back part to the front part, with the two ends of the sinew; then pierce both from the back part to the front part, in two other ends of the sinew which are on the other side; and this is the gentler way of stitching and the most common. 
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this word, and some attest to it, that one must sew the belly with two needles, each having thread; and one should insert one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew belts; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the suture is more grievous than in other places of the belly.  
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, just as the fire has moved it, so put back together the intestine and the cost; then put on top powdered charcoal, and if the fire has moved it, put on any ointment that is present, until the wound swells; and sew the thread, and let the sinews, the muscles, and the nerves be soldered together; then cure the wound as other wounds, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, put on, as soon as it begins to swell, old cotton, and stir it twice a day until it is healed. 
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no need of other medicine in several positions except when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will make commonality with principal members, it is necessary that you moisten linen lightly in tempered oil, or in rose oil, and put it around the angles, and under the armpits; and if he feels pain or decay in the bowels, which often happens, then give enemas of warm red wine, and likewise if the decay comes up to the intestine; and pierce it within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one. 
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is because of the fineness of its veins and the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves. 
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the gut protrudes from the wound, put it back in as you would the intestine while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become green or black, then you must bind the area that is black so that blood does not flow there, for there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ligature, and hang the two ends down from the part below the wound until it comes out to facilitate extraction when the gut falls out, and the wound heals. 
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the eye 
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is round and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, for I saw a man who was wounded in the belly by a lance; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and there was discharge and flatulence; I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to refine it until he was healed, and the wound closed. 
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it soldered, I doubted that the patient would not have pain in his belly; and he did not have any pain, but remained in better condition, and ate and drank; and some experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this way: take tweezers with large heads, then bring the edges of the wound together, and when the tweezers have opened the mouth, put them on the two edges so that they tighten their mouth on it; and then cut off the head, and this stays so that it cannot be loosened, then put another tweezer afterwards in the same way as before, until the wound is all closed up; and sew the wound. 
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	These chiefs are burned in the intestine and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread which is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this way: take the chief of this intestinal thread that is well flayed, and then tie to the chief of this thread a fine twisted linen thread, then put the thread into the needle and sew the intestine, and straighten it at the rupture; and this manner of sewing with tweezers is no stronger than according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the intestinal folds, there is nothing but subtlety. 
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or wherever it may be 
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it becomes chronic, is universally called "fistula," and likewise when it is healed and has receded. 
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to its appearance, a hard and whitish knot, where there is no pain felt, and is also raised like the feather of a bird; sometimes it opens with a clear passage, and other times thick; sometimes small, and other times large; and I have spoken of them in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, when there is no flesh, this occurs only through one of nine causes: that is to say, by the scarcity of blood or flesh; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the edges, which does not allow new flesh to grow; or because there is too much pus; or because the wound is putrid, and the matter is of bad quality; or because the medicine used in treatment is not good; or because the corruption is a type of pestilence; or because the nature of the region is slow to digest and slow to heal, and swollen by nature; or because there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures with medicines in the division. 
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is fitting that I make you know the cure of fistula which is made by work of hands. 
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body; for there are fistulas which come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or at the diaphragm, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and if it reaches the property of the principal member, and similar things. 
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas which are of this manner are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula which does not come to the place that I have said, and you are confident in the cure, and you see it known, if take a tent of linen or iron, if the fistula is straight, if you desire; and if the fistula is twisted, if you seek with a subtle tent of plumbago, for the plumbago bends itself around the tortuousness; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well search it by tents, if you cauterize it by one of the openings, for the moisture will cut from one opening to another, and cleanse it; then draw blood at your power, that you know if there is bone or nerve, and it is completely cleansed, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels at the pressure of your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or from a nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the corruption and rotten flesh that are within; and then heal as long as it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep in a straight place, it is fitting that you cut completely, as far as you can, and then put softened tents steeped in medicinal water, and push them to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the superfluity which remains at the bottom; and then put ointments healing raw flesh, as long as it heals; and if it is not healed by this, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it. 
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not bother you or the main limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, cut away all the corruption until it is completely removed, then treat the underlying things with flesh-growing medicine until it is healed; and if it is not healed and returns to its former state, know that you have not gone far enough: if you uncover and scrape as much as you can until you reach the bottom, remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is well. 
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; if there is nothing else to do but leave it to nature; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with forceps, extract it with an instrument suitable for this purpose; and if there are many bones, treat them all, leaving none behind; and if the moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, cut away the moisture and flesh and free the bones.  
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put something promoting rot on the wound and leave it until the worms have eaten away the flesh around the bones; then you will be able to remove the bones more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as one of the leg or thigh, only allow the corruption until all the blackness is gone, then restore the wound; and if there is a large part that has become corrupted and reaches the marrow of the bone, then you must sew and cover everything up to the corruption, and then treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg so that you may take it as an example and aid in your work.  
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so that the matter came to the leg and it swelled with a large abscess, but there was no reason to open it; but the healers in their folly worked so much on it that they opened the abscess, and much matter drained out, and it became a fistula, and many holes developed that all discharged pus and moisture from the body; and many healers treated him for two years, and there was no one skilled in the art of hands, until I was called upon, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what was draining from the holes with a large amount of pus; and the young man's flesh became red, and he had a yellowish color.  
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I put a tent in one of these holes, and then I encircled all the holes, and found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg. 
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened then, and cut into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came up to the bone inside; I removed what appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and thought that there was no other corruption, except for that which I removed; and I began to restore the wound with medicines for a long time, but could not solder; and then I began again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and removed it, and then tried to solder the place; but I could not until I cut around a palm of the bone, and pierced it through its entire length, then I restored it with medicines; and it was healed and soldered quickly, and I did not have to start the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not suffer, and for the fear of death that I had for him. 
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation it bled often, but he was healed entirely, and in place of the bone there grew hard flesh, and it was of good disposition and had no harm nor anything contrary at all, neither going nor coming. 
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, then it must be treated in this way: take a linen cloth, and bind it to the head of the bone which appears, and order someone to extend it upwards; and put another woolen bandage larger than the first bandage, and tie it on the flesh that is above the bone, and stretch the head so that you draw down the corrupted flesh, and uncover the flesh on the place where you wish to cauterize, so that the sinew does not scorch the flesh; and put a coal or a board beneath the bone to move aside the corrupted flesh; and it must be treated as long as one can see and feel the corruption, and treat again another time. 
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not appear, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then expose all the flesh; then put a coal underneath, and then sew from one part to the other the corruption, and let the suture be as long as the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and sew the bone where it holds on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, then there is no other remedy than to cut it; and if the corruption is at the point of the hand or the point of the foot, then it is very strong, but nevertheless it behoves you to inquire about this corrosion, how it appears to you; and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but let the vein or nerve not oppose you; and know that the incisor and the saws for cutting these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and the appearance of them, their thickness and their subtlety, their size and their smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it behoves one to equip oneself with an instrument for each semblance of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of the illnesses; so consider the instrument which you need according to what is fitting. 
dou feu	of fire 
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The flesh rots either from within or from without; and when you have medicine that corrodes through the treatment of medicines, and it does not profit, then it is necessary to cut off that member up to the place where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes through this from death, or from the malice, which is greater, of the lack of the member; and the signs are that the member becomes black, so that it seems as if it were burned by fire, and rots after the blackness, then that corrosion goes from member to member, and takes hold of the whole body; if you hasten to cut off, and if it is from the sting of some venomous beasts, such as a sea scorpion and viper and similar ones, if the corrosion is at the head of the toe, then cut it off, and do not give it space to come up to the hand. 
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, bind it at the joint so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, bind it with a knife; and if it passes the knife, it is death, and there is no other remedy than the quantity of its virtue; and do the same when the corrosion comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, bind it after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, bind all the foot; and if it rises to the leg, bind it at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die; and the manner of binding or sewing the limb is that you tie it above and below, and extend one of the bandages below, and another bandage above, and you loosen the flesh which is between the two bandages at a span wide, so that the bone is uncovered; then bind or sew, and put on each side a linen cloth so that the seam does not touch the healthy place, and it brings the patient other injury and abscesses. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs while you are working, cauterize the area quickly, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete, and then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his left foot: he developed a blackness that looked like a burn from fire, and this corrosion first appeared on the back of his left foot, until it spread throughout his whole foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he quickly decided to cauterize his foot, and it was healed; and some time later, the corrosion returned in the back of his hand, and he came to me, and I put things that repel on it after cleaning the body, but I could not stop the corrosions; and he asked me to cauterize his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of repelling the matter; and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die, because the man's strength was weak; and he completely despaired, and returned to his land, and quickly decided to cauterize his hand, and it was healed; and I only tell this story so that others may do the same, if they need to. 
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess comes in fleshy places and stays for so long that it gathers a lot of pus; then it bursts and the pus escapes, leaving the place empty, just like a vessel; and the skin above is as thin as a delicate cloth, and does not reach to the bone or nerve; such a sickness is called “sain” and is not called “fistula”; but if it becomes so elongated that it reaches the bone completely, then it is called “fistula”; and the skin, if you cut through all around it, just as it is thin, like a cloth; and does not heal because of its corruption. 
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you believe that the skin will heal and the corruption is not complete, and the skin is thick like flesh, then treat it with an enema: look to see if the breast is large and the pus that comes from it has a foul odor, then give an enema of Egyptian medicine which is made as follows: take equal amounts of aloes and oil, and put them in a vessel over the fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take some according to your need, mix it with water and honey, and administer it as an enema into the breast and draw out the pus; leave the medicine in for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; do this many times until the breast is cleansed and the odor is gone. 
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowel is perfect, do not allow char to form there; and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the bowel runs to the lowest place where it is. 
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast grows swollen and indigestible after many days, know that the breast does not heal. 
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons cut after a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches. 
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men whose wounds heal quickly and some who do the opposite; and if a swollen breast remains undigested after many days, know that the breast does not heal; and if the breast is slow to heal and is prolonged, apply drying medicines, moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diachylon ointment, for there is a great part of vitriol in it, and it is the last medicine; take diachylon ointment and make it with rose oil and rose water equal in quantity; then cook it and use it; and this same makes thickened honey better when diachylon ointment is not present, or you can take myrrh and aloes and frankincense, and grind them, and powder them on the honey when it is off the fire; then glue I drape and stretch it out over the breast, and sometimes administer aristolochia longa and roots of white lily, which are also like flour of spelt and centaury; use them simply or compounded: grind them and make powder, and put on the honey that I have mentioned, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged and is not cured by this cure, then know that the corruption is perfect and makes an impression in the bone, or in hard limbs, or in ligaments; so the cure of the fistula as we said before.  
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the finger 
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	A panaritium is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the hand or foot, or by chance arises in other places; and when it is envied, and no care is taken, then it becomes a large abscess, running and discharging pus so abundantly that it runs to the root of the nail, and by chance runs all the way through; and corrosion comes even to the bone, until there is a foul-smelling pain, and the flesh of the finger is swollen, and its color is dark. 
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the section, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away all the superfluity that remains from the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards. 
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cauterization is a great help if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses the flesh, and it begins to grow in, and the wound festers, then you must put a wedge under the nail that does not touch the flesh, and push it upward, and cut away this thin flesh subtly and lightly, and apply burning and corrosive medicines on the remaining flesh to remove everything; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.  
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it away and treat it deeply, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see the bone corrupting, cut it away in a way we have said before, then treat it until it is healed; and if it is hard, swollen, and he feels great pain, it is necessary that you heal it first; then cut the nail with a sharp spatha, cutting across above it, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, put something on top that soothes. 
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of deafness in the hand 
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The bone that grows in the hands of some men is sometimes all flesh and sometimes has part where it has bones, and sometimes it has a nail, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or its birth is in some way in the bones. 
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in any part of the body does not move and he who is born at the joint of the body may move; the size of him who is fleshy so it is light, in this way: cut him at his root with a wide spatula. 
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is grievous to cure; if you hold it, cut it.  
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For him who is born in any part of the body but at the last joint, it is fitting that you cut first the flesh roundly to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable size for it, then treat it until it is healed. 
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joining that comes to two bones together comes by birth, or by the joining of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.  
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is fitting that you cut that joining so that the bones rejoin according to their natural forms; then put between two cloths or soft cloths soaked in rose oil so they do not join again; or you put between two thin pieces of lead until the bone has joined, as it should.  
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to any of his limbs with the palm, then cover that swelling as it should be covered. 
des vils	of vile things
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large winding vessels full of melancholic superfluities, which come in several parts of the body; and they occur more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry things than in others. 
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary then that you administer to him sometimes purging with coles, and afterwards the sage of basil. 
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cautery with iron is done in two ways: one is that you cauterize them and draw out the black blood; and the other way is that you tie off the vein and burn it all the way through. 
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	Bloodletting is done in this manner: first heat the leg with hot water very strongly until the thick blood becomes thinned, then bind the patient's leg above the thigh just below the knee; then cauterize the vein in one, two or three places, with a wide cut, then draw and burn out the black blood with your hand from one end to the other, as much blood as the strength of the patient can suffer; and then tie it off and order him to eat meats mixed with black colewort; and repeat the evacuation and healing when the veins are full and the patient is troubled. 
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The raising of the arrow is according to this manner: seize the leg of the patient, if there are many hairs, then put it in a bath, and apply hot water to the leg until it becomes red, and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then cut the place where the vein is long at the head of the knee, or in the part below the ankle; then pierce the skin with a knife, and flay the vein from all sides, until it appears when touched; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters under the skin it seems also like a white cord; then put the arrow underneath, until it is raised from the skin, and then pull it gently at the knife, and then cut it in another place above three times; then flay the skin upon the vein until it appears, then raise it with the arrow, as you did, and pull it to another knife, as you did first; then cut another incision, or several if you need them, then raise it, and cut it at the back of the foot, then draw and raise it up to the second incision; then extract it incision by incision, until it is all out, then cut it; and if you cannot draw and raise it, put a double-threaded needle through all of it, tie it, and draw it, and put it under the arrow, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it comes out; and watch that it does not cut, for if it cuts, one cannot draw or raise it, and it brings harm to the patient; and when you have drawn all of it, put wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the place of the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and entangled together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it obliquely, but do not sever it completely; and treat it as we have said before. 
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vein if it is curved and does not cut cleanly, it will cut the vein; and it must be of large curvature because if it were slender it would sever the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is the form: 
de la voinne civile	of a civilian vein 
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in hot parts where neither herbs nor trees grow, and in earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it appears elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from rot that comes under the skin, as serpents and worms come inside the body, embedded between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that a very great inflammation comes in the leg, then the flesh changes color, and the vein begins to protrude, as a root of a plant. 
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein opens, it is fitting that you wrap a piece of linen around it from three and a half to eleven and a half fingerbreadths, tie it, and leave the linen hanging on the leg; and every time it begins to protrude beyond the thread, wrap it around the linen again and tie it.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never at this vein more than twice, and even when it opens at the ankle joint or foot, and there comes much pus and where it escapes: treat it as we have said before. 
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between skin and flesh 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This sickness is called in our land "beef disease," because it often happens to oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down, and he who has it feels it well from limb to limb, as long as it eats through the skin where it goes, and jumps far; and it comes from corruption of certain humors, just as come worms and serpents and lampreys and ascarides or roundworms in the belly; and there is doubt about its malice, for when it goes through the body and ascends to the head, and it comes to the eye, it may perchance enter and destroy the eye; and this happens many times.
