Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it cleansed and drained, if it cannot be removed when it goes: then it is necessary that you tie the place above and below with a strong tight ligature, then cut on top and drain it forcefully; and if the worm is completely embedded in the flesh and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it runs into the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or close to the eye, remove the eyebrow below it, then cut on top and drain it forcefully; and it is necessary to use medicines dissolving the body's corrupted humors for the patient and to avoid foods causing putrefaction. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes in some limbs, and then can move from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you. 
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm; and a little while after, I saw it rise as quickly as a worm to her shoulder, as fast as quicksilver when it runs from one place to another; the pain moved from that place, and went into her shoulder, and then a little while after ran through all her body, until it came to her other arm; then she told me that it turned again around her body, just as I saw it. 
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered greatly how she moved so from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness in this manner. 
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had seen many who had felt pain move from one place to another, but I had never seen it as I saw it in this woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and uncovered veins, and because of that appeared this constrained windiness; and it does not appear according to this reason in those who are fleshy, and have moist bodies and full veins.  
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see curing this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then bind it above and below hastily, and then cauterize it so long as this windiness constrained to its place will be forced out; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it at your eyes, then cure it with what expels windiness, such as foul-smelling pills, and serpent pills, and similar others. 
des saiettes	arrows 
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in bodies where they fall.  
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their kind is that there are those which have large points, and small ones, and barbed ones, and soldered ones; and those which have two angles, and those which have barbs, and those which have pieces; and those which fall into any member fall according to two manners: either in principal members they fall, such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.  
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When the head of the arrow is located in any part of these limbs, and the signs of death which I will tell you about later appear to you: then it is necessary that you refrain from extracting this arrow, because death comes afterward in many situations; and when these evil signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then treat it and cure the wound. 
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow is lodged and pierces the bone, and leaps the dura mater which is above the brain, is when there is dimming of vision and stupor and trembling and redness in it, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and disturbance of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps it occurs without pus from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps he loses speech and voice; and a discharge of white moisture from the wound resembling pus, and also a burning sensation like that of fire; and if these signs appear to you, then refrain from treatment and treat the arrow if it is not embedded. 
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of a heart attack when it strikes or occurs is that it is near the left breast and also feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and perhaps the heart attack moves just as the pulse does, and there comes forth black blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: know then without doubt that death approaches.  
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of a wound that is not treated by cautery is that without pain there is discharge of pus from the wound and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and desires cold air. 
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the wound strikes in the covering of the buttock, it is below the ribs; and it gives great anguish and great pain and sighing; and all the limbs from the shoulders move. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the wound strikes the stomach, it may happen that some undigested food comes forth from the wound. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow lodges in the belly, and it does not pass through the intestines, there is no hope for a cure or the extraction of the arrow. 
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow lodges in the bladder, and the urine escapes and begins to flow, and the patient feels great pain; know that the wound is mortal. 
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and arm and spine of the back and thigh and legs, and similar limbs are safe according to various positions. 
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and it is not venomous as I will tell you so that you may do otherwise.  
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow struck or pierced him in the root of the nose: I tried it, and drew it out from the other side below the fat of the ear, and he was healed without harm. 
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And draw out an arrow with one hand that fell into the fat under the skin below the paper, and the arrow was embedded, and could only be reached by its point towards the fire, and it was a large arrow the size of a Turkish bow, made of light iron without ears; the wound healed well, and he did not suffer any ill effects. 
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I drew out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow with ears: I shaved his beard, and worked carefully until I drew it out, and the Christian healed well. 
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I drew out an arrow from a man that had fallen into his belly, and thought he would die; and then after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change; I cut above the arrow and hooked it, and drew it forcefully, and he did not suffer any ill effects. 
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man into whom an arrow has fallen or lodged, and the wound is stitched shut above it; and the arrow remains within him, and does not change its natural position, nor find any hindrance in any of his natural functions. 
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you see another man into whom an arrow has fallen in his face, and the wound is stitched shut above it; and it remains thus, causing him great pain; and many other similar things. 
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated an arrow wound on a prince of the king, which had fallen between his nose and cheek, and was leaning slightly towards the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded. I was called to treat it three days after it fell. 
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow. 
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I probed it with great subtlety and did not feel it at all; and he felt numbness and pain below his right ear. 
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the point of an arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the plaster on for many days and sewed up the wound thoroughly and kept the patient for a long time until he felt the arrow one day within his flesh and told me so.  
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put corrosive medicine on the wound for many days until it was open and I probed it and felt the head of the arrow stirring in place; then I added to the opening of the wound with that same corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me; and it healed well within four months, and then I widened the wound so that I could put in forceps and move it from side to side, but it would not come out; then I did not cease to refine and devise ways with instruments until one day I took it with forceps well made, according to its form which will be shown at the end of this chapter, until I drew it out and closed the wound. 
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the master judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored; I restored it then, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was completely healed. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you place your cure on what I do not say, because books cannot grasp everything; but wise masters compare upon very little things, and upon what is present and lacking, they find nine works, and nine instruments, for the removal of foreign things which occur in this art. 
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not exit the limbs where they are fixed except according to two ways: either through the place where they enter, or through another part; and the one which exits through the place where it enters is an arrow embedded in the flesh, and rarely exits now. 
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, leave it until the flesh around it is rotten and the opening is enlarged; and also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it like that for several days, and move it each day; and then it will come out. And if it does not come out, pierce around it with a very fine instrument until the flesh around it is expanded, and then remove it. 
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the accidents that I have mentioned appear to the patient: do not remove it, but leave it until it is equal after several days, for if the arrow comes as far as the syfac, it is death. 
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not reach the syfac, and the patient remains for several days without bad accidents, then engage in the removal. 
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very stuck like this and cannot come out forcefully, then apply bandages around it as I have told you; then treat the area until it is healed. 
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in a place in the body so that you cannot see it, then try to grasp it with all your strength; and if you feel it, then draw it out with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot do this because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then widen the wound so that it is large; and draw out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears by which it is held, remove the flesh that is stuck to it from two sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can draw it out; and be careful not to break the arrow so that you might draw it out more easily.  
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the surrounding flesh is ripe, then treat it, for the extraction will be easier. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood opposes you, then apply what we have said about wound treatment in its chapter; and be careful not to cut a nerve or vein, and try as best you can to draw out the arrow without danger, whether quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the position they were in when the arrow fell upon them, for this is the greatest help. And if you cannot, then place them according to what the signs show you. 
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	For an arrow that has come from another direction, or where you see nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in the place where it can be seen or felt distinctly: cut there, as much as the forceps can grasp, and then extract it: if it jumps now. 
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is caught in the bone, turn your hand round and round until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then draw it out. 
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it still and then begin the extraction again until it comes out forcefully; and if it were from an arrow, push it all the way in; and if it were a bone, and you see that it is difficult to push, then administer the instrument with its point facing down, so that the point of the arrow enters the groove of the instrument; and then push forcefully, and if the arrow is barbed, push the instrument with its point entering inwards, to ease the extraction. 
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is poisoned, it is necessary that you cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as is appropriate. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow sticks in the flesh or the thigh or the belly or the bladder or the side, and it is close to the surface, and you can grasp it, then grasp it; and be careful not to grasp a vein or nerve, and then extract it, and then stitch the wound if necessary; and treat it until it is healed. 
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps with which one treats arrows resembles a bird's beak, and see here the shape: 
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow. 
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the pushing tip is also like the feather of a bird, to push at the point of the arrow, as this is its shape: 
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the forceps for pushing and pulling is this:  
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common body veins 
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins from which one can be bled, of which there are XVI on the head: to wit: II batans which are after the ears, which are called the two “herbech”; and the II arteries which are in the II temples apparent; and II veins which are in the II corners of the II eyes, which are called “aspires”; and the vein which is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein which is on the head above the nose; and the II guindeges which are at the neck; and the II veins which are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins which are called “augeherich”; and II veins which are below the tongue. 
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are V in each arm: the one is the cephalic, and is on the left side, and the common people call it “vein of the head”; and the median is called “faste”, and is composed of the cephalic and the basilica, and the common people call it “vein of the heart”; and the basilica is on the right side, and the common people call it “vein of the belly”, and it is above the fossa, and it is that which one bleeds, which appears manifestly above the pouch. 
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvation vein is the one between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is below the curve of the hip pocket on the left side, and the second saphenous vein is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those. 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The sinews of the veins that are after the ears help with old catarrhs and migraines; and the qualities of the sinew, as I told you, is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a vise, so much that the two veins appear behind the ears in two pendants from the head: put your thumb there, and where you feel the pulse below your thumb, it is a sign to cut; then take the lancet, and insert it below the vein until the bone, then lift your hand along the whole vein upwards, and cut both the skin and the vein well twice across, and let blood flow out as much as you see; then bind and tie it, until it is healed; and I have already said the incision and the cautery in the first book. 
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries which are in the two temples is good for ancient migraines, and habitual ophthalmia, and for the body's acute tears as well; and the quality of the bleeding is as I say: and it is that the patient constricts his neck so that the two veins appear openly; and he feels the pulse below his thumb, and then presses with force; then lifts the heart above the vein at the top with his index finger, and inserts the lancet below, and lifts the vein upward, and cuts it, as you have done in the other two veins, and let blood flow according to your need; then untie the patient, and place your thumb on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on; then bind it firmly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of them and their cutting and their extraction, as is the beginning of the book. 
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bloodletting from the vein on the forehead is worth as much as the bloodletting from the cephalic for old illnesses of the face, and migraine, and redness. 
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the amount you see; then untie the patient's collar, and tie the vein as long as it is healthy and never open it again with a wide flame. 
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not right for the flame to be too strong; and hold the cautery sideways, because the bone is nearby, and by chance breaks the cautery when it is delicate. 
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bloodletting of the two veins that are in the two temples helps against epilepsy, and against redness, and against inflammation in the eye, and against diseases of the face; and the quality of their bloodletting is such that the patient squeezes his neck by twisting with any ligature, as before; then bleed, and let the bleeding be through a passage, a spot long with the cautery one spot wide, because there is no flesh.  
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, by chance they break; then make a clean cut of blood, as much as you need, and then bind it on cotton, and bind it well. 
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bloodletting of the vein at the nose is good for ague, and for sudden fevers, and for facial illnesses such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, even when it is old; and the quality of the bloodletting is that the patient twists their neck, then strains their nose with your left hand, and takes a long subtle flame, and sticks it into the lip space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow; do not go too deep in, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for one night, because it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame: 
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bloodletting of the two veins helps in the constriction of the anus, and at the beginning of hemorrhoids, and many diseases, and scabies, and corruption, and herpes, and fistulas; and the quality of the bloodletting is that the patient tightens his neck below one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing above the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a seat, then bleed the vein for a long time and widely, then draw out the blood temperately, or as much as necessary; then do the same in the other vein, then untie the tie, and draw out all the veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed. 
de la sainie des leivres	Of bloodletting of the lips. 
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Bloodletting of the veins above the lips helps with boils in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and nosebleeds and pain. 
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the vein is such as to make the patient sit in front of you, and pull out his neck as I have said; then turn back the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are known by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins: therefore cut both of them, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, cut the largest of each side, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner. 
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the vein below the tongue 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The vein below the tongue helps after the cephalic vein, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and eye diseases, and mouth diseases; and the quality of the bleeder is such that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and he lifts his tongue, and looks underneath on each side a black vein: therefore cut one and the other, and do not go too far forward, because there are arteries below. 
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins through which we commonly bleed are bled in two ways: either by pricking with a large lancet, or with a subtle olive-pointed instrument called an "anise"; and they are wide or narrow according to the width and narrowness of the veins. 
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the lancet is very well known and is as wide as you see: 
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the raised veins full of thick visible blood and those containing thick and troubled blood; and this is the shape of the olive lancet:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pointed and is for bleeding subtle veins where there is subtle yellow blood. 
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	Bleeding from the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps illnesses that are below the throat, and in the neck, chest, and abdomen; and it is fitting for the bleeder to bleed moderately, and he must be wary of the artery that is underneath. 
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and the blood flow comes, then you must cauterize it as I have said; and the flame should not be stabbing but cutting like a knife. 
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open clearly, then you must extract it and change another; or if you want any vein of it, or you heal in its place the vein below the arm: it opens clearly; and cut with a knife flame as we have said. 
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see to know the place of the vein, then it is fitting that you extract the arm so that you touch the place as long as you know the pulse; then mark the place with ink, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with a knife flame; and beware that you do not wound the artery when you see the swollen place, for it is of the artery: wipe it therefore. 
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it protrude at the top as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from an artery: hurry then and put your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens; bind up the arm and leave it like that, and do not move it; let the patient be afraid, and do not move it until it is healed. 
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding does not stop and it comes back to you and the medicine is not present, then bind the artery when it is exposed because the head of the artery retracts; and stop the bleeding. 
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a bark of mulberry, and cut it, and take one of the halves and tie it on well until the next day; if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, then treat it as we have said with powders that stop blood; and the stopping is not greasy in many positions because of the small size of the wound, and the strength of the bandage on the arm. 
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein of the middle arm helps so much that it draws blood from above the head and below the body, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins as we have said; and it behooves the healer to be careful for the nerve that lies beneath, and if he does not point too far in, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and the healing is griped, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve appears much of the time, and if it does not appear in some men because of its subtlety, then you must heal it with an instrument that numbs; and escape the nerve as best you can. 
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then he makes the incision long. 
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The incision of the cephalic vein helps so that it draws blood from the head, and helps as well; and it behooves one to incise with a flame of olive or myrtle, for it is the safest of all the veins, because there is neither nerve nor artery beneath it. 
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to seek the easiest place, and do not worry if one must try the first time, and start again; and perhaps the place swells for some people when one tries the first time, but it does not matter. 
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the incision is according to your thought. 
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing that you must know about bleeding is that it is administered only to preserve health and to avoid future diseases; and the incision should be made in one of the three veins which are: namely, the cephalic, basilic, and saphenous; and one should bleed at the beginning of spring in youth, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of repletion appear; and one should bleed on the first day or the third, after two or three hours from the day.  
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bloodletting which is administered to the sick has no determined hour, but only when need arises by day or night, at all hours and all times; and it is not fitting to bleed children until fourteen years old, nor a woman carrying a child before the fourth month until the seventh.  
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Nor should those who have passed sixty years be bled. 
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wishes to be bled, in whatever manner it may be, it is fitting that they purify their bowels with a mild clyster, if they have retained much phlegm, so that the veins do not draw from the bowels harmful superfluities which might injure the principal members; nor should one who is too full of meats, nor who is drunk, to the point of intoxication, nor one who is suffering from dropsy be bled; and one should not bleed after a colic attack, vomiting, discharge from the belly, and multiplication of births in women, and from toil, watchfulness, and hunger, and those whose vital force is altogether exhausted, or by something of the weapon or of the body; but afterwards subtilize the humors if they are thick, by foods and drinks and by medicines if you have them; then enter a bath if nothing forbids it, to thin the blood, and bleed from the vein of the left arm near the third finger, as we have said; and guard yourself on that day from labor, and pain, and lust, and similar things; and be calm and joyful, and let the bleeder stand higher than the one being bled, and rub the arm two or three times, then tighten the ligature moderately, for when it is too tight or too loose, the blood will not flow; and then rub the place with your hands until the veins swell, and are felt; then moisten the blade of the bleeder with a drop of old oil, then put your index finger of your left hand below the place where you wish to bleed, so that the vein does not jump and fail when cut. 
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee as quickly as strings in a musical instrument, and some of these are full of windiness, so that when one puts on the flame, it withdraws from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of them; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore it is necessary that the bloodletters be advised in these things. 
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; if not, begin again a little below that place or above hastily, if the veins are not swollen. 
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the veins are swollen, and the patient is frightened, leave him for one or two days and do not bind the arm: perhaps abscesses will come; do not enter into a bath, then begin again the bloodletting if it pleases him; and if the opening is small, or you cut subtly with a knife and doubt that he will not issue as much blood as you see, apply all the flame directly to that opening itself; and work quickly, so that the vein is swollen; for this happens often when the wound is small. 
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not begin the cutting again, and put a poultice of oil there, for it draws away the blood from the body, and the oil softens the linen in this place; and thus administer the oil-linen in every vein that you cut to staunch the flow of blood; and the same does triacle and a bandage of them, when it is put on the place; it is so subtle and separates when it is too large. 
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens, even when it has not been cut more than once or twice and the opening of the vein is small, hasten and put on the place a sponge moistened in hot water and salt for an hour; and you must do this after the blood flows from the vein, and if it remains there after some days without any blackness or greenness, do not harm it; and if you see, put on something of aloes or myrrh dissolved in juice of calamint, costmary, or similar. 
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there occurs an abscess and swelling at the vein of the basilisk; so put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft under the pressure of your hand, that appearance is bad. 
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore be careful that you do not put anything on it of what we have said, for fear you might cut into an artery but make a dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed. 
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each blood according to the quantity of its virtue and its color.  
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it is red; and if you see it thick, let it flow out until it is thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down. 
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is full and strong and needs bloodletting to make a wider incision, and the flames should be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and he should be bled often in small amounts, and one must bleed him by cutting across, not by stabbing; and this method of bleeding saves from excessive loss of blood and damage to nerves, and it is worth more than long or deep bleeding. 
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for him whose body is weak at the time of a purging, it is fitting to give softened bread in pomegranate juice; if he is hot, draw blood three or four times. And if he is of cold complexion, give him before the purge softened bread in thickened syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chicory, and a well-scented syrup. 
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints at the purging, after the passing of much blood, it is fitting that he inhale broth of flesh and subtle scented syrup, and use the other things we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of the veins. 
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to empty some arms, and purge another time, it is fitting that when he is weakened by a great purging, that he purges a little at a time, according to the quantity of his continuing strength.  
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to bandage their arm after the first bleeding, and they have strong flesh, then bleed them seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour. 
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to be bled elsewhere, they should be bled on the second day or the third. 
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body that has already been heated, and it causes fever; so it is necessary to draw out a large quantity, and widen the opening as much as it will flow freely like a stream; then after you have observed all the conditions of bleeding, place your hand on their pulse while they are bleeding so that death does not come in place of the stream, for this often happens when the bleeder is negligent; and it is not fitting when you see the arm loosened and make blood come out the second time, and the opening is closed, that you press strongly upon it; nor if it is curved, that they stretch the arm hastily, for that would be bad; but leave it until it bleeds the second time; or put a point of flame at the opening until the congealed blood at the vein's opening flows freely, and place a small piece of silk moistened with vinegar on it and press lightly. 
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not constrict it, until the abscess is calmed. 
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires drawing blood a second time, do it in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm. 
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein at the bend of the arm is healthier than the vein in the head because it is composed. 
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of bloodletting is that the patient plunges their hand into hot water until the flesh is red; then it is tied moderately so that the vein appears well, then it is bled across, not lengthwise or breadthwise; and let the puncture be wide, and bleed very close to the joint of the hand, and if none can come out, put the hand back into hot water, and let the blood run into the water until you have enough; and if it is summer, do not put the hand back into hot water again, for it is applied more in winter than in summer; and bleeding from this vein is safer than all other veins, because there are neither arteries nor nerves. 
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The vein of the salvation of the right hand is worth for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: draw out the hand, and put it in hot water, as long as the vein is swollen, if you see it; and if the vein is across, and if you cut it through and through, it does not matter; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are underneath all bare of flesh, and then put the hand back into hot water, if the blood is frozen in the wound, and cannot come out. 
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drained as much blood as needed, put oil and wax on the vein to heal quickly, and do this for every vein. 
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The vein in the left hand is good for the disease of the spleen, and do everything as I told you about the right. 
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The vein of the shoulder is worth for all illnesses that are below the body, such as illnesses of the marrow, and retention of fluids, and illness of the loins, and of the thighs and old legs, and similar illnesses. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its vein is that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it bleeds, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and by above the foot go many veins; therefore, if the vein at the ankle or a larger vein, than one further up is better.  
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bleed it on the foot, be careful of the nerves that are below, and the vein bleeds as well as in cutting; and let the flame be anesthetized. 
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, put the foot back in the hot water and let the vein drain well. 
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the sinews fail the first time, begin again the second time a little above, for the flesh is salty; and do not doubt the nerves, as we have said, and so make the incision on the other foot equally. 
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The flesh of the sciatic vein is at the ankle strong, and its sinew is worth the pain of the hip, when it is for hot blood. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its sinew is such that the patient enters or bathes, and twists above the ankle four times in twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, draw the sinew in all the ways that you can, and across; and it is worth more that you cut it, for the flesh is underneath, and it is very full of men. 
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, draw any vein of which it opens or behind the two feet, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and make as much blood flow as you see, and then untie the cord, and put cotton on it and remove it; it is now healed.  
des sainies de ventouse	from suction cups 
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horn, or glass, or wood; and cupping is done in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking. 
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping that is done without pricking is also done in two ways: either it is with all heat, or without heat; and cupping which is done by pricking and extraction of blood is done in fourteen places on the body, of which one is on the top of the head; and another on the back of the neck; and two others on the sides of the neck; and a cupping glass under the chin; and a cupping glass on both shoulders; and a cupping glass on the buttocks; and cupping glasses along both arms; and cupping glasses on both legs; and cupping glasses on both ankles; and cupping does not draw blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken anyone as much as one does when drawing blood from a vein; and it is not right for it to be administered, neither with all heat nor without heat, in any illness which comes from repletion, until all the body has been emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if it is necessary for illness to cup, or by custom, then we administer them each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in any time; because there are those who when they need cupping have a heavy head; and there are those who find repletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and in their neck, and darkness among them; and there are those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swelling of the tongue, and spit blood; and there are those who faint, and see blood by night, and are seized with nausea and death and similar things. 
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is the middle of the month, we forbid them to be cupped after three hours of the day. 
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding of the arm helps against headache... that comes to them, and it should not be done after the evacuation of the whole body; and this cupping is in place of the bleeding of the head, and it should not be used by those who are of cold complexion or who have diarrhea, because it does them great harm; and for this reason, old men should not use it, nor those who have cold illnesses. 
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover often become oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower because of the fear of oblivion. 
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Cupping on the neck is in place of the healing of the head and the basilica, and for this reason it is worth using for the constriction of the breast, and for the splitting of the channel of the diaphragm, and for all other things; and a little must be put, for if it holds too firmly, it will cause oblivion or stomach and heart ache. 
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Cupping on the second ribs of the neck is good for headaches, and ophthalmia and migraine, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and it replaces the healing of the basilica; and you must instruct the patient to press his hand upon it, so that he does not cut the artery, and blood does not flow. 
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Cupping under the chin is good for mouth diseases, and gum decay, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is placed on the two lips. 
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cupping on the shoulders is good for illness that comes from heat and fullness. 
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Cupping on the elbows is as good as three veins in the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the healer that he not make too strong a suction, for the flesh is thin there, and lies beneath nerves and arteries.  
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping that is on the rump is good for hemorrhoids of the buttocks, and for illnesses below; and it is fitting that the cupping be large, and be of horn, so that it has need to draw well; and by chance, if it were delicate, it would break; and it would make big wounds.  
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	If the cupping glasses on the legs bleed freely, because they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains in the limbs, and in the bladder, and soften tumors; and they are placed on the two thighs, and the two ankles, but always they weaken the body after long use, and cause emaciation in many conditions. 
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put on a cupping glass is that you first put it empty and suck moderately, then apply it quickly and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the place red and swollen and see the redness of the blood; then remove it and replace the cupping glasses, and be careful with the disposition of the bodies, because there are some who have such fat flesh and clear pores: so it is fitting to prick only once and make large wounds and one deep prick; and suck lightly. 
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is large, it is fitting to cut it twice: the first time to make subtle the way for thick blood. 
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it is fitting to cut it a third time; and when we wish to draw blood little by little, we only make one incision. 
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we wish for a lot of blood, we often begin again; and if the vein is thick, we pierce it deeply enough so that the core is slightly pierced, and it is fitting for one who has thick, hard skin, and those who have few pores, that you anoint the place where the cupping glasses will be applied with oil that is stimulating and dissolving: if it is summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is winter, with watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or another similar one.  
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of balsam, or oil of anise, and similar ones. 
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one whom you are treating has tender flesh and large pores, it is not advisable to put oil on it, but rather wash it after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberries, or water of pumpkins, or water of porcelain, or other similar ones. 
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture should rise with water of rue, or water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things. 
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large superfluities should rise with old wine, or water of vinegar, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar ones; and it is not advisable to cup before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and do not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he wash himself when he is about to be cupped and when he has been cupped. 
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And guard that he who is recovering is not choleric, and if his wound is too sore and inflamed; it is fitting that he should take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces in season, and similar things; and eat little, and roast chicken, and moist meats. 
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.
