And he who has a cold complexion should take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine halfway between old and new, and eat little, and eat little birds and pigeons; and on the day that he will be cupped, he should drink more than eat; and it is fitting to give some men sometimes trefoil or nutmeg before or after cupping, to comfort the main limbs; and let the wound be subtle, but it is not fitting for those who are hot to drink it. 
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Cupping glasses which are put without cutting are those which are put on the liver, and on the thighs, and gout, and on the belly and buttocks and loins and hip, because these limbs do not suffer from being cut, and we only do this to draw blood from limb to limb, such as when we put them on the breasts when a newborn is unhealthy; to remove the viscosity which is in the limb, such as when we put cupping glasses on the belly and buttocks to reduce the limb; and it removes pain, when there is inflammation or stone, as it removes by its attractive virtue possibly the inflammation, or detaches the stone from its place; and thus it does when one puts it on the liver and on the thighs when there is retained windiness, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes full of lukewarm water, such as in illnesses with pleurisy, and in this manner one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water in which herbs suitable for this have been boiled.  
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass applied by fire is as follows: 
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	It has two fingers wide and half a palm in length, and it has at its side near the middle a small hole, as for putting in a needle, and it is of iron, smoothed beforehand so that it does not bruise the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle there is a crossbar of iron or wood to put a wick soaked in oil, and they are made large and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who use them; for cupping glasses for children are different from those for old people, and for thin people than for fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should put this cupping glass on the limb as follows: take the wick of wax or linen, and put it through the hole in the middle of the cupping glass, so that the flame is at the bottom of the glass so that it does not burn the patient; then place it on the limb, and your thumbs should be on the hole we have mentioned, so that when you want to see if the vapor is going, you can remove the cupping glass; and take the linen as before, and start again often, if needed.  
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping glass which is administered for pleurisy, in any acute [pain], it has neither a stem nor a hole, and it is not administered unless it is full of water, and it is placed upon the member only; and this is its form: 
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Cupping glasses are not administered unless it is in members where one cannot put cupping glasses because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in those naked of flesh, such as the breast or nose, and other similar [places]; and the quality of the user is that when you find cupping glasses that are in good water, clean and without holes, take them. 
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, raise the place slowly, and then sharply, very well, and then aspirate it; and if the veins are too close to the body's flesh, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and apply it until the flesh is contracted; and if the veins are multiplied, apply powdered vitriol, or alum, and similar things, until they are contracted; or put half a handful of peeled beans on the place and leave them until they burn at the place, then it will stop now; and if you need more, take other veins. 
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the veins do not want to be taken, rub the place with fresh blood, or insert a needle until the vein comes out, and then apply them, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will burn; and when you see that they fall, sprinkle a pinch of powdered aloe and salt, or ashes on top, they will stop now. 
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures 
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations. 
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the folly of men has kept them from this chapter, so they have never seen any of the old books nor read a single letter in them; and for this reason, the science is foreign to our land, for I have never found anyone good at it; and I know nothing of it except through the science of the old books, which I have studied so much that I have acquired knowledge of it, and by experiment and by the custom of my life; and I have described in this chapter what it contains, and summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I have done in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary then that we say or prologue of this book the sums of speech and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and remains on truthfulness, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others. 
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the sick person on one side and the other, if nothing hinders him, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age; or if his time is not very high, or too cold; and forbid cold meats, which are to know cold dishes, and game, and goat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of a hot abscess, nor of the spreading of matter to the limb; if the sick person returns to his first usual government which he used. 
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to mend, it is necessary that one nourish the patient with foods that promote thickening, or viscosity, such as cooked wheat in broth, rice, and pies, and veal stomach, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things. 
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with thick nourishment the muscles are built up and the break heals more quickly. 
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the old and infirm cannot be properly set or joined according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those which are too tender, such as the bones of young children; but do not worry, set the broken bone with large splints which bind and hold the limb together until it is strengthened as it was before; and do not remove them for a while, and for this reason, it is necessary to nourish them with thick foods as we have said. 
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways. 
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures. 
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to splintering, and another in sharpening, such as the point of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it's a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small crack all the way through. 
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each manner has its own treatment and instrument for restoration, according to what the memory brings back into place; and a fracture of the bone is known by the fact that the limb is twisted and clearly appears to be so, and it sounds when pressed with the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound on touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but there may well be twisting, or a crack, or a small fracture.  
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not fitting that you move it with your hand, but put on the medicines that come afterwards and then extract it now subtly. 
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that a fracture which goes awry, and the two parts are separated, it is fitting to now put them back together equally, just as abscesses come; and if hot abscesses come, leave it alone for a day, until the abscess is appeased; then put it equal to the muscles that you can lightly and wisely touch, and know that the restoration of it is lighter than the restoration of those who have pieces broken; then extract it as fitting afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone has two broken parts, whether it is a hand or foot, or at your hand it is a small limb, or two cords, or one cord and at your hand; and put the limb according to its natural shape so that when the parts of the broken limb are loosened, then reset with all means the additions to their places to the muscles that you can, and be careful that by your work no injury nor pain comes to the patient; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms. 
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he will feel it well in his hand if it seems to him that it is not quite right: if it sets beautifully, and you do not hold it too tightly, do not press as those who make it come by their work abscess hot and contraction on the limb, as we have often seen. 
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, treat the patient well so that he does not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor turning, nor in any other way; and guard well that the limb is so secure that he does not feel any pain. 
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels any pain, it is not quite right, and you must put it in a different position so that he does not feel any pain; and make sure that it is straight, so that crookedness does not come when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I tell you. 
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and largeness and shape. 
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and hands and similar ones; so it is fitting to wrap them in soft and fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: so it is fitting to wrap them with a wide and strong bandage, for the wide bandages embrace the whole large limb, and restrain it from all sides equally, so that there is no mark; then tie around splints lightly, three turns or four according to the limb, and restrain your hand one finger breadth from the entire bandage, then go above the fracture and restrain it less, so that the fracture then moves away one fingerbreadth from the fracture; and soften the bandage finger by finger, until you grasp a large part of the sound place, then take up the other bandage, and turn around again on top of the fractured place; then return to the part below the fracture, and restrain it moderately, neither too tight nor too loosely, as we have said in the first chapter above; then put between the bandages splints of linen or cloths, so that they are all equal, then tie everything over with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling. 
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply something soothing to the hot abscess, and which removes the swelling, and leave it like this for several days; then strain them on your splints, and they are half the width of a cane, well sawn, or wood from which one makes the pegs, or palm reeds, and they are according to this figure: 
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the splint which one puts on the fracture be a little larger and wider than the others; and it is also as long as is appropriate for the limb, small or large; then strain them on the splints as you did at the first time, then tie a thread evenly on top, as in the first time on the break; narrower on top, looser below; and it is necessary that the threads are medium, not too thick nor too thin, and they are of soft flax; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen from works of fools who make their bandages with twisted linen thread, and this is a great error, because the bandage cannot be even if it is too subtle, and it does not suit that there be less than two fingers' space between each splint. 
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is bruised by the heads of the needles after stitching in their flesh, put under them wads of linen or wool fleece so that they do not bleed. 
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture and the heart is broken, I will say the cure hereafter. 
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not suit to extract all the needles from broken limbs on the first day. 
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it does not suit to put needles in too firmly except after 5 days or 7, or more according to your discernment of the hot abscess that arises; and see here the manner of ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists: and it is that you take flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg yolk, and put this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the plaster that restores a fracture in several positions, and for women and for small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.  
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three handfuls of horehound and lavender and endive and asafoetida and gum arabic and myrrh, each ten drachms; aloes, five drachms; alkanet, nine drachms; and make powder, and mix them with the white of one egg. If the complexion of the man is hot, then use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is of value to many men. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of plaster which is good for torsion: take myrrh and vismalve, each ten drachms; aloes and asafoetida, each nine drachms; gum arabic six drachms; Armenian bole ten drachms; and grind well, and confect with vinegar or the white of an egg, and administer it.  
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another manner of plaster for joints and bones separated from their places, and eases the pain arising from it, and softens the use of the bone, and the fracture: take new wool, and moisten it in vinegar and boiled oil, and put on the place. 
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and properly removes pains. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to make a plaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves and terrestrial poppy leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to make a plaster for the restoration of a bone fracture and to soften the remnant of an abscess. 
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take marshmallow root, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, of each one part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is inflamed, mix it with moist coriander water, or water, and apply it. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to make a plaster stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes for the restoration of the limb.  
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take marshmallow roots, flax seeds, henbane, melilot, and sage, and violet flowers and chamomile, of all one part; grind, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine according to the heat of the limb, and its rest. 
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that you should not put anything on a broken limb to restore strength except for cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and he says it should be neither too soft nor too hard. 
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen says that you should put on a broken limb, to restore it, dry things a little hot, such as myrrh and aloe and frankincense and similar things, as we have said. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of plaster that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and horsehair chopped up, or bird feathers, and agrimony, and weigh them equally, and grind them, and make plaster and bind it.  
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then unbind it a little afterward, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor that the bone moves from its place; if so, do not unbind it for several days. And if pain comes to the place, or itching, or restlessness or swelling, hurry and unbind it and remove the plaster now; then take a light cloth and a damp sea sponge, and dip it in water and lift the place until the itching stops and the pain is soothed; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry wool moistened in water or rose oil on top, and bind it overnight until you are sure of a hot abscess; and relieve the inflammation from the limb and remove the pain, then start the binding again subtly and apply a little plaster, and do not tighten it as much as before; and continue gently until it is healed.  
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess grows and reddens, and has pain and swelling, I have removed all of it, and you need plaster and bandage, if it starts again, as you did first equally. 
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the limb, do not untie it except after III days or IV or V or VII; and never leave it for XX days, according to what one sees, as long as the fracture heals, and approaches the adjustment of the flesh on top; then restrain more than at first, and thicken its flesh, as I have said before; and if you see the place dry more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come; therefore, raise a bath of warm water, every time you untie it, and this be every third day, and apply a compress to the wound; by this work then cut off the nourishment to the limb, and quickly amend what the foolish mire does, which leaves the limb crooked: this is bad, and these are perilous works, and I see no other thing than leaving it alone and working on it straight. 
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various ways of breaking 
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways of fractures, and diverse figures, and the causes are destined; for there are fractures which are made by the percussion of a sword, and the neck breaks all the bone up to the sinew which is beneath the bone, as a hatchet or club does; and therefore this manner of fracture is called "hachure". 
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts the bone above without piercing it, and this manner of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures is great or small. 
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is blunt force trauma, or a fissure or blow from a stone, or falling on stone, or other similar things. 
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture, which approaches up to the membrane that is beneath the bone, or it is upon the bone, and this wound is either large or small.  
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound is rejoined to the bone as fine as a hair, and the crack is small, and therefore it is called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound that is made by hitting with a stone or falling, or by similar things, makes the piece of bone enter inwards, and the bone chips are as they do the cauldrons when they strike on the cauldrons; if the stone enters inside. 
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often to those who have soft or damp bones, such as the skull of a child; and it occurs in all these kinds of fractures that small pieces are detached like splinters; and I will speak about them in their place. 
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all kinds of fractures by the traction on them, and the inquisition at attempts, and by the rotten flesh that is upon them. 
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The resemblance capillary is known by this that when one has uncovered the bone, and rubs quickly upon it, if it appears black breakage. 
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of a fracture, take heed to the accidents of the patient, and if you see any evil accident, such as vomiting of bile, and emission of understanding, and stretching, and trembling, and fever ague, and if they issue forth forcefully and red, and other such things in various dispositions, then it cannot be healed without doubt. 
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a lamentable accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the cure.  
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture first comes to you, and it is in winter, then it is fitting to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at which time you are able.  
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the cloth under the bone becomes corrupted, and come the accidents that we have said.  
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches as far as the membrane that covers the brain, it is fitting that you split the divided part thus: and take the head of the patient in your hands and uncover above the bone in all the ways that you can, and above the shape of the wound more often than you can, and if discharge of blood comes to reveal the bone, or an abscess forms, aid him with what is necessary, and fill the place with cloths moistened in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the abscess that has formed is appeased, and be sure of the discharge of blood; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method if you cut at a narrow tailoring in front, and this is the form: 
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I put the other incision larger than the first. 
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have a number of diverse incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and they are made of untempered iron; and in use lightly, so that you do not dull the head. 
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, it is fitting that you pierce around it, so that you administer incisions with trephines, not completely so that they do not pierce beyond the bone where you are testing, and must have upon the point a margin or a circle, which does not let the point pass beyond the bone; and you ought to have several of them, so that each one comes in its place according to the type of bone, so that you have trephines for all types; and this is the form of the three manners of trephines: 
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put the trephine on the bone, and turn it at your wrists until you know that the bone is pierced; then put the trephine elsewhere a little afterward, and so do all around, then cut with incisions the space of the bone which is between the perforations, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, so much that you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as tongs, pincers; and guard that you do not touch the brain nor the spinal cord. 
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone and cut it, it is fitting that you leave the instrument which remained from the bone for all other instruments resembling an incisor, but it must be thinner and more subtle than the other incisor; and if any small bones or no scales remain, remove them lightly with the instruments; then treat the wound with tents and dressings as we have said. 
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of working is that which Galliens says, which is safer and more effective, and this is his word. 
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is fitting that you uncover a part of the bone where the fracture appears to move so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place below the head of this lenticular incisor which has this shape: 
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, but the part is sharp on two sides so that the cutting edge is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet on top so that you lightly chip away at the bone all around and be well aware of the cloth which is underneath; if it gets close to the bone remove the bone lightly because one can bone it well without harm and without fear. 
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not reach as far as the cloth, and the bone is cut only on the surface, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to scrape away that roughness and remove the scales with a fine razor which you must have in various quantities, in order to administer the most suitable one according to the work and the shape of the fracture. 
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you start with large razors, and then use more subtle ones, and do not cease doing this until it is well done.  
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other capillary cuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary that you administer according to its direction; and this is something that is not answered to one who has put his study in this art.  
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the sciatic nerve is uncovered, it is necessary that you take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it in oil of roses, and place it upon the wound; then take another cloth doubled into two or three, and moisten it in wine and oil of roses, and place it upon the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can so that you do not burden the sciatic nerve, then administer a bandage over it, and do not tighten it too hard only enough to hold the wound; and leave it thus for one or two days, until the abscess is calmed down, then untie it and administer medicines such as lily roots, wheat flour, frankincense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; and make a powder of these things and put it upon the wound, and then administer cleansing medicines without biting; and be careful that the wound is clean, so that you do not leave any ointment on it, nor allow pus to gather there, for when pus gathers on the cloth covering the brain, it will corrode and spread, and cause the patient great harm; for when something biting is put upon the sciatic nerve, it irritates it above. 
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt. 
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackness does not come except for the medicine that has been put on it, so that its virtue may have effect, then you must take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix them in a cloth, and put it on the wound; then cure it in the manner that is proper, until it is healed. 
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one by itself, for these are bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, but only bends or twists, and then heals. 
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is fitting that you put your little finger or thumb on the nose, and place the broken part inside your index finger, and push it gently with your thumb until the nose returns to its natural shape; and do this lightly, and take care that the patient does not feel pain from your work. 
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the knee, and the bone cannot come back into place, it is necessary that you put it equal to the head of a nail with a large hole. 
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, do it in the same way, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscesses that have formed are appeased, then bind at the head of the knee with bandages of linen, if the break is in one part. 
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind on the other side, if the break is there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the hollows of the knee. 
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some healers say that one should moisten the bandages with butter and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they be softened with a confection of egg yolk and flour; then leave the bandage on until the bone is firm and the cartilage has hardened. 
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never use burnt goose feathers in place of tents, and if it is tightly wrapped with linen cloth, hold the fracture still, and the patient blows among them; or do what you see. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the nose while you are working on it, put cerate or moistened cotton in rose oil, or a poppy seed poultice.  
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess does not come, put a plaster on top, made of sesame flour and frankincense powder, mixed with egg yolk; then apply it to light cloths, and do not tie the nose; and if the fracture in the nose is small and it is broken into small pieces, extract it with suitable instruments for this, then stitch up the wound and treat it with things that promote healing, such as soldering, with plasters and ointments suitable for this; and if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it like a tent, and put splints of linen cloth in it until it heals.  
de la routure de la mandibule	of the breaking of the jawbone 
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken below, and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only slight, and it is not broken in two, but merely splintered inward, if the practitioner considers it lightly. 
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is in the left jawbone, put your index finger of the right hand, and push the fracture inward lightly, and hold it with the other hand by the outside, and set it equal. 
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is separated into two, it is necessary that you administer extension in two parts, so that it is equalized. 
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of the teeth, or fracture, bind them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put cerate on the broken jawbone, and place one double cloth over it; and place a large well-made star upon the cloth, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jawbone, and tie it up to the muscles as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods. 
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the shape changes, untie it on the third day, and then put back what has changed; and put a plaster on it, made from mill powder with plenty of egg or sesame flour, after you have removed the wax; and put a light cloth over the plaster, and if the plasters dry out, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until they are healed; many times it is healed in three weeks. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if boils come, treat them as we have said many times. 
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, examine whether any piece of bone has been removed; if it is subtle, remove it with suitable instruments. 
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with a flame according to your need.  
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there remains none, if the wound is large, sew it up, and put on suitable plasters for that purpose, to promote flesh, until it is healed. 
de la forcele	of the forceps 
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps breaks several times in front of the shoulder, and the fracture is according to III ways: either it is broken and separated into two, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.  
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the forceps is broken; and the other extends the neck toward the part; then put the fracture equal to your will, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor swelling.  
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to further extend it, place a round sphere of cloth or wool under the patient's shoulder, and make it large according to your need; stretch and lift the force, and pull out the sphere with your hand so that you align the fracture as it should be. 
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw out the head of the humerus further because it is stuck fast, it is necessary that the patient lies often on his back and put a medium pillow under the shoulder, and push down the shoulder with your hands until the bone of the humerus is raised. 
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then straighten the fracture to your liking, and if you find it broken into pieces, you must cut it open; and draw out the pieces gently. And if the bone cannot join because of any obstacle, apply one of the incisors that you have; but put this instrument under the humerus to hold the symphysis. 
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it resembles a spoon and is not beveled and is as wide as it should be according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work;
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if boils come, moisten a cloth in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and apply it. 
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The setting of a bone, when it is without wounds and without incision, is that you put on the bone a plaster of powder from the mill and egg yolk, and put light lint on top, and put a splint under the armpit if you need it; then take a very large bandage a palm wide, and then put the cloth doubled on the lint and the plaster; then take a thin stick three fingerbreadths wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the ends of the bandage hang down; and put the stick on the fracture, and turn the bandage up to the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the sick armpit; and loosen from each part, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture correctly, and you see clearly that the stick does not move on the broken bone, then leave it alone for a day, and when the ligaments are relaxed, then restrain them; and let the patient lie on his back, and put a small pillow under the armpit when he sleeps, to raise the shoulder high up; this will lighten the fracture from the weight by raising the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless some bad accident occurs, for 20 days; then begin the plaster again if you see that he needs it, and remove it and leave it like that until he is restored; and it is restored at most in 28 days, and less in some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the breaking of the shoulder 
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It sometimes happens that the shoulder breaks or its joint dislocates and it is not possible to tell except by touch; if you set it according to the form of the fracture and reset it according to its natural shape in all the ways that you can, then put on the spot powdered millstone with plenty of egg white, and light bandages, and put a double cloth on top; then place a broad and delicate splint, a bit wider than the shoulder, and if underneath the splint any hair grows at any point of the shoulder, use that hair for bandages of linen so that the splint lies evenly; and then bind it all with one large firm bandage so that the splint does not move from its place and look at the binding every day; and whenever it loosens, untie it and put the splint back in place if it has moved, and let the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 days or 25. And when this number is reached, untie it and be sure, for it is not a bone that can be set easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone sticks out in front and not below the heart, then lift it up, and set the bone, and do what we have said about the fracture of the collarbone to soothe a hot abscess. 
de la brisure dou pis	Of the fracture of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The foot is rarely broken in the middle, but it happens seldomly; but it often breaks at the ankle. 
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks breath, and all at once, and by chance vomits blood, and the hair stands on end in the broken bone, and one can feel it well. 
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on his back, and puts a cushion between his shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the ribs of the two bones with his hands, and subtly makes them equal in all ways as he can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be; then put plasters and bandages over the broken bone, a subtle plaster of salt or another light herb, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it above the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the bandage roundly on the back, and untie it carefully, and watch every hour the binding, and if it softens, untie it; and if it is necessary to untie it because of corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and untie it, and remove the plaster, and treat what has come in a manner of cures; then reset the plaster and untie it until it is healed. 
de la brisure des costes	Of the breaking of ribs 
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs only comes in their thicker part after the back and mainly inwards, and they only break because they are slippery; and one feels it well upon inquiry, as is due. 
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the setting back in place is such that you put the break equal, as it should be.  
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply a plaster, and remove it with a splint if needed. 
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib break is slanting inwards, the patient feels great pain and shortness of breath as well as pleurisy because the bone pierces the lining; and they have sharp pains and vomit a large amount of blood, it is a serious danger to health and the ancients considered it a grave injury.  
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to give foods that swell the belly to push the break outwards. 
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make pus come if it has not already come. 
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, we heal it. 
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say we put cupping glasses on the spot to suck out humors, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cupping glass might draw superfluities to the spot because of weakness. 
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say we should cover the spot with linen soaked in hot oil, and put bandages between the ribs to apply equal pressure around it, then it is cured with a poultice of herbs, meat and medicine. 
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because of the bone pressing on the cloth, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the spot of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put an instrument underneath to hold the flesh back; then one should saw through the bone and pull lightly, and then sew the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat it with poultices until it is healed.  
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if boils come, put them on cloths softened in rose oil and put them on the place; and cure while the place of those that it is fitting for boils, and let it lie often on its side or where it should be, until it is healed. 
de la brisure dou col	of a break in the neck 
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there comes a break to the bones of the neck, and it often happens that he faints; and also to the spine of the back. 
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, take heed if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move them nor extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that he is mortal in several ways, and if he moves them and feels well when they are extended and pricked, know that the junction of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be healed if care is given to him. 
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healthy or not, see if the legs are softened, and if the accidents are in the hands, and on the back there is windiness and excretion without will; and when he is turned on his belly, there is excretion without will. 
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is turned on his back and he wants to sit up, he cannot. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that he is mortal; if you do not work on his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, the thing is lighter. 
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you warm it if there is a hot abscess, then put rose oil or egg yolk oil on the spine until it is calmed; then put a comfortable and drying plaster on top, and bind it with a bandage, and order the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed. 
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bones are broken, it is fitting to operate upon the heart; and remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat it with ointment containing charcoal, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the “head of the cow,” put your left hand into your pocket, and place it equal to the other hand at your power, then apply the plaster and the splint on top, if you need them; then remove it, and if there are any broken bones, do the same, remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed. 
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the hip bone 
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it does happen, there would be only a slight weakening at the head; and pain for a long time, and lameness in walking, and the patient feels pain at the site, and numbness, and swelling where the break occurs. 
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand above it, as long as you are above the break; and know which is the break and its shape; and if the break is only in the head, then make that break equal, as long as it is of a natural shape. 
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it goes inward, then make the patient lie on his stomach so that the restoration of this break appears to you.  
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it equal, apply a plaster, then place a splint of wood or horn on top, and immobilize the break so that it does not move; and bind the area below the ribs, as long as the ligature is even.  
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his sound side, or on his back. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses should come, do not touch them until the abscesses are calmed, and apply what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and immobilize it as it is fitting, if there is no bad incident; and this is the way. 
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder 
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, so you must restore it according to one of the two ways: one of which is that you take a splint plain of medium thickness, according to this form: 
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends with two ties and put them at the top, and place the patient on a seat; then lay his broken arm on the splint so that it reaches the armpit, and have bent a curve in the splint; then lean it against some heavy thing or have someone else hold it down; then put your hands on the fracture, equal to their assembly, until the fracture returns as it should.  
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one lays the patient on his back, and ties his hand to his neck, then commands two assistants that one should hold what is above the fracture with his hands, and the other should hold below all the ligament, and stretch each in his own direction.  
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, extract the ligature below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the assistants to their part.
