Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, it is necessary that you put one ligature halfway below the armpit, and the other towards the elbow, below the fracture; and also if the fracture is towards the elbow, it is necessary to put the ligature lightly, without effort, as long as the fracture is aligned above the place, and above the elbow; then align the fracture, as it should be, and extract it, if abscesses do not appear. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses do appear, do not extract it until seven days, and put moistened linen in water and rose oil on it, as long as the abscesses are appeased; then extract it, and the way to extract it is that you put the plaster on the fracture, then assemble the arm on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the drape, and extract on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its place, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is not moved. 
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone moves, use splints and place on the fracture a splint larger and stronger than the others, and have between each splint a space of two fingers, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture by three fingerbreadths on each side; then strain upon the splints as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the fracture, more strongly and less in moving away. 
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the setting of the splints and the constriction, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt a boil might form, let it be bound until the seventh day as we have said; then look at each bandage every three days, so that itching does not occur, nor swelling, nor does pus come to the place, or suppuration might not come to the limb because it is too tight. 
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said. 
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident comes, do not untie it except after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, with his hands on his stomach; and put under the shoulder one cushion full of wool equally, and look every hour of the day or night, that the shape of the broken limb does not move, or that the bandages are not softened; if the bone sets by the virtue of medicine, and give him the meat that we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the meat is at first subtle; and when he begins to recover, let it be thick. 
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be kept for forty days in all; and then it must be untied and given baths and ointments to dress the place so it heals. 
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is bad and embedded, it will remain to loosen for I day or II months. 
de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm 
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of II bones, which are called the two "fosciles," of which one is small, and it is the one that fills the pouch; and the other is large, and it is the one that is below, towards the little finger; by chance breaks the large foscile alone, or the small one, and by chance both together. 
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small foscile is broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing; and when the large one is broken, the healing is bad, and more painful than when they are broken together. 
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small foscile that is broken, it is necessary to gently extend it a little, and set it equal. 
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is a large muscle, then it is necessary to restrain more forcefully; and extend it on a cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the little toes lower than the other toes, and let the patient be crossed upon himself, and the cushion in front of him higher so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then extend the minister's arm below at his hand, or at the knee, and another minister above. 
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the sights equal according to its best form. 
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is any detached that you cannot reposition it with force, then put it on top of the bone as we have said before. 
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken about it in a singular chapter; then take care of it.  
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if boils occur at the beginning of the restoration, then make a cerate plaster from rose oil and white wax, not too hard nor too soft; and bind the plaster subtly over it until the boil is soothed. 
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then remove the cerate and apply a plaster of mill flour with plenty of egg; then apply splints, and let the splint from the fracture be stronger now, and a bit wider than the others; and know that it should have six splints or arms in various positions: whether the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two; and pull more above the fracture than elsewhere, and always less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages on the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread with which it is pulled be linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said. 
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And inspect the limb and the ligament after a few days. 
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accidents come to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you bathe the limb in hot water, until the itching is soothed; and let the limb not be too tightly bound. 
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then start the binding again, and if the ligaments are softened and the bones dislocated, and similar things, so address it.  
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you are careful that swelling cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, it is necessary that you loosen it a little and leave it like that for a few days, until the swelling goes down, and then remove it. 
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of the things that we have said happen to the patient, do not unbind him for 20 days.  
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Where it hurts, then he can put his hands on his neck, and let his necks be even, and guard against movement and shaking, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in XXX days or in XXXV, and perhaps in XX days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues. 
de la brisure de la main	Of a hand break 
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and as we have two there are few breaks, and there comes only more weeping many times.  
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or weeping, it befits that the patient sits cross-legged, and sits straight in front of him equally; then puts his hand on the stretched cloth, and extends the ministers the broken bones, and sets them equal to the others, as long as they are well joined; and put the plaster and bandages, if abscesses do not come, then he puts a splint according to the quantity of the place; and let it be wrapped in one linen cloth. 
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is in the flesh around the belly of the sole, make a sphere of cloths, and instruct the patient to bind it to his broken foot; then tie it with a long cloth, let the star be as wide as the palm of the hand, and pull it out as needed. 
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the toe, it is fitting that you put one star above and another below on the foot so that the hand is open and straight; then bind it tightly around the hand, and seal the binding between the two. 
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of the fingers of the two hands, if it is the thumb, set it equal as needed; and pull it with the palm, and if you see fit put a small straight star to raise the fracture so it doesn't move; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, as in the index finger or one of the others, set it equal and bind it with the healthy finger that follows; or bind them all together holding it tight, or put a star on it as you would on the thumb; and be careful in the restoration and arrangement of a hot abscess, and heal those who come to you as I have said. 
de la cuixe brisie	Of a broken thigh 
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and one can see it well when it turns in front and behind; and the restoration is done by tying one lien above the fracture and the other below. 
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	The patient lies on his face, then each minister extends his lien to his side equally; and this is when the fracture is between the bones. 
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the thigh, one of the liens should be towards the groin, and the other liens below the fracture.  
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near the knee, then the liens should be below the knee, and the extension downwards; then put the splints on the bone equal with his two hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then put the plaster on, and the tie, if abscesses come. 
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside then return to your work and your treatment; the ligature is made in this way. 
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the fracture with a bandage doubled two or three times, and leave the excess, then turn the leg until the heels reach the root of the thigh, and pass a long thread between the thigh and the leg below the knee, and bring the ends of the thread above; then turn the bandage on the leg and thigh, and place splints on the fracture, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and thigh with soft cloths to equalize the pressure, then begin to tie three or four twists on the fracture; and as you go higher above the fracture, the tighter it should be; then take hold of the two ends of the thread that you have passed between the thigh and leg, and tie them to the three splints which are above, then return below to the end of the thread until you reach the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it as is, until no abscess or swelling or other such thing comes.  
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, so that the dislocation occurs and is addressed as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that protrude, they should be removed if possible; and if it is not possible, then it is necessary to split the location and pull forcefully; and the treatment is done as we have said, until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And if the thigh is ever broken and splints are put on it, as in the shoulder or arm; however, in this restoration, no one will scold the patient. 
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in 40 days, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of complexions.  
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the hollow of the knee 
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the hollow of the knee there are few fractures, but it bends many times. 
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, unless it is only a crack or hole, and occurs in any wound, whether wounded or unwounded, this is felt well. 
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that one puts equal to what is broken at its due place, as much as it can be assembled and moved; then apply the plaster, and he puts a round star, if you need it, and removes it as it should be done, then observe all the arrangements we have mentioned in other fractures, such as abscess cautery and other similar things; apply to each accident what is appropriate for it, until it is healed. 
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg 
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called by right name "tibia," and the other is called "fibula"; and there occurs any fracture as it comes to the arm, and therefore the restoration is as that of the arm equally, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then turn the leg in all directions. 
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the slender bones are broken, do so beforehand. 
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bones are broken, there is great pain, and it is easily seen; and turn below.  
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply extension and set it equal, and bind the splints evenly; but nevertheless, if the break is bad, and there are many pieces, the extension should be less and lighter; and align according to your skill. 
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of wood that are thick enough to support the leg on one side and the other, and they should be as long as the leg from the knee down; then wrap them with two bands above and below, and tie them in the middle, so that the leg cannot lean to the right or left, and thus it is well; and no one should administer bandages longer than the leg, and if it is wood, put it on the leg to prevent movement, and properly make this at the break or where there is a wound; and move the leg every day to see if there is a hot abscess or another accident; cure it until it is healed.  
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the breaking of bones or foot 
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there does not come a break, but the bones of the foot sometimes come to a break and one must know how, and it does not happen with force in more dispositions. 
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if it happens that the bones of the foot are broken, and you see these bones rise upon each other, then put the patient's foot on the ground, as if they wanted to walk, and then place now your foot on theirs, where the bones are raised, and press until they return to their places; then put a plaster and bandages over it, and put under the belly of the foot a small board with two fingerbreadths thick, then straighten the foot gently, and when you have wrapped bandages around, and other things which you need. 
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandages, for you will find the bones equal, whether they are broken or dislocated.  
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the bones broken, set them as we have said for the bones of the hand; then put on the broken bone a splint according to the length of the bone, and let it be a finger's breadth wider, then put underneath the foot that board which I have mentioned, and bind it firmly; and if there are two or three, or more, bones broken, put on each bone a splint according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the board underneath the foot; and let it be so that the top of the board is under the belly of the foot, so that it holds it well. 
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said for other fractures, as we have said; and treat each accident as it deserves. 
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the wrist  
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, make her sit enlarged, then incline her to the part of her back, and have her held from behind; then fill the cavity of the woman's nature with cotton, and put in as much as your fist will hold; then raise the woman, and lift her back little by little, and then the cotton will jump, as far as it comes to the entrance of the nature, and return the bone with the fist. And when she wishes to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in, and do this for VII days or so: the fracture will be restored, and if you see, take a bladder of a kid, and tie to the opening a cane, and push the whole bladder into the nature; then blow through the cane until the bladder is inflated inside; the nature will return the bone to its place; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like that for several days, until it is healed.  
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of a man's arm or a woman's is broken, restore it as we have said in the bone of the hip; and these fractures are not hidden from those who apply their study and experience, and understand my book. 
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For a fracture signifies in several ways the right path to restoration; understand then. 
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the case of a broken penis, take a goose's neck and insert the penis into it; then wrap it with bandages and leave it for three days or so, and it will heal quickly. 
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound 
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is fitting for one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that he be healed now, so that the healings we have mentioned testify to this. 
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, and there remains vitriol, if you have nothing else, then begin again to restore the fracture that same hour or day, if an abscess does not form. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess does form, then leave the restoration until a new day, until the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause a bad outcome. 
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the chest uncovered, then it is necessary that you set it lightly with your hands, with a small extension. 
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not seem to you to be able to set it equally with your hands, then have this instrument of iron which has seven or eight in length and its width is according to the quantity of the wound; for this it is necessary that it imprint three or four, according to what he may need in each cure of fracture; and let it be round and have a large knob so that it does not bend at compression on the limb during your work, and let it be sharpened in front, and thick from the middle forward, thus: 
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", for which it is necessary that the curved head be placed on top of the visible bone; and the end at once, so that it returns and is aligned with the other. 
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, then it is necessary that you cut the head of the bone, so that the instruments have power. 
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot put the bone back as we have said, then cut with an instrument suitable for this, either a chisel or saw, at your discretion; then remove what remains in the bone of roughness and small splinters. 
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is put back, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. 
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Do as much as is necessary for it to be in place, then moisten the dressing with black stiptic wine, and properly if it is summer; and do not put any cerate or anything else that has oil on the wound, lest it cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer splints when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut a cover all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and be well aware that the wound is not strained with the fracture; and many times foolish surgeons have done this and brought death or corrosion upon the patient sometimes; and let the strapping be softer and gentler than for other fractures. 
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that evil accidents may come, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, it is not fitting to put splints on top; but wrap around, instead of splints, hard cloths, and tie them. 
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the bowels are inflamed in the wound, remove what you have put on top of it all, and apply healing ointments for wounds, such as tetrafarmacon ointment and similar ones. 
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is fitting that you loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, until it is healed and sound. 
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is fitting that the limb be supported in such a way that the bowels run down lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day passes and it cannot heal but the bowels come back in, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which reason you must probe the wound with a tent, and remove all these detached pieces that cause this pain.  
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, it is fitting that you cure it, according to what he said in this chapter before. 
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, and other similar large members, do not draw it out, for many times death comes, but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall out by itself after 20 days or 30, then cure the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, leave it. 
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of burns that come from solder
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the health of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a bad thing to see the shape of the limb; and perhaps it cannot make the limbs do their natural works. 
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if the swelling is fresh: if you administer astringent medicines, such as aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, sarcocol, acacia, and similar others, so that you take any of these things or all together, and mix them with astringent wine or with egg white or with oil; and put them on the swelling in bandages, and bind it well, and do not untie it for any days; and then unbind it, and begin another, until the swelling is removed; or you bind it on a piece of lead well made; because the property of lead is that it removes all swellings from the limbs; and if the swelling has already become hardened like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, cut it off with a knife, making the superfluity apparent; or you shave it with a razor until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed. 
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	a limb which is weak after healing 
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored and the limb remains weak and thin afterward, it happens for many reasons: one is because it was bound too tightly and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages and nourishment could not come to the limb; or because of too much movement, or movements that are too large, not done at the proper time; or because he has little blood in his body, so he is weak. 
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat and soften his body so that his blood is multiplied in him; and administer baths to him and give him joy and rest; then put pitch on the limb so that the pitch attracts great nourishment, and bathe it often with warm water until nourishment reaches the limb; and it returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the limb twisted after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bone is open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nonetheless it does not lose its natural function: do not believe those fools who say that one must break the limb all over again, and many foolish men have done this in our land; and this work is blamed, and it brings great harm, and by chance death; however, if the nodules and the torture are fresh, it is fitting that they be softened with hot water, or softening herbs be cooked, such as leaves of mallow, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and let a softening plaster be made, such as diachylon well made, and take the mucilage of mallow, and mix it with gelatine fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top; or you take fat figs, and crush them with flaxseed meal, and similar medicines that lessen the swelling.  
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the dislocation removed by rubbing continually and for a long time with wet hands. 
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And it should be administered movement to the limb every hour. 
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the crookedness is old and hardened, like stone, it needs to be removed with iron, so it should be cut up to the bone, with a subtle incision lightly; and put caution and study in the cure. 
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations 
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, and the patient feels great pain and injury. 
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation comes to someone, if it must be brought back now without delay. 
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the place swells, and by chance if one puts it back in its place; because of this, it is not good to move it when it is swollen: many times it brings spasms and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, make the patient well then leave it, until the abscess boils are appeased; then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then soften it lightly, and cure each limb as its cure will come in its place. 
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations from the head to the feet. 
des mandibules	of the jaws 
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes it happens that the jaws are dislocated together, and the dislocations of both are according to two manners: either they are a little displaced from their places and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated and hang down towards the ground, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and envelops his tongue with speech. 
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself through several positions.  
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is entire and complete, you must reset it quickly, and do not delay; and in such a manner that the assistants hold the head of the patient, and put the tip of one of his fingers into the root of the dislocation of the mandible inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides; and let the other hand be free, to apply pressure evenly; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.  
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the healer puts it equal, until it returns to its place. 
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if returning it is difficult, even if it are the two jaws together, then apply rose-water of sharp heat and oil, so that they soften lightly; do not pull too hard when returning it, as we have said. 
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are returned equally, and the patient's mouth closes well without softening, then put soft cloths in cerate made of rose oil and wax, and then bind it lightly with soft bandages; let the patient sleep on his back, and his shoulders be placed between two cushions so that he does not move them either to the right or to the left, nor exert himself to chew but take light food, as long as the pains are removed and the jaws are joined; and then eat what he wants lightly, and do not trouble himself to open his mouth for eating and drinking, as long as the jaw is well joined and healed. 
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be put back in place within an hour, and are not converted to their positions, then fevers and accustomed chills come about, and perhaps loosening of the bowels, and perhaps vomiting of pure bile. 
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is fatal; and many times they die within nine days. 
de la forcelle	of the fork  
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fork cannot be dislocated from the inside along its continuation and at the foot, and it is sometimes dislocated outwards, and one feels it well. 
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on his back, and extends his arms; and then presses the place with the hollow of his hand, and it will return; then he puts plaster and bandages on it, and removes them; and the head which is towards the shoulder cannot be dislocated; if however it does, and if it is dislocated sometimes, then you must put it back in its place, as we have said; then put plaster and bandage on it, and remove them, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; and in the same way the head of the shoulder blade is returned when it is detached from its place.  
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder 
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: one of which is that it dislocates at the side of the armpit below; and the second is at the side of the breast; and by chance it dislocates above, and this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor does it dislocate inside for the nerves; and many times it dislocates below towards the armpit, especially for those who have little flesh, because for these it is hastened; for those who have enough flesh, it is difficult, and it goes back with difficulty. 
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that there is percussion or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this. 
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must examine it until you are sure; and then begin the treatment.  
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that a dislocation has occurred when the shoulder joint is displaced downward toward the armpit and there is a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear difference between them; 
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the ministers lift the hand of the patient high, then put their thumbs under the armpit, and lift the joint forcefully upwards to its place; and the minister lifts the hand and extends it upward, then puts it below; so it will come quickly. 
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said within three days afterward, then it is fitting that the patient be bathed in hot water; and the minister apply a softening and soothing ointment, such as a decoction of marshmallow and fenugreek and melilot in water, and let it be applied; then let the patient be laid on their back, and place under the armpit a cloth of wool equal, not too soft nor too hard, then let the minister place their heel on the cloth, and lift the head of the shoulder virtuously, and pull the hand of the patient; and another minister hold the head of the patient so that it does not move down; this shoulder will return immediately now. 
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, you can put something heavy on them, and the dislocation will return now. 
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the resetting can also be done in another way: and it is this that you put a long pointed stick into the ground, whose head should be as round as a pestle, and not too thick nor too thin; then it is placed below the patient, but let him have cloths under him, and the patient should be lying on his length along the wood; then his arm should be extended downwards from the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a stick of two arms in length and four inches wide, which has a round head to enter perfectly under the shoulder, according to this form: 
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie cloths on top of the head of the stick so that the stick does not injure the patient, then put it under the shoulder of the patient; and extend his arm along the stick's length, and tie the shoulder on the stick, and the arm at the head of the hand, then place the arm on the rung of a ladder wide enough, and let the hand be extended downwards, and leave the body hanging on the other side: the joint will return now.  
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, no matter how, it is fitting that you put under the armpit a sphere of equal wool, then put the plaster prepared with powder from the mill, with incense and yolk of egg, on all the shoulder and around, then strain it under the armpit carefully, and turn the bandage over the plaster, and embrace the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain thus. 
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is fitting that he rest a little, as long as the limb is comforted, for it will heal faster; and then rest more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed. 
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come, or for another reason, it is fitting that you administer cauteries to three holes, as it is put forward or in the chapter of cauteries. 
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it loosens after seven days, and the joint does not stay in place, and cannot raise its arm above, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint was never fixed in its place. 
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocation which is near the buttock and the breasts or behind, is made by thrusting and extending of the hands and is administered in another place; and cure as long as it is healthy. 
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes pain to the limb and tardiness in movement, let the patient bathe many times until that pain is relieved and returns to its first nature. 
de la dislocation dou coute	of dislocation of the hip
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the hip joint is dislocated at points and at points returns; and if it is dislocated in all parts, even in front and behind, and the dislocation is not fixed because one sees it well and feels it well; and it is dislocated according to each figure. 
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick knife with the healthy one, if you can see it openly. 
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is raised, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch his shoulder at all. 
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it so that abscesses may come, for if abscesses were to come, it would be a hardship to reset it; and by chance it cannot be reset at all, especially when it is in the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and it is more painful, and by chance death comes.  
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it is such that you can reset it, that you extend his hand with your two hands; and his arm should be spread out, and the hands down below according to the knife around, above and below, and push the joint at its edges together, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place. 
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he bends his hand towards his hand, and feels pain at the root of the palm or the bone that is dislocated. 
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, apply strong extension; and when the one minister extends the arm, and the other minister holds it, so that it does not move during extension; then turn the arm in all directions, after you have wrapped a double cloth long and wide; and when the ministers reach the joint, they anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint forward until it returns; and when it is in its place, apply dry plaster with yolk of egg, and hold it tightly, and hang the arm on the patient's neck, and leave it for several days, then untie it. 
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, apply the plaster and bandage again, and leave it for several days, until it is firmly set; then untie it. 
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the joint is reset, and it moves, then bathe and rub it well, and press until it is relieved; or you put a greasy sheep's wool on the joint, leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and let him enter a bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint moderately, then put the wool back on, and then enter the bath again; and do this two or three times, until it is healed; and if you see it, put moistened cow dung heated with butter on it, and bind it up; and it will return to its place. 
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand 
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its return is lighter, more so than the other joints. Nevertheless, it must be reset quickly, in the same hour that it is dislocated, whether the flesh is swollen or whether there comes a hot abscess.  
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is such that you place the sick hand on a table, and extend the ministers hand, and he looks to put it even, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the jointure, and pushes it as far as it returns Entirely, it is fitting that you look whether it is well in its place; then have the patient place the back of his hand on a table for extension and resetting. 
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, have the patient place the back of his hand on the table, and the minister put his hand on that appearance of the joint. 
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it now returns, it is well. If not, bind soothing plasters for abscesses and leave it like that without restarting. 
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it in place after several days, the joint will remain crooked; do not harm the patient further than until his hand is weak and cannot grasp anything at all: then know that the nerves are cut, or the artery; there is no other remedy except to cauterize near the case, and perhaps nothing else will avail.  
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the plaster that we have mentioned, then bind it and leave it for 5 days, then untie it and leave it like that. 
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some stiffness, apply warm water and rub it until it is healed. 
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes on the back of the palm or on the belly; then extend the finger and push the dislocation into your pouches until it returns, then support the head of the finger and bend it towards the part where it is separated; and leave it for 2 days, and then straighten it that day; and bind it at night, as we have said, and untie it during the day, and make it move, and rebind it at night; and do this often until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you did before, until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated elsewhere. 
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	from the loosening of the shoulder blade from the back 
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade from the back or the neck is dislocated, if there are several dislocations, there is no cure, for death hastens the patient. 
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the movements leap further without volition, and he cannot hold them, and many times they are softened some limb, or the two thighs or the two arms or one. And many times the shoulder blade moves in four parts; the one that moves at the back is called "gilbositez": the cure is that you observe if the gilbositez has come from childhood: if there is no cure or healing at all. 
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And the one that comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient ways of cures were spoken in many words, where there is not much profit in all; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways. 
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the swelling which comes to the breast before, neither flesh nor bone feels it; and so too the one which comes straight on both sides, and it cannot be cured except for the one properly which comes to the back, as I said; and it is that the patient be stretched out on his face in an even place, and have a strain beneath him so that he does not move. Then put one ember at the head into the ground formed, and the other at the feet, and tie a string below the buttocks of the patient, and the other at the haunches, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two assistants know the strings, one at the head and the others at the feet, between the two embers; and they are well fastened, the ember as we have said, and the healer puts his palms on the spine formed, until it revives. 
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this cure, take a board three arm's lengths long and place the end below the armpit, and have the patient lie on their side, then push the head of the board under the armpit; then place the middle of the board on the spine; and have the patient put their feet on the other end of the board, and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see it, do it on the shoulder that turns inward. 
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you should put two firebrands at the head of the patient's arm a good distance apart, and two others near their feet; and between each firebrand, above and below, a hand's breadth in length; and in each firebrand, one hole through which the shoulder turns, and they should be firmly set in the ground so they do not move; and between each pair of firebrands there should be one turning firebrand, from which the ropes turn; and in the two turning firebrands there should be two small firebrands a hand's breadth long, to turn the shoulder; then tie the rope that is among the armpits to the turning firebrand near the head, and the other rope near the feet to the other turning firebrand; and each of the assistants turns their turning firebrand with all their strength, and the master aligns the spine as we have said. 
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when they are equal, put on a drying plaster with plenty of egg white, and then bandages, and then the splint from a tablet three fingers long, which covers the place of the gibbosity and the part of the spine that is healthy; then tie it with a ligature, as we have said, and use the patient with gentle nourishment, until they are healed; and if anything comes at the end of healing, administer softening and soothing medicines with the splint that we have mentioned before; and sometimes administer a piece of lead, and sometimes the appearance appears in the back vertebra of the spine, and think that it is a dislocation; and it is the bone that appears, so you should not presume, for it could bring death. 
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations 
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only come loose from dislocations, not as the other joints do; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, and in front and behind; and more often inside than dislocated in front and behind.  
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the recognition of its dislocation within is such that when you join the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the patient's knee appears more open than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee towards the fire; and it is the flesh which is below swollen with a hot abscess, because the head of the thigh bone comes there. 
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him for whom it comes back out, is that this event is contrary to those before. 
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him for whom it occurs in front are such that his leg is well according to its fulfillment; nevertheless, he does not bend his knee without pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot before, and he retains his urine, and swells his groin, and when he walks, he passes on his heel. 
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him for whom it occurs behind are such that he cannot extend his knee, nor bend it, and his leg is more twisted than the other, and his groin is softened, and the head of the thigh bone is in place below the ribs.
