Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The resetting of this kind of dislocation is such that you consider if the dislocation is old and it remains according to its arrangement, then there is no cure; and he should not have presumption. 
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those whose dislocation is fresh, and there are four ways of dislocation, if you hurry so that you return the joint, and extend it inside and outside, and move it to the right and left; by chance it will return, and needs no other treatment. 
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this way, it is necessary that you prepare a strong minister, and extend the leg strongly with two hands, or with a linen which is tied above the knee; and another minister extends his hand over it in such a way that he puts his hands under his armpits, then he binds it with a soft linen on the thigh; and another holds the head of the bandage; and they extend upwards and downwards all at once, so that the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging. 
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four likenesses, and if the dislocation returns as we have said, it is well. 
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, it is necessary to apply treatment according to its likeness. When the dislocation is in the shoulder, it is necessary that you lay the patient on his sound side, then put the bandage at the root of the thigh, and the place which is below the angle, then extend the bandage upwards towards the angle, and towards the armpit; then take other assistants to hold his arms, and embrace the large part of the sick thigh, and stretch it outward: it will return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than others. 
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tighten it in this manner as we have said, it is necessary that you bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong bandage above on the two heels, and above on the two knees, and let the sick leg be extended two times more than the others; then let him be hung by the head of a pole, and let him be at least two arm's lengths above the ground; then command one assistant to embrace the head of the thigh, and let another assistant hang with the patient, who embraces in turn the thigh, for the joint will return now hastily.  
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is down, let the patient lie down as we have said of him who has gout, and tighten the bandage on the affected leg properly, and on the foot also; then put two fires, one at the head and the other at the feet, then put one fire between the thighs in the shape of the patient's hand; and place cloths of damp towels around it so that it does not burn the patient, then extend each minister toward him, and let him hold his hands equal to the dislocation. 
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good. 
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put it on a table, and press it together as we have said in gout, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.  
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to quickly extend the affected leg, and according to what I have said; and let him place his hand on the pain of being above the affected angle, then press with the other hand, and extend down towards the knee. 
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the shoulder, it is not right to extend the patient downwards, nor to lift him up onto the ground, but rather he should be as though his hip was dislocated downwards, as we have said about lying on both hips; and he should be on his face, and the bandage extended as we have said before, and one must press upon the joint at the table; and it will be done when the patient extends his legs, and they are equal; then adjust the thighs, and put on a plaster, and bind it with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and he rests for three days or four, then unbind him, and put plaster on top; and if you see that they are equal, bind it as before, and leave it for three days; then unbind him, and let him walk well, until his limbs are strong. 
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee 
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inwards and outwards, and behind; and it does not dislocate forwards. 
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are such that you command the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it does not straighten at his thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your thighs, then bend the two sides of the knee joint; and another attendant extends his foot, as long as the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he straightens his leg well at his thigh lightly; and put a plaster on it, and let the leg air at the thigh, and tie them together tightly for three days or four, then untie it; and do not bother the patient to walk, as long as the limb is comfortable. 
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place, apply strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed. 
de la dislocation dou talon	Of the dislocation of the heel  
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes moved, and sometimes completely dislocated, both inwards and outwards. 
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and tense before the part where it is dislocated; if the return is slight, one must gently extend it with his hands when it is only moved. 
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, you must make the patient sit upright, and hold him firmly by the leg, above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left twice, then extend it upwards, and push the foot up well; and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, start the work again, because it will return; and if it cannot return thus, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and put a strong post firmly in the ground between his thighs, and tie cloths around it so that it does not bruise the patient; then hold the ministers' thigh, and another minister extend the foot with his hands or with a strap, which he ties above the ankle of the foot; then each minister extends equally, and the post should be now between the patient's thighs to hold the patient when extending it; then put the ministers' fingers equal to the dislocation at his hands, and another minister holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.  
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it has reached its point, apply the plaster and bandages over it, and bind it firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are on the ankle behind so that the bindings are not too tight; then leave it for II days or III, and if the binding loosens, re-bind it; then untie it on the third day or the fourth, and forbid the patient from walking for IV days; and if he walks before this time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes near the wound, it is fitting that you soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed. 
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, they must be nicely extended without effort, and it is an easy thing.  
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the back or foot, it is fitting that you make the patient sit on a flat place or on a table quite straight, and put your foot on what appears of those joints, then press with your foot strongly until it returns; and when it is aligned and nothing appears, put under the sole of the foot a table with two legs, then bind it strongly, and leave it for III days, then untie it; and let him rest until it is healed. 
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and of dislocation together 
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and you want to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies: so do not be presumptuous in the treatment unless you are wise in the art and have used it long, and unless you are pitiful and merciful and slow, do not dare; and use at the beginning soothing things for a hot abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place so that the abscesses may come alive; and when the limb is in place, administer soothing things for a hot abscess, and treat the wound as it should be with drying ointments; and if with the dislocation there are breaks, and small bones are detached, set them, and do what we have said in simple illnesses; and guard yourself from entering the path of fear according to what I have said, for this is worth more than you might think according to your Creator, and for the safety of your soul and body. 
Amen	Amen
